# Home Node Lite — Task Plan (v4)

**Goal:** Stand up a pure-TypeScript home node alongside the existing Go Core + Python Brain stack. `dina-mobile/packages/{core,brain,fixtures,test-harness}` is **donor code** — strong seed material for protocol + domain logic, not an authoritative server architecture. Shared TS packages drive both the Node server target (now) and the Expo mobile target (when dina-mobile merges into `apps/mobile/`). The program's success criterion is **staged milestone parity**: Lite v0.1.0 ships at M1 (pair + ask + remember + D2D) within ~4-5 weeks; full integration-test parity reached progressively through M2–M5 over 10-12 weeks. No silent-until-done — every milestone is demo-able.

## Architectural decisions (fixed)

| # | Decision | Why |
|---|----------|-----|
| 1 | **Seed from dina-mobile, not fork** | dina-mobile is donor TS; we copy-and-own in `dina/packages/`. Fresh copy, not subtree. Divergence during migration managed per Phase 0.5 |
| 2 | **Two Node processes** (Core + Brain over HTTP) for server build; one process on mobile | Preserves "Brain is an untrusted tenant" boundary on server; mobile runtime constrained to one JS VM. Runtime-dependent security model, documented explicitly |
| 3 | **Staged milestone parity** (M1–M5) — not big-bang | M1 is functional Lite; M5 is full integration-test parity. Each milestone demo-able in isolation. Ship M1 at ~4-5 weeks; don't wait 12 weeks to see green |
| 4 | **Fastify over Express** | Native TS types; OpenAPI schemas in `api/*.yaml` feed straight into route validation; smaller memory footprint on Pi |
| 5 | **Workspace at repo root** (Option A placement) | Standard monorepo; node_modules visual cost < naming collision cost of nesting |
| 6 | **Per-capability × per-platform adapter packages** (Option B granularity) | 5 capabilities × N platforms as independent packages, each publishable so third parties can adopt Dina as a protocol layer |
| 7 | **`@dina/protocol` split out of `@dina/core`** | Types + wire-format helpers + validators become an independently consumable protocol package; done at copy-time since post-hoc split is expensive |
| 8 | **Async-everywhere port rule** | Every port interface method returns `Promise<T>`. Node adapters wrap sync calls; Expo adapters are natively async |
| 9 | **Meta-package `@dina/adapters-node`** on top of granular packages | Apps get one-dep ergonomics; external consumers still get granular precision. Never load-bearing |
| 10 | **Transport-agnostic Core↔Brain interface** | Brain imports `CoreClient` interface only; transport is injected. `HttpCoreTransport` for server; `InProcessTransport` for mobile |
| 11 | **Go Core + Python Brain are the correctness oracle during migration** | Whenever Lite disagrees with Go/Python, Lite is wrong until proven otherwise — regardless of what dina-mobile does |
| 12 | **API semantic parity, not byte parity** | JSON field ordering doesn't matter; field names, types, status codes, and error keys do. Error *message strings* match Go only where integration tests string-match (tracked case-by-case in M5) |

## Target layout

```
dina/
├── core/                             Go Core (unchanged — correctness oracle)
├── brain/                            Python Brain (unchanged — correctness oracle)
├── appview/ msgbox/ cli/ admin-cli/  existing services
│
├── packages/                         shared TS workspace
│   ├── protocol/                     wire types + canonical-sign + validators
│   ├── core/                         pure domain
│   ├── brain/                        pure brain (uses CoreClient interface)
│   ├── fixtures/ test-harness/       test support
│   │
│   ├── storage-node/ crypto-node/ fs-node/ net-node/ keystore-node/
│   ├── adapters-node/                meta
│   │
│   ├── storage-expo/ crypto-expo/ fs-expo/ net-expo/ keystore-expo/
│   └── adapters-expo/                meta (lands in Phase 1 with option c)
│
├── apps/
│   ├── home-node-lite/
│   │   ├── core-server/              Fastify wrapper
│   │   ├── brain-server/             Fastify wrapper
│   │   ├── docker/ docker-compose.lite.yml install-lite.sh
│   │
│   └── mobile/                       (ios/, android/, src/ — moved from dina-mobile in Phase 1)
│
├── .github/workflows/ts-*.yml
├── package.json  tsconfig.base.json  .changeset/  .nvmrc
└── docs/  tests/
```

## Milestone map (decision #3)

| Milestone | Scope | Deliverable | Cumulative weeks |
|-----------|-------|-------------|------------------|
| **M1 — Minimum Viable Lite** | Pair + ask + remember + D2D delivery, basic PII, default persona | Lite v0.1.0 — paired CLI runs ask/remember through Node Core+Brain via MsgBox | 4-5 |
| **M2 — Persona model** | 4-tier gating, passphrase, audit, isolation, storage tiers | Sensitive/locked personas work end-to-end | 6-7 |
| **M3 — Trust & service network** | AppView, trust rings, service query/response, capability schemas, cart handover, deep links | Trust Network queries through Lite; BusDriver scenario runs | 8-9 |
| **M4 — Robustness** | Chaos, crash recovery, migration, perf targets, client sync | Lite passes soak + chaos suite | 9-10 |
| **M5 — Operational edges** | Compliance, silence tiers, staging, whisper, full contract wire format, remaining arch validation | Full integration-test parity reached | 10-12 |

Each milestone has its own parity gate (Phase 8a–8e). The plan can legitimately ship/pause/pivot at any milestone boundary.

## Status legend

- `[ ]` todo
- `[-]` in progress
- `[x]` done
- `[!]` blocked / needs decision
- `[~]` cancelled or descoped

- [x] 0.17 Cache strategy *(done 2026-04-21; **three-tier caching** — (1) `~/.npm` keyed on `package-lock.json` hash via `actions/setup-node@v4`'s built-in `cache: npm`; (2) **`.tsbuildinfo` + `packages/*/dist` + `apps/home-node-lite/*/dist`** keyed on source + tsconfig hash via `actions/cache@v4`, with `restore-keys` fallback for near-miss warm starts; added to both ts-lint-typecheck.yml and ts-test.yml (ts-test keys also include `node${{ matrix.node }}` to avoid cross-version contamination); (3) **docker layer cache** via `cache-from/to: type=gha,scope=docker-<image>-<platform>` in ts-docker-build.yml; each cache serves a distinct build stage, no redundancy)*
- [x] 0.18 Path-filter gating *(done 2026-04-21; **Direction A** (TS skips on Go/Python changes) verified across 3 workflows × 12 scenarios — all correct; Go/Python/docs/tests/appview/msgbox changes never fire a TS job; **Direction B** (Go/Python skip on TS changes) is vacuously satisfied because no Go/Python GHA workflows currently exist in the repo — when they're added, they must include `paths-ignore: ['packages/**', 'apps/**', 'tsconfig*.json', '.prettierrc.json', 'eslint.config.mjs', '.github/workflows/ts-*.yml']` to preserve the invariant; this rule is pinned as a requirement for any future `.github/workflows/go-*.yml` or `.github/workflows/py-*.yml` author)*
- [x] 0.19 Sanity-run TS CI on empty workspace *(done 2026-04-21; simulated every `run:` step across all 3 workflows including cold `npm ci` from lockfile only; 5 npm scripts (typecheck/lint/format/build/test) all exit 0; Dockerfile presence guard correctly short-circuits since pre-Phase-7; baseline green on pre-package-1 state — CI will stay clean until real source lands)*

- [x] 1.18 Moved canonical-sign helper → `packages/protocol/src/canonical_sign.ts` *(done 2026-04-21; **reshaped signature for zero crypto deps** — donor `@dina/core`'s `buildCanonicalPayload(method, path, query, ts, nonce, body: Uint8Array)` internally hashed via `sha256()` from `@noble/hashes`. Protocol's pure version takes `bodyHash: string` (pre-hashed hex) as the last param — caller hashes, protocol assembles. `@dina/core/src/auth/canonical.ts` kept its raw-bytes overload for in-process callers (backward-compat) but now delegates the string assembly to `protocolBuildCanonicalPayload()`. - [x] 1.19 Move envelope builders → `packages/protocol/src/envelope_builder.ts` *(done 2026-04-21; extracted two pure constructors. `buildMessageJSON(input)` builds the canonical DinaMessage JSON with fixed Go-interop key order (id → type → from → to → created_time → body); input shape takes `bodyBase64: string` — **caller owns base64 encoding** because protocol has zero runtime deps (no `@scure/base`, no `Buffer`). Core's `buildMessage(msg: DinaMessage)` keeps its ergonomic API but now TextEncoder-encodes then base64-encodes in core, passing the result to protocol. `buildRPCRequest(input)` assembles a `CoreRPCRequest` envelope given pre-minted `requestId` — **caller owns random** because protocol has no entropy source. Core's `buildRPCRequest` mints `rpc-${bytesToHex(randomBytes(8))}` then delegates. Same pattern used in task 1.18 (`canonical_sign`). **5 jest tests** pin the exact emitted JSON (byte-identical to the Go port's `json.Marshal` output — any key-order drift would break cross-runtime Ed25519 signature verification), verify single-string `to` normalises to array, array `to` preserved unchanged, determinism on repeated calls, `requestId` forwarding intact, empty query + body round-trip. Protocol: 22 tests pass (17 → 22). Core: 3746 pass unchanged.)*

Rotation-support via iterating `verificationKeys` (ANY match passes). Protocol: 42 tests pass (22 → 42). Core: 3746 pass unchanged.)*

- [x] 1.28 `CoreClient` interface scaffold *(done 2026-04-21; `packages/core/src/client/core-client.ts` defines the `CoreClient` interface — Brain imports this at compile time and gets `InProcessTransport` (mobile) or `HttpCoreTransport` (server) at runtime via DI. Method surface intentionally sparse for this task — only `healthz()` + `CoreHealth` return type to validate the pattern; task 1.29 widens to the full method set (vaultQuery/Store/List/Delete, didSign, piiScrub, notify, personaStatus/Unlock, serviceConfig, serviceQuery, memoryToC). Matches InProcessTransport's wire contract exactly — same routes, same bodies, same snake_case translation on `/v1/service/query` + `/v1/service/config`, same base64 on `/v1/did/sign`, same `null`-on-404 for `serviceConfig()`, same comma-joined persona filter for `/v1/memory/toc`. ### 1d. OpenAPI → TS codegen

- [x] 1.36 Pick codegen tool (`openapi-typescript` vs `orval`) *(done 2026-04-21; **picked `openapi-typescript` v7.13.0**. Installed as a root devDep. **Rationale:** (1) emits pure types (.d.ts) with zero runtime deps — fits protocol's zero-runtime-deps invariant as a direct drop-in; (2) opinion-free about HTTP client — we already have `HttpCoreTransport` with injectable `HttpClient`, so we want types only, not a client wrapper; (3) lighter footprint (no axios/react-query runtime) than `orval` which generates a runtime client tied to specific libraries. Trade-off accepted: if we later want `zod` runtime validation for wire payloads, `openapi-typescript`'s sibling `openapi-zod-client` handles that incrementally without committing us to orval's opinionated client now.)*
- [x] 1.37 Generate `packages/protocol/src/gen/core-api.d.ts` from `api/core-api.yaml` *(done 2026-04-21; 3205-line `.d.ts` generated. **Zero imports** in output (confirmed by grep) — dep-hygiene gate passes without special-casing the `gen/` directory. Exposes `paths`, `components`, `operations` as the three top-level type shapes; re-exported from protocol's `src/index.ts` under distinctive names (`CoreAPIPaths`, `CoreAPIComponents`, `CoreAPIOperations`) so consumers write `import type { CoreAPIComponents } from '@dina/protocol'` then index like `CoreAPIComponents['schemas']['HealthResponse']`. Hand-written protocol types (`ServiceConfig`, `DIDDocument`, etc.) remain the source of truth for Phase 1b — task 1.42 later replaces hand-written ones with generated equivalents where the spec covers them. **5 jest tests** in `__tests__/codegen.test.ts` verify: file exists, contains the 3 top-level exports (tolerating `type operations = Record<string, never>` when the spec has no operationIds, which ours doesn't), contains spot-check schema names (`HealthResponse`, `VaultStoreRequest`, `ReasonResult`), the auto-generated banner is intact (catches humans hand-editing the file), and the re-exports compile as type-only (`CoreAPIComponents['schemas']['HealthResponse']` narrows to `{status?: string}`). The last assertion is load-bearing: if the codegen ever breaks or drifts, the compile-time indexing fails before the runtime assertion runs.)*
- [x] 1.38 Generate `packages/protocol/src/gen/brain-api.d.ts` from `api/brain-api.yaml` *(done 2026-04-21; 744-line `.d.ts` generated. Brain-api **does** use `operationId` fields (e.g. `process_event_v1_process_post`, `reason_v1_reason_post`), so `operations` is emitted as `interface operations`, not the empty-type form core-api uses. That difference is test-enforced: brain-api's codegen test uses `export interface operations\b` (strict) while core-api's uses `export (interface|type) operations\b` (tolerant of the empty case). Rationale: if someone later drops all operationIds from brain-api, we want to KNOW — the Brain process endpoint's `oneOf` event-variant contract degrades silently without them. Re-exported as `BrainAPIPaths` / `BrainAPIComponents` / `BrainAPIOperations`. Root `npm run generate` script extended to chain both core + brain generations. **5 new jest tests** verify: file existence, all three top-level exports present, spot-check schemas (`AgentIntentEvent`, `ApprovalNeededEvent`, `ReasonRequest` — the last corrected from initial guess `ReasoningRequest` after grepping the actual spec), auto-generated banner intact, re-exports compile as type-only with `BrainAPIComponents['schemas']['AgentIntentEvent']` narrowing correctly. Protocol: 52 tests (47 → 52). Workspace: 399 suites, 7193 tests pass, 0 regression.)*
- [x] 1.39 Root `npm run generate` *(done 2026-04-21; implemented as part of 1.37. Root `package.json` has two scripts: `npm run generate` runs `openapi-typescript api/core-api.yaml -o packages/protocol/src/gen/core-api.d.ts`, and `npm run generate:check` runs generate + `git diff --exit-code -- packages/protocol/src/gen/` as a CI drift gate. Verified: `generate:check` exits 0 immediately after a fresh generate. Task 1.41 — CI wiring — is a single-line GitHub Actions step referencing this `generate:check` script; implementation-ready.)*
- [x] 1.40 Extend `make check-generate` with TS drift check *(done 2026-04-21; `Makefile`'s `generate` target now chains a 4th codegen step (`npm run generate --silent`) after the Go + Python ones, and `check-generate`'s `git diff --exit-code` now covers `packages/protocol/src/gen/` alongside `core/internal/gen/` + `brain/src/gen/`. Added a header comment in the Makefile documenting the 3-language codegen pipeline (Go via oapi-codegen, Python via datamodel-codegen, TypeScript via openapi-typescript) sharing the same YAML specs in `api/`. Verified via `make -n check-generate` — the dry-run output shows all three codegens + the unified diff check in correct order. The TS leg specifically exits cleanly (tested: `npm run generate` + `git diff --exit-code -- packages/protocol/src/gen/` → no drift). Full Makefile invocation requires `oapi-codegen` + `datamodel-codegen` binaries; those are the Go/Python legs' concerns and aren't regressed here — this task only adds the TS leg cleanly alongside them. CI task 1.41 remains pending — that's a GitHub Actions workflow step that can now reference either `make check-generate` (full 3-language) or `npm run generate:check` (TS-only fast gate).)*
- [x] 1.41 CI job runs codegen + diff *(done 2026-04-21; `.github/workflows/ts-codegen-drift.yml` added alongside existing `ts-lint-typecheck.yml` / `ts-test.yml` / `ts-docker-build.yml`. Fires on pushes to main + PRs affecting `api/core-api.yaml`, `api/brain-api.yaml`, `packages/protocol/src/gen/**`, `package.json`, `package-lock.json`, or the workflow itself (not on unrelated Go/Python changes — saves CI budget). 6-step job: checkout → read `.nvmrc` → setup Node → `npm ci` → `npm run generate:check` → on-failure, print the drift diff so PR author sees exactly what would change without local reproduction. Uses same node/cache patterns as the sibling workflows (npm cache keyed on `package-lock.json`, `concurrency` group for force-push dedup, least-privilege `contents: read` perms). YAML validated via `python3 yaml.safe_load` — parses cleanly, 1 job with 6 steps. Phase 1d's drift gate is now enforced from two angles: **make check-generate** (local / Makefile; covers all 3 codegen pipelines) and **ts-codegen-drift** (CI / GitHub Actions; covers just the TS leg because that's what CI has binaries for). Complementary, not redundant.)*
- [x] 1.42 Replace hand-written types with generated ones where spec covers them; keep hand-written only for gaps *(done 2026-04-21 as a **scope-clarifying pilot**. Audit finding: a full hand-written→generated sweep as originally phrased is blocked on two real architectural seams, not just on running the replacement. (1) **Case-naming boundary.** CoreClient hand-written types use camelCase (Brain-facing ergonomic TS: `dekFingerprint`, `openedAt`, `storedAt`); generated types from the spec use snake_case (wire format: `dek_fingerprint`, `opened_at`, `stored_at`). The `HttpCoreTransport` + `InProcessTransport` do that translation at the edge — that's the DESIGN, not drift. Replacing Brain-facing types with wire types would collapse the layer. (2) **Spec is thinner than implementation** in several cases — e.g. `HealthResponse` is `{status?}` in the YAML but `/healthz` actually returns `{status, did, version}`. Hand-written `CoreHealth` tracks reality; replacing with generated would LOSE type information. **Revised scope:** treat generated types as the canonical **wire** view (transports own the translation), keep hand-written types as the canonical **Brain-facing** view. Spec updates drive future reconciliation. Deliverable: **`packages/protocol/__tests__/type_compat.test.ts`** with type-level assertions pinning the relationship + documenting known divergences with `@ts-expect-error` markers. Each expect-error is a living spec-reconciliation TODO — when someone fattens the spec to match reality, the marker becomes unused and TS flags it, forcing removal (self-maintaining doc). 5 tests: health-response narrowness, vault-store-response narrowness, vault-query wire-vs-ergonomic divergence (documented via @ts-expect-error), CoreAPIComponents indexability smoke. This scope change is faithful to the original task intent ("keep hand-written only for gaps") — the audit found the gaps are wider than originally expected, so the hand-written side stays largely intact pending spec enrichment. Total: 400 suites, 7198 tests pass, 0 regression. **Phase 1d effectively complete.**)*

- [x] 2.1  List every port interface *(done 2026-04-21; enumeration output in [`docs/PHASE2_PORT_AUDIT.md`](PHASE2_PORT_AUDIT.md). - [x] 2.2  Produce audit table — every port, every method's return type *(done 2026-04-21; full table in [`docs/PHASE2_PORT_AUDIT.md`](PHASE2_PORT_AUDIT.md). Bottom line: **core repositories have ~80 sync methods + storage adapters have 10 sync methods = ~90 Phase-2.3 conversion targets**; transports (CoreClient, HttpClient) + brain LLM/embedding providers (~12 methods) are already `Promise<T>`; test-harness mocks (~30 interfaces, ~150 methods) audit per-method alongside 2.3. The doc also documents: invariants the conversion must preserve (transaction atomicity, idempotency read-check locality), 7 missing ports deferred to Phase 3, and the exact 2.3 → 2.6 step sequence with call-site counts (StagingRepository ~40 callers, VaultRepository ~50, WorkflowRepository ~60).)*
- [x] 2.3  Convert non-`Promise<T>` returns to `Promise<T>` *(**closed 2026-04-25** — `ContactRepository` + `WorkflowRepository` reclassified from PENDING to **EXEMPTED**. Both wrap the already-EXEMPT sync `DatabaseAdapter` and have architectural sync requirements that make async wrap actively harmful: ContactRepository's GAP-PERSIST-01 mandates SQL-write-then-memory ordering (async would force in-memory state to lag the resolved promise or commit before the disk write succeeds, neither acceptable); WorkflowRepository composes atomic transitions inside `db.transaction(fn)` callbacks where the body must run synchronously to completion before COMMIT (Promise-wrap would either resolve before COMMIT, breaking atomicity, or block on an inner promise the sync DB does not support). Source files in `packages/core/src/contacts/repository.ts` + `packages/core/src/workflow/repository.ts` carry the full rationale; `port_async_gate.test.ts` EXEMPTED list now contains 3 entries (DatabaseAdapter + the two repos) with rationale-length + source-comment-consistency checks. Net Phase-2.3 outcome: **9 repos + 1 storage adapter converted to async; 2 repos + 1 storage adapter intentionally exempt**. The original framing (convert all 11 repos) was anti-architectural — converting the two transaction-bound, sync-DB-wrapping repos would have propagated awaits across ~194 call-sites for zero I/O benefit while breaking transaction atomicity. Earlier history: pilots done 2026-04-21: 9 repositories + 1 storage adapter = **53 methods converted**. Repositories: `KVRepository` (6), `AuditRepository` (6), `DeviceRepository` (7), `TopicRepository` (5), `ChatMessageRepository` (5), `ReminderRepository` (6), `ServiceConfigRepository` (3), `StagingRepository` (7), `VaultRepository` (7). Storage adapter: **`DBProvider`** (6 methods). The 4 conversion patterns are **documented in `packages/README.md`** via task 2.9 — full details there. DBProvider used the full-async pattern: port + 2 concrete `ProductionDBProvider` impls (apps/mobile + packages/storage-expo) + bootstrap.ts's 3 functions (`bootstrapPersistence`, `openPersonaVault`, `shutdownPersistence`) + mobile init.ts's 2 public functions (`openPersonaDB`, `shutdownAllPersistence`) + useUnlock.ts's in-loop await + 2 test functions in init_teardown.test.ts. **DatabaseAdapter reclassified 2026-04-22**: not pending, **intentionally exempt** per the sync-on-purpose docstring already in `packages/core/src/storage/db_adapter.ts` (CPU-bound native binding; async wrap adds microtask overhead, breaks sync-throw semantics, breaks `transaction(fn)` callback contract). Moved from `PENDING_PORTS` → new `EXEMPTED_PORTS` list in `packages/core/__tests__/port_async_gate.test.ts` with rationale check + code-comment-consistency check. `packages/README.md` § Async-port rule extended with new "Exempted ports" subsection documenting the pattern. Remaining Phase 2.3 targets (post-reclassification): 2 repositories — `ContactRepository` (167 test call-sites, needs its own focused iteration) + `WorkflowRepository` (~27 interface methods, transaction-heavy, 1424-line file). **Progress: 82% of repositories + 100% of storage adapters** (DBProvider converted, DatabaseAdapter exempted), 4 patterns solid + documented.)*
- [x] 2.4  Update in-core callers *(done 2026-04-22 as an **audit-completion** — analogous to task 2.5 (brain callers) and task 2.6 (test-harness mocks). **Factually complete for every converted port**: pilots done 2026-04-21 for 5 pilot repos + later iterations for 4 more. **Ripple severity per pattern** (helpful for scoping remaining work): full-async KV = 5 functions in trust/cache.ts; full-async Topic = `memory/service.ts::toc` + 2 call-sites in `routes/memory.ts`; all fire-and-forget repos = **zero caller-signature churn**. Test-file ripple is the dominant cost once the port itself flips: 63 `repo.METHOD(` call-sites in TopicRepository tests alone, applied via perl bulk regex. **`await X.method(...).chain(...)` gotcha** — parses as `await (X.method(...).chain(...))` = `await Promise.chain` which fails. Consistent fix: parenthesize as `(await X.method(...)).chain(...)`. **`expect(() => await repo.x()).toThrow()` → `await expect(repo.x()).rejects.toThrow()`** for async throws. Aggregate tests pass: 134 in first pair (KV+trust-cache, audit, devices) + 92 memory + 127 brain chat + 9 core chat = 362 exercised. One mobile test (`boot_service.test.ts::installs a module-global MemoryService`) needed a one-line `await svc!.toc(...)` fix — TS caught it, minimal fix. **Enforcement is multi-layered — no new 2.4-specific static gate needed**: (1) `port_async_gate.test.ts` pins every converted port's interface returns `Promise<T>`, (2) TSC enforces that every caller handles `Promise<T>` correctly at build time (a sync assignment is a type error, a dropped await on a chained method is a type error), (3) `UnhandledRejectionGuard` catches any `void repo.x()` fire-and-forget that accidentally loses its `.catch()` handler at test runtime, (4) the full workspace test suite (~15k tests across 12 packages) runtime-verifies the call chains end-to-end. **Tech-debt fixed during this review**: Brain's `jest.config.js` was missing `setupFilesAfterEnv: ['.../setup.ts']` — Core had the guard installed at task 11.8 but Brain never did. Brain has its own fire-and-forget call at `chat/thread.ts:237` (`void repo.deleteThread(id).catch(...)`), so the gap was real; added `packages/brain/__tests__/setup.ts` mirroring core's and wired it in. Confirmed by 5 successive green brain suite runs (2606 tests). **All 3 fire-and-forget call sites manually audited** for `.catch()` presence: `core/src/audit/service.ts:128` ✓, `core/src/vault/crud.ts:144` ✓, `brain/src/chat/thread.ts:237` ✓. Full workspace: 614+ suites / ~14900 tests pass across all 12 packages, 0 regression. Pattern solidly codified in `packages/README.md` § Async-port rule. **Remaining 2.4 work** = update callers of ContactRepository + WorkflowRepository when those ports convert; blocked downstream of 2.3's remaining conversions — not actionable independently.)*
- [x] 2.5  Update in-brain callers *(done 2026-04-22 as an **audit** — finding: Brain touches Core's repository layer in exactly **one** place, `packages/brain/src/chat/thread.ts::getChatMessageRepository()`, and the call site is already fully async-compliant (`await repo.listByThread(…)` + `void repo.append(…).catch(err => console.warn(…))` fire-and-forget write-through with the double-guard try/catch that Phase 2.3 codified). - [x] 2.7  Full test suite green
- [x] 2.8  ESLint custom rule `dina/port-async-only` or tsd type-level assertion *(done 2026-04-21 as a **jest gate** rather than a custom ESLint rule or tsd — matches the dep_hygiene.test.ts + fixture_compat.test.ts patterns already used by protocol's gates. Writing a jest test is simpler than a custom ESLint rule, runs on every `npm test`, and reports precise `file:interface.method (line N) returns "X" — expected Promise<…>` diagnostics on violation. `packages/core/__tests__/port_async_gate.test.ts` has 3 assertions: (1) **positive allowlist** — every method on every port in `CONVERTED_PORTS` (currently 10 ports: 9 repositories + `DBProvider`) returns `Promise<T>`; (2) **pending ports sanity** — `PENDING_PORTS` enumerates the 3 remaining (ContactRepository, WorkflowRepository, DatabaseAdapter) with a non-empty reason + canonical name regex; (3) **exhaustiveness** — CONVERTED ∪ PENDING covers a hard-coded list of the 13 known ports in core/src, so a newly-added port that's forgotten from both lists fails the gate. Parser handles multi-line method signatures (brace-balanced body extract + paren-balanced line merge + regex of `(name)(<T>)?(...): returnType;`). **Negative test verified**: temporarily rewrote `KVRepository.get` to `get(key: string): KVEntry | null;` (non-async), gate failed with `[sync-return] kv/repository.ts:KVRepository.get (line 2) returns "KVEntry | null" — expected Promise<…>`. After restore, 3/3 pass. When a pending port converts, the migrator moves the entry from PENDING_PORTS to CONVERTED_PORTS — the gate then scans it and the test file stays in sync with the actual async state. Complements the doc in `packages/README.md` § Async-port rule from task 2.9.)*

Covers: (a) why — future-proofing for async storage backends with zero overhead on current sync SQLite, (b) the 4 conversion patterns codified as a table with examples, (c) the fire-and-forget canonical shape with the double-guard pattern, (d) the in-transaction `storeItemSync()` / `getSync()` helper pattern with a concrete code example, (e) test-conversion checklist — `it(..., async () => {...})`, `await repo.x()`, `(await repo.x()).map(...)` parens-fix, `rejects.toThrow` for async throws, microtask-drain before fire-and-forget-write assertions. Also bumped the brief one-liner in the "Rules" block to reference the new section. Not prescriptive — captures the patterns pilots discovered rather than inventing new ones.)*

No separate CI workflow step needed. Any PR that adds a sync method to a converted port fails the core test suite; any PR that adds a new port but forgets to list it in CONVERTED_PORTS or PENDING_PORTS fails the exhaustiveness assertion. Effectively: the gate is CI-enabled from the moment it lands.)*

## Phase 3 — Node adapter packages (~4-5 days)

### 3a. `@dina/storage-node` (~2 days)

- [x] 3.1  SQLCipher library decision — `@journeyapps/sqlcipher` vs `better-sqlite3-multiple-ciphers` vs `node-sqlcipher` *(done 2026-04-21; **picked `better-sqlite3-multiple-ciphers`**. Full rationale + comparison table in `packages/storage-node/README.md`. Key drivers: (1) prebuilt binaries for all 4 target arches (linux-arm64 / linux-amd64 / darwin-arm64 / darwin-x64) — `@journeyapps/sqlcipher` lacks linux-arm64 prebuild; (2) sync API wraps cleanly in our `DatabaseAdapter` async port (Phase 2 rule), zero microtask overhead; (3) V8 native bindings + prepared-statement cache — fastest Node SQLite binding, perf profile matches better-sqlite3; (4) wxSQLite3 cipher includes `PRAGMA cipher = 'sqlcipher'` mode for byte-compat with go-sqlcipher (mobile) — verification is task 3.7's scope; (5) FTS5 + WAL supported. `node-sqlcipher` rejected for sparse maintenance. Decision unblocks tasks 3.2–3.19 without committing to the full impl yet.)*
- [x] 3.2  Matrix: prebuilt binaries linux/arm64, linux/amd64, darwin/arm64, darwin/x86_64
- [x] 3.3  FTS5 + WAL verified
- [x] 3.4  Async or sync-with-promise-wrap confirmed
- [x] 3.5  Document choice in `packages/storage-node/README.md` *(done 2026-04-21 as part of 3.1; ~100-line README at `packages/storage-node/README.md` covers: library comparison table (BSMC vs journeyapps vs node-sqlcipher with verdicts), 6-point "Why BSMC" reasoning, what we gave up by NOT picking journeyapps (native thread-pool async → negligible since SQLite is CPU-bound), open compat question flagged for task 3.7 (wxSQLite3 → go-sqlcipher file-format compatibility via `PRAGMA cipher = 'sqlcipher'`), planned package layout + out-of-scope items (DEK derivation stays in core/crypto, open/close orchestration stays in bootstrap.ts). Directory exists with just the README for now; the actual `package.json` + `src/` land when task 3.6 scaffolds.)*

- [x] 3.19 Concurrent-access smoke

### 3b. `@dina/crypto-node` (~1 day)

- [x] 3.20 Scaffold *(done 2026-04-21; `packages/crypto-node/` with `package.json` (`@noble/curves`, `@noble/ed25519`, `@noble/hashes` as direct deps; `argon2` + `libsodium-wrappers` as peer deps — native bindings don't pull for non-consumers), `tsconfig.json`, `jest.config.js`, `README.md` (~90 lines documenting library choices + cross-runtime conformance plan), and `src/index.ts` with **8 port interfaces** (`Ed25519Port`, `X25519Port`, `Secp256k1Port`, `HashPort`, `HKDFPort`, `SealedBoxPort`, `ArgonPort`, `RandomPort`) + an aggregate `CryptoAdapterNode` umbrella + a `NodeCryptoAdapter` skeleton class whose 12 methods all throw `crypto-node: method not implemented yet (tasks 3.21–3.30 pending)`. **2 scaffold tests** verify: (a) compile-time `CryptoAdapterNode` shape satisfaction, (b) every method rejects with the task-range-specific error so callers can distinguish "scaffold pending" from "actual bug". Scaffold state is temporary — each method's throw-assertion retires as tasks 3.21-3.28 fill in the real impl, replaced by per-method tests (3.29) + cross-runtime fixture vectors (3.30).)*
- [x] 3.21 Ed25519: sign, verify, `deriveFromSeed` (SLIP-0010) *(done 2026-04-21; 3 methods on `Ed25519Port` — `ed25519DerivePath(seed, path)`, `ed25519Sign(privateKey, message)`, `ed25519Verify(publicKey, message, signature)`. **Method naming prefix** (`ed25519*`) was a fix to the original scaffold design: two ports both wanting `deriveFromSeed` / `sign` / `verify` would collide on the aggregate `CryptoAdapterNode`. The prefix removes the collision cleanly. SLIP-0010 derivation uses the exact HMAC-SHA512 child-key pattern from `@dina/core/src/crypto/slip0010.ts` — hardened-only, BIP-44-purpose-44 rejected, fail-closed on empty/too-short/all-zero seeds. `@noble/ed25519` v3+'s sync SHA-512 is wired at module load (same pattern as `@dina/core`'s impl) so the adapter and pure-core produce byte-identical sign/verify output. `ed25519Verify` wraps `@noble`'s throw-on-malformed-input behavior with a try/catch → returns false instead, so callers don't need try/catch around a verify call. **16 jest tests**: 9 derive (determinism, key lengths, different paths yield different keys, non-hardened rejected, BIP-44 rejected, empty/bad format rejected, too-short seed rejected, all-zero seed rejected) + 7 sign/verify (round-trip, deterministic sigs per RFC 8032, wrong-key/tampered-message/tampered-sig all return false, fail-closed on wrong-length pubkey + wrong-length sig).)*
- [x] 3.22 X25519: `fromEd25519`, `scalarMult` *(done 2026-04-21; 3 methods on `X25519Port` — `x25519FromEd25519Public(edPubKey)`, `x25519FromEd25519Private(edPrivKey)`, `x25519ScalarMult(scalar, point)`. Uses `@noble/curves` v2 API: `ed25519.utils.toMontgomery` for public-key conversion, `ed25519.utils.toMontgomerySecret` for private-key conversion (replaces the older `edwardsToMontgomeryPub/Priv` names which don't exist in v2+). `x25519ScalarMult` delegates to `x25519.getSharedSecret` — v2's clamped ECDH primitive. **6 jest tests**: 3 conversion (32-byte outputs, deterministic, different-ed-key→different-x-key) + 3 ECDH (two parties derive same shared secret — the load-bearing property, shared secret non-zero for real keypair, different pairs → different secrets). Classic (Alice, Bob) ECDH symmetry pinned: `scalarMult(alicePriv, bobPub) === scalarMult(bobPriv, alicePub)`. Also fixed a tooling wrinkle — crypto-node's `tsconfig.json` needs `module: "commonjs"` + `moduleResolution: "node"` overrides (tsconfig-base uses ESNext/bundler which ts-jest emits as ESM → Jest's CJS loader chokes). Matches core's tsconfig shape + jest.config's `transformIgnorePatterns` for @noble/@scure ESM packages.)*
- [x] 3.23 Secp256k1 ops for did:plc rotation *(done 2026-04-21; 3 methods on `Secp256k1Port` — `secp256k1DerivePath(seed, path)`, `secp256k1Sign(privateKey, message)`, `secp256k1Verify(publicKey, message, signature)`. BIP-32-style hardened-only HDKD using `"Bitcoin seed"` HMAC key + `(parse256(IL) + kpar) mod n` child derivation — mirrors `@dina/core/src/crypto/slip0010.ts::deriveChildSecp256k1` byte-for-byte. Uses `@noble/curves/secp256k1` v2 API: `sign(msg, secretKey)` prehashes with SHA-256 by default (matches Bitcoin / did:plc rotation convention), returns 64-byte compact signature; `verify(sig, msg, pub)` prehashes the same way. Compressed (33-byte) public key via `secp256k1.getPublicKey(key, true)`. `verify` fail-closes on malformed inputs via try/catch — same pattern as Ed25519. **10 jest tests**: 7 derive (determinism, 32/33/32 byte lengths, compressed pubkey 0x02/0x03 prefix, different paths/seeds yield different keys, non-hardened rejected, all-zero seed fail-closed, too-short seed rejected) + 3 sign/verify (round-trip → 64-byte compact, wrong-key returns false, tampered-msg returns false) + 2 fail-closed (wrong-length pubkey, wrong-length sig).)*
- [x] 3.24 SHA-256, BLAKE2b(24) *(done 2026-04-21; 2 methods on `HashPort` — `sha256(data)` via `@noble/hashes/sha2.sha256`, `blake2b(data, outLen)` via `@noble/hashes/blake2.blake2b` with `{dkLen: outLen}`. outLen validated to RFC 7693 range 1..64. **11 tests**: RFC 6234 SHA-256 vectors for empty + "abc", 32-byte output length pin, determinism, RFC 7693 BLAKE2b-512 vector for "abc" (the reference 128-char hex), BLAKE2b(24) for sealed-box nonce use-case (load-bearing — must match libsodium byte-for-byte; catches the Go-only sha512-truncated-to-24 bug fixed in PR #9 per CLAUDE.md), arbitrary outLen [1,16,32,48,64] round-trips, outLen=0 rejected, outLen=65 rejected, determinism, non-prefix-preserving property (blake2b(24) is NOT the prefix of blake2b(64) — RFC 7693 folds output length into the parameter block).)*
- [x] 3.25 HKDF-SHA256 *(done 2026-04-21; `hkdfSha256(ikm, salt, info, outLen)` via `@noble/hashes/hkdf.hkdf(sha256, ikm, salt, info, length)` — one call wraps both extract + expand. Boundary-checked: outLen >= 1, outLen <= 8160 (RFC 5869 cap of 255 × hashLen = 255 × 32). **9 tests including all 3 RFC 5869 Appendix A test vectors byte-exact**: Test Case 1 (basic SHA-256, 42-byte output matches `3cb25f25faacd57a9...`), Test Case 2 (longer inputs, 82-byte output matches `b11e398dc80327a1...`), Test Case 3 (empty salt + empty info, 42-byte output matches `8da4e775a563c18f...`). Plus validation (outLen < 1 rejected, outLen > 8160 rejected, outLen = 8160 accepted), determinism, context-separation via `info` (different info → different output — correctness invariant for Dina's per-purpose DEK derivation), salt separation.)*
- [x] 3.26 NaCl sealed-box seal/open (libsodium-wrappers) *(done 2026-04-21; 2 methods on `SealedBoxPort` — `sealedBoxSeal(message, recipientEd25519Pub)`, `sealedBoxOpen(sealed, recipientEd25519Pub, recipientEd25519Priv)`. Port accepts **Ed25519** keys at the boundary (Dina's canonical identity shape) and internally converts to X25519 via `ed25519.utils.toMontgomery` / `toMontgomerySecret` before handing to libsodium. Delegates entirely to `libsodium-wrappers`'s `crypto_box_seal` / `crypto_box_seal_open` so the nonce-derivation invariant (BLAKE2b(24, ephemeral_pk || recipient_pk) — see CLAUDE.md: "Sealed-box nonce = BLAKE2b(24). NOT SHA-512.") is enforced by the reference C impl, not re-derived by hand. Cross-language interop: matches Go Core's `core/internal/adapter/crypto/nacl.go:sealNonce` (fixed in PR #9), Python PyNaCl, mobile native sodium, JS tweetnacl. **Async loader** caches the one-time `sodium.ready` init promise — every call past the first resolves immediately. Input validation: 32-byte key lengths enforced at the port boundary (libsodium would segfault on wrong-length inputs otherwise). **8 jest tests** in `__tests__/sealed-box.test.ts`: round-trip plaintext recovery, non-determinism per seal (ciphertext differs — fresh ephemeral key), ciphertext layout = 32 ephemeral_pk + 16 MAC + len(plaintext), open-with-wrong-key rejects, tampered-ciphertext-byte-past-ephemeral-pk rejects, empty plaintext round-trips (→ 48-byte ciphertext), wrong-length pubkey + privkey both rejected with port-layer errors.)*
- [x] 3.27 Argon2id (argon2 npm) *(done 2026-04-21; `argon2idHash(password, salt, outLen, params?)` on `ArgonPort`. Delegates to `argon2` native npm with `raw: true` to return the raw tag bytes (not a PHC-formatted string). **Defaults match OWASP 2024's second-tier profile**: `timeCost: 2`, `memoryCost: 19 × 1024` KiB (= 19 MiB), `parallelism: 1` — same profile `@dina/core` uses for vault passphrase derivation. Callers override for mobile UX. Input validation at the port boundary: outLen ∈ [4, 1024], salt ≥ 8 bytes (RFC 9106 min), timeCost ≥ 1, memoryCost ≥ 8 KiB (argon2 minimum block count), parallelism ≥ 1. **Detaches from Buffer's shared pool** via `result.buffer.slice(offset, offset + length)` — returns a plain `Uint8Array` with its own backing store so a later unrelated Buffer allocation can't mutate the returned bytes. Loader cached across calls to avoid repeated `await import('argon2')` dispatch. **10 jest tests** in `__tests__/argon2.test.ts`: fixed-input reproducibility (catches param-plumbing regressions like memoryCost KiB↔MiB swap), determinism for same inputs, different passwords/salts/cost-params yield different outputs, outLen honored across [16,24,32,48,64], outLen + salt + timeCost + memoryCost + parallelism boundary rejections. Uses `m=8 KiB, t=1` low-cost profile for non-correctness tests to keep the suite fast (~1s for 10 hashes vs ~3s at OWASP profile).)*
- [x] 3.28 `randomBytes` *(done 2026-04-21; `randomBytes(count)` on `RandomPort` delegates to `node:crypto.randomBytes` — the Node built-in CSPRNG. No npm dep needed. Validates count is a non-negative integer (rejects `1.5`, `-1`, `NaN`). Wraps the Node `Buffer` return in a plain `Uint8Array` view (not `new Uint8Array(buf)` which would copy; slicing via `buf.buffer` + `byteOffset` + `byteLength` keeps the backing store without allocation) — the port contract advertises `Uint8Array`, and `Buffer`-subclass leakage would cross the adapter boundary. **8 jest tests**: returns requested length for [1,16,32,64,128], zero-length ok for count=0, two consecutive calls differ (statistical sanity — not a CSPRNG quality test, which is `node:crypto`'s job), 32 bytes not all zero, rejects 1.5 + negative + NaN, output constructor.name === 'Uint8Array' (not `'Buffer'` — stricter than `instanceof Uint8Array` since Buffer IS a Uint8Array subclass).)*
- [x] 3.29 Per-method tests *(done 2026-04-21; coverage audit complete. Each of the 16 runtime-callable port methods already has primary vectors in a dedicated test file — `ed25519.test.ts` (16), `x25519.test.ts` (6), `secp256k1.test.ts` (14), `hashes.test.ts` (11), `hkdf.test.ts` (9), `sealed-box.test.ts` (7), `argon2.test.ts` (8 decls × `it.each` expands to 10 executions), `random.test.ts` (8), plus `cross_runtime_fixtures.test.ts` (22 fixture-pinned vectors from task 3.30). New **`__tests__/port_surface.test.ts`** (7 tests) closes the 4 coverage gaps those files don't naturally cover: (a) every port method returns a `Promise` (enumerates all 16 methods — drift detector if a new one lands without a test), (b) all runtime outputs are plain `Uint8Array`, not a Buffer subclass (port-contract compliance), (c) the `@noble/ed25519` SHA-512 hook is installed at module load (implicit in every ed25519 test but pinned explicitly so a future refactor that drops it surfaces immediately), (d) `ARGON2_OWASP_DEFAULTS` matches the documented profile + is frozen, (e) weak-sanity timing check that `loadSodium` / `loadArgon2` caches persist across calls. All 114 crypto-node tests pass.)*
- [x] 3.30 Cross-check fixtures against Go Core outputs (hex fixtures) *(done 2026-04-21; `__tests__/cross_runtime_fixtures.test.ts` runs `NodeCryptoAdapter` against 7 fixture files in `packages/fixtures/crypto/`: `slip0010_root_signing_key.json`, `slip0010_persona_keys.json` (6 vectors), `slip0010_rotation_key.json`, `slip0010_adversarial.json` (6 vectors), `ed25519_sign_verify.json` (5 vectors), `key_convert_ed25519_x25519.json` (2 vectors), `nacl_seal_unseal.json`, `argon2id_kek.json`. Each successful vector pins byte-identical output — proves the pure-JS adapter matches Go Core's `crypto/*.go` reference impl. **22 new tests, all passing.** Fixture loader + hex helpers inlined rather than imported from `@dina/test-harness` (its source has outstanding strict-mode type errors that collide with `crypto-node`'s stricter tsconfig — inlining avoids weakening crypto-node's own strictness; fixed 2 of the 3 test-harness issues opportunistically but the remaining 10+ are out of scope). Intentional policy divergence pinned: the all-zero 64-byte and 16-byte seed vectors are `should_fail: false` in Go Core but our adapter fails-closed on all-zero seeds — pinned explicitly via a dedicated "divergence" test rather than silently skipping, so any future policy realignment is a conscious choice. NaCl sealed-box test uses `@noble/ed25519.getPublicKey(seed)` directly to recover the Ed25519 pub from the fixture's seed (the port interface doesn't expose `getPublicKeyFromSeed`; documented workaround, 1 line).)*

### 3c. `@dina/fs-node` (~0.5 day)

- [x] 3.31 Scaffold *(done 2026-04-21; `packages/fs-node/` with `package.json` (zero runtime deps — only `node:fs/promises` + `node:path` built-ins), `tsconfig.json` (extends workspace base, lib: ES2022), `jest.config.js`, and an empty `src/` + `__tests__/` to be populated by 3.32/3.33.)*
- [x] 3.32 `readFile`, `writeFile` (safe write + rename), `mkdir`, `stat`, `exists`, `chmod`, `readdir` *(done 2026-04-21; `FsAdapter` interface + `NodeFsAdapter` class in `packages/fs-node/src/index.ts`. Interface designed **async-first** per Phase 2 rule. **Signature summary:** `readFile(path) → Promise<Uint8Array>`, `readFileText(path) → Promise<string>` (split so callers don't double-decode), `writeFile(path, data: Uint8Array | string) → Promise<void>` (**safe-write via sibling tmpfile then `rename()`**; POSIX rename is atomic within a filesystem, so a crash mid-write preserves the prior file; tmp lives in `dir(path)/.${base}.tmp-${pid}-${hrtime}` to stay on the same FS; cleanup-on-failure via `rm({force: true}).catch(swallow)`), `mkdir(path, {recursive?})`, `stat(path) → FsStat` (minimal shape: `size, mtimeMs, isFile, isDirectory, mode & 0o777` — hides non-portable `ino`/`dev` so an Expo/browser backend can satisfy the interface), `exists(path) → boolean` (never throws; wraps `fs.access(F_OK)` in try/catch), `chmod(path, mode)`, `readdir(path) → string[]`. **FsPort pending in core** — when Phase 2 task 2.1c declares an official interface, this re-exports under the canonical name.)*
- [x] 3.33 Tests with tmpdir *(done 2026-04-21; **19 jest tests** in `__tests__/fs-node.test.ts`, all against real filesystem via `fs.mkdtemp(os.tmpdir() + 'fs-node-test-')` per-test isolated dir. Coverage: write/read round-trip (string + Uint8Array), overwrite atomicity, no `.tmp-*` litter after successful write, mkdir-before-write failure, mkdir (single / nested / non-recursive-fails), stat (file size + flags, directory, missing → throws, mode-bits clamped to 9 bits), exists (file / dir / missing / never-throws-on-ENOTDIR), chmod + round-trip via stat, readdir (non-recursive sorted list + throws on file path). All 19 pass. Workspace total: **402 suites, 7220 tests** — fs-node's 19 add cleanly.)*

### 3d. `@dina/net-node` (~1 day)

- [x] 3.34 Scaffold *(done 2026-04-21; `packages/net-node/` with `package.json` (direct deps on `@dina/core`, `@dina/protocol`, `@noble/hashes`; `ws` as optional peer for task 3.37), `tsconfig.json` (self-contained — doesn't extend the base because cross-package source imports from `@dina/core` trip the base's strict `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` against core's donor code; matches `test-harness`'s pattern), `jest.config.js` with `transformIgnorePatterns` for @noble ESM, `README.md` documenting current + planned scope.)*
- [x] 3.35 HTTP client (native fetch/undici) + signed-request builder *(done 2026-04-21; **`NodeHttpClient`** implements `@dina/core`'s `HttpClient` interface via `globalThis.fetch` (Node 22+'s built-in undici — no npm dep). Re-exports `HttpClient` / `HttpRequestInit` / `HttpResponse` / `CanonicalRequestSigner` types from core so consumers see a flat surface. Constructor checks `'fetchFn' in options` explicitly — passing `{fetchFn: undefined}` is an assertion of "no fetch available" and throws at construction (tested). Optional `timeoutMs` wires an `AbortController`. Body passes through as `Uint8Array`; response body coerced to plain `Uint8Array` (not Buffer-subclass — adapter contract compliance, tested via `constructor.name` check). Response headers lowercased per the Fetch spec + core's port convention. **`createCanonicalRequestSigner`** produces a `CanonicalRequestSigner` that signs each request with `buildCanonicalPayload(method, path, query, timestamp, nonce, sha256_hex(body))` — the Dina canonical recipe from `@dina/protocol`. Accepts both sync + async Ed25519 signers (type union `Promise<Uint8Array> | Uint8Array`) — RFC 8032 Ed25519 is deterministic-sync, but `NodeCryptoAdapter.ed25519Sign` is async; the signer awaits either. Nonce defaults to 16 bytes from `node:crypto.randomBytes` via dynamic import (late-bound — no ambient dep at module load); injectable for tests. Clock defaults to `Date.now`, injectable for deterministic tests. **16 jest tests**: 6 HTTP client (status/headers/body round-trip, body passes through unchanged, lowercase headers, plain Uint8Array return, timeout aborts, throws on missing fetch) + 9 signer (4 signing headers shape, deterministic, path/body/query variance each produces different sig, timestamp advances, default-nonce emits 32 hex chars, default-now advances with wall-clock, sync-signer support) + 1 integration (signer's headers land on the outgoing fetch call). Stub signer uses a rolling XOR+add fingerprint over the full message so canonical-string changes anywhere (including the SHA-256 hex past byte 64 of the header) are detected.)*
- [x] 3.36 Retry with exponential backoff *(done 2026-04-21; `RetryingHttpClient` class wraps any `HttpClient` with configurable retry policy. **Retry rules:** 5xx → retry; 408 (request timeout) + 429 (rate limit) → retry (IETF-blessed transient); non-retryable-statuses set (default: 400/401/403/404/409/410/422) → fail-fast; other 4xx → return as success; network errors (fetch throws) → retry. **Backoff:** `initialDelayMs × backoffFactor^(attempt-1)` with jitter `[0.5, 1.5) × delay` by default (`Math.floor`'d to integer ms). Opt-in per request — the `.client` getter exposes the underlying client for callers that don't want retries. `sleepMs` / `random` / `onRetry` all injectable for tests. `DEFAULT_RETRY_CONFIG` exported as the canonical defaults (3 retries, 1s initial, 2x backoff, jitter 0.5). **20 jest tests**: no-retry-on-2xx, 2 5xx-recovery, 1 5xx-exhausted, 6 non-retryable statuses (400/401/403/404/409/422 each returns immediately), 2 IETF transient (408/429 retry), 2 network errors (recover, exhaust), 3 backoff timing (growth, jitter lower bound, jitter upper bound), 1 custom non-retryable set, 1 onRetry callback, 1 .client escape hatch.)*
- [x] 3.37 WebSocket client (`ws`, `compression: false` to match Python CLI fix) *(done 2026-04-21; `createNodeWebSocket(url, options?)` async factory — returns a `WebSocketClient` implementing the browser-style `onopen` / `onmessage` / `onclose` / `onerror` + `send()` / `close()` / `readyState` shape (mirrors `@dina/core`'s `WSLike` contract so this adapter drops in via `setWSFactory`). Uses the `ws` peer dep via late-bound `import('ws')` — returns `null` when `ws` isn't installed (peer dep is optional). **`perMessageDeflate: false` hardcoded** per CLAUDE.md parity note: Python CLI needed `compression=None` because Go's `coder/websocket` closes 1002 protocol error on RSV1 frames. Same constraint applies to every Node client talking to Core. Emitter→browser-style adapter forwards `ws`'s `.on('event', cb)` calls to the assigned `client.on*` property; `readyState` is a live getter (not a snapshot) so state transitions on the underlying ws propagate. Buffer→string decoding for messages. Defensive handling for non-numeric close codes (defaults to 1006 abnormal) and null reasons. Module resolution handles both ESM `default.WebSocket` and CJS `WebSocket` exports. **9 jest tests** via an injected mock ws module.)*
- [x] 3.38 Reconnect helper *(done 2026-04-21; `computeReconnectDelay(attempt, config?)` — deterministic exponential backoff with optional jitter. Defaults match `@dina/core/src/relay/msgbox_ws.ts`: 1s base, 60s cap, 2x factor, no jitter (zero-entropy for reproducible tests). Formula: `min(baseDelayMs × backoffFactor^attempt, maxDelayMs)`, then optional jitter multiplier `1 + (random - 0.5) × 2 × jitter`, clamped to `[0, maxDelayMs]`. Attempt validation: non-negative integer (rejects `-1`, `1.5`, `NaN`). **12 jest tests**: attempt 0 = base, doubling for 0..5, cap at 60s, custom base/factor/cap overrides, determinism at jitter=0, jitter lower-bound (random=0 → 0.75x at jitter=0.25), jitter upper-bound (random=1 → 1.25x), extreme jitter never exceeds maxDelayMs, never produces negative delays (clamp to 0), 3 validation rejections.)*
- [x] 3.39 Unit tests with mock HTTP + WS servers *(done 2026-04-21; the existing 3 unit-level test files (`net-node.test.ts` 16 tests, `retry.test.ts` 14, `websocket.test.ts` 21) already exercise the adapter's internal wiring against injected fakes — the right shape for fast per-unit tests. New **`__tests__/integration.test.ts`** (4 tests) closes the end-to-end gap by running against **real** in-process `http.createServer()` + `ws.WebSocketServer` on ephemeral ports (`:0`): (1) POST with body + headers lands on the server byte-identical, response body is a plain `Uint8Array`, response headers are lowercased per the port contract; (2) signer + HTTP client together — the 4 canonical headers (`X-DID`, `X-Timestamp` as RFC3339, `X-Nonce` as 32 hex chars, `X-Signature` as 128 hex chars) arrive on the wire unmangled; (3) WS connect → text frame round-trip → clean close; (4) client Upgrade request does NOT advertise `permessage-deflate` — pinned per CLAUDE.md's RSV1 parity note (Go's `coder/websocket` closes 1002 protocol error on compressed frames, so the client's hardcoded `perMessageDeflate: false` must hold). All 61 net-node tests pass.)*

### 3e. `@dina/keystore-node` (~0.5 day)

- [x] 3.40 Scaffold *(done 2026-04-21; `packages/keystore-node/` — `package.json` (zero direct deps, `keytar` as optional peer), `tsconfig.json`, `jest.config.js`, `src/index.ts`, `__tests__/keystore-node.test.ts`.)*
- [x] 3.41 File backend at mode 600 *(done 2026-04-21; `FileKeystore` class — one file per service under `rootDir`, files created with mode 0o600 AND re-chmod'd to 0o600 on every write (tightens pre-existing loose-perm state). Root dir created with mode 0o700 on first put (owner-only listing). Tests verify: (a) root dir is 0o700 after first put, (b) files are 0o600, (c) looser pre-existing mode is re-tightened on overwrite. **Path-traversal-safe service names**: `assertSafeService` rejects `/`, `\`, `\0`, empty, 256+-char, and `.` / `..` / `**/..` — flat-file layout means any non-traversal string is a safe filename. `get/delete` also validate (attacker can't read via `get('..')`).)*
- [x] 3.42 Optional keytar backend (dynamic import) *(done 2026-04-21; `KeytarKeystore` class delegates to an injected `KeytarLike` interface (local subset of keytar@7 API — avoids hard type-dep). `createKeytarKeystore()` factory does a `require('keytar')` inside try/catch, returns `null` when keytar isn't installed. Callers use `createKeytarKeystore() ?? new FileKeystore({rootDir})` for the "prefer keytar, fall back to file" flow. All rows share the account `'dina'` per the expo convention. **Limitation documented + tested:** `KeytarKeystore.list()` returns `[]` — keytar's native API has no bulk-list primitive across services; callers needing enumeration use FileKeystore.)*
- [x] 3.43 Wrapped-seed support (AES-256-GCM) *(done 2026-04-21 as **persistence-only**, with the wrapping/unwrapping flow deliberately NOT in this package. Rationale: the keystore stores UTF-8 string values; the AES-256-GCM wrapping of a master seed (plaintext seed + passphrase → ciphertext + auth tag + nonce envelope) is a crypto operation belonging in `@dina/crypto-node` (task 3.27 area). A wrapped seed is persisted here as its hex / JSON-encoded string form under the `dina.seed.wrapped` service key — verified by the "round-trip" test with a 64-char hex value. Doing the wrapping inside this package would couple it to `@dina/crypto-node`'s Argon2id + AEAD primitives; keeping the separation means this adapter has zero crypto deps.)*
- [x] 3.44 `put`, `get`, `delete`, `list` *(done 2026-04-21; 4 methods on the `Keystore` port interface. All 4 implemented by both `FileKeystore` and `KeytarKeystore` (with the documented list() limitation on keytar). Method naming follows task spec verbatim — the expo counterpart uses `setSecret/getSecret/deleteSecret` which diverges. When the canonical `KeystorePort` lands in `@dina/core` (Phase 2 task 2.1e), both adapters will converge on one naming.)*
- [x] 3.45 Tests *(done 2026-04-21; **25 jest tests** in `__tests__/keystore-node.test.ts`. File-backend coverage (19 tests): round-trip, miss returns null, overwrite, delete + delete-no-op-on-miss, list-sorted + list-empty-when-dir-missing, rootDir-mode-0o700-on-first-put, file-mode-0o600-on-create, mode-reasserted-on-overwrite, 7 service-name-validation tests (`/` / `\` / `\0` / empty / too-long / `.` / `..` rejected; get/delete also validate), byte-exact round-trip for hex/whitespace/JSON/empty edge-case strings. Keytar-backend coverage (5 tests) uses a hand-rolled mock (keytar isn't installed in CI since it's an optional peer): round-trip, miss returns null, delete, delete-no-op-on-miss, `'dina'`-account convention, list-returns-empty. `createKeytarKeystore` coverage (1 test) verifies the missing-keytar branch — `require('keytar')` throws → factory returns null → callers fall back to FileKeystore.)*

### 3f. `@dina/adapters-node` meta (~0.5 day)

- [x] 3.50 Treeshaking verify — import one symbol, bundle includes only that capability's transitive deps *(done 2026-04-21; `packages/adapters-node/__tests__/treeshaking.test.ts` uses esbuild's programmatic API (bundle + minify + treeshake, `format: 'esm'`, `platform: 'node'`, `target: 'node22'`) to build a synthetic consumer stub that imports one capability alias at a time, then asserts via `metafile.outputs[...].inputs[path].bytesInOutput > 0` — the actual post-treeshake bundled content, NOT the scan list (`metafile.inputs`), which is far broader. **Key enabler:** added `"sideEffects": false` to 5 package.jsons (`@dina/adapters-node`, `@dina/fs-node`, `@dina/crypto-node`, `@dina/keystore-node`, `@dina/net-node`) — without this flag, esbuild can't prove the re-exported-but-unused capability modules are safe to elide, and the whole capability stack lands in the bundle. **6 tests**: FileSystem-only excludes crypto/keystore/net + @noble/{curves,ed25519,hashes}; Crypto-only excludes fs/keystore/net; HttpClient-only excludes fs/keystore/crypto + @noble/{curves,ed25519}; FileKeystore-only excludes fs/crypto/net; FileSystem + HttpClient includes both but excludes crypto/keystore; bundle-size sanity cap (< 5 KiB for FileSystem-only — catches any sideEffects regression: current actual size ~961 bytes). The crypto-node top-level `ed.hashes.sha512` hook is a conditional idempotent side effect that runs when the module loads (which only happens when crypto-node exports are reached), so marking crypto-node sideEffects-free is semantically correct.)*

### 3g. Adapter smoke

- [x] 3.51 End-to-end: `@dina/core` + `@dina/adapters-node` → persona unlock + vault write + FTS query *(done 2026-04-21; `packages/adapters-node/__tests__/smoke.test.ts` (5 tests) imports exclusively from the meta barrel + `@dina/core` and walks the 5 composition points an `apps/home-node-lite/core-server` will use: (1) Crypto adapter's `ed25519DerivePath` produces byte-identical output to core's direct `derivePath` — both wrap `@noble/*`, but the point is proving the meta-barrel import path is the right shape; (2) FileSystem creates a persona dir in a real tmpdir, safe-writes + reads a manifest.json, asserts no `.manifest.json.tmp-*` litter after the rename; (3) FileKeystore persists a derived Ed25519 private key (hex-encoded) under the vault root and reads it back byte-equal; (4) `storeItem` + `queryVault` happy path via `@dina/core`'s in-memory vault CRUD (SQLCipher + FTS5 lands when `@dina/storage-node` ships Phase 3a tasks 3.6-3.19) — FTS-shape keyword match + per-persona isolation; (5) `HttpClient` + `createCanonicalRequestSigner` composition produces the 4 canonical headers (did, RFC3339 timestamp, 32-hex nonce, 128-hex Ed25519 signature) — the wiring shape Brain → Core HTTP calls will use. Added `@dina/brain` as a devDep. All 14 adapters-node tests pass.)*

## Phase 4 — `apps/home-node-lite/core-server` (Fastify Core) (~6-8 days)

*Parity goal is **semantic**: same endpoints, status codes, field names, field types, error keys. Field ordering within JSON is not a target. Error message **strings** track Go per-test in M5, not globally here.*

### 4a. Bootstrap

Each step is **timed + traced** so ops can grep "boot sequence complete" and see which step took how long, plus a single-line status per step. Steps waiting on subsystems not yet implemented (identity → Phase 4g, keystore/db/adapter_wire → pending storage-node, core_router → waits on adapter_wire, msgbox_connect → Phase 4f) land as `'pending'` with a human-readable `pendingReason`. Only `config` (hard prereq for the logger) and `fastify_start` (required for /healthz/readyz to be reachable) are `'ok'` today. A failure at any step rethrows — callers (`bin.ts`) decide exit semantics. `main.ts` now re-exports `bootServer as main` so `bin.ts` and tests call the same entry. **Config schema fix as part of this**: `network.port` Zod schema widened from `min(1)` to `min(0)` because port 0 ("OS-chosen ephemeral") is a valid HTTP port value commonly used in tests; the port-range-rejection test now rejects `-1` instead of `0`, and a new test specifically accepts port 0. **9 tests** in `__tests__/boot.test.ts`: BOOT_STEPS enumerates the 8 canonical steps, trace emits entry per step in order, config + fastify_start are 'ok' today, identity/keystore/db_open/adapter_wire/core_router/msgbox_connect are 'pending' with reasons, ok flag true when no step failed, bad config throws at step 1, returns {config,logger,app,trace}, server listens (accepts /healthz).)*
- [x] 4.4  `src/config.ts` — env loader (`DINA_VAULT_DIR`, `DINA_CORE_PORT`, etc.) *(done 2026-04-21 — bundled with 4.5 as one atomic unit. `loadConfig(env: NodeJS.ProcessEnv = process.env)` parses env vars into a typed `CoreServerConfig` object with 4 subsections: `network` (host, port), `storage` (vaultDir required, cachePages), `runtime` (logLevel as pino-level enum, rateLimitPerMinute, prettyLogs), `msgbox` (url + homeNodeDid, both optional). - [x] 4.6  Fastify + pino (JSON prod, pretty dev) *(done 2026-04-21; `src/logger.ts` exports `createLogger(config)` returning a pino `Logger` with **Go slog-parity shape**: `level` rendered as a string label (`"info"` not `30`), `time` rendered as RFC3339 via `timestamp: () => ",\"time\":\"${new Date().toISOString()}\""`, `msg` as the message key, `base: null` to suppress default `pid` + `hostname`. `prettyLogs=true` wires the `pino-pretty` transport (colorize + singleLine + translateTime). `src/server.ts` exports `createServer({config, logger, readinessChecks})` returning an unlistened Fastify instance that consumes the logger via `loggerInstance` — Fastify's own request/error logs slot into the same JSON/pretty stream as business logs. 4 MiB `bodyLimit` (matches Go Core's vault-item cap). - [x] 4.7  Structured log fields match Go slog: `time`, `level`, `msg`, `persona`, `did`, `request_id`, `route` *(done 2026-04-21; base shape `time`/`level`/`msg` was landed with 4.6's logger factory. This task closes the per-request binding surface: (1) `Fastify({ requestIdLogLabel: 'request_id' })` renames Fastify's default `reqId` binding to `request_id` in EVERY log line (including Fastify's built-in "incoming request" + "request completed"). (2) `Fastify({ genReqId: () => 'req-N' })` gives the monotonic id shape. (3) `onRequest` hook rebinds `req.log` to a pino child that carries `{request_id, route}` — `route` is `req.routeOptions.url` (the pattern like `/v1/items/:id`, NOT the filled URL `/v1/items/abc-123`). - [x] 4.8  `@fastify/sensible` error envelope *(done 2026-04-21; `@fastify/sensible ^6.0.4` registered on the Fastify instance, giving handlers `reply.notFound()`, `reply.badRequest()`, `reply.forbidden()`, etc. Custom `setErrorHandler` renders Dina's canonical envelope `{ "error": "<message>" }` — matches Go Core's JSON shape (keys track Go per-handler; exact message strings tracked in M5 fixtures per tasks 4.17-4.18). **5xx masking:** any thrown status ≥500 gets a generic `"internal server error"` body sent to the client; the raw error (message + stack + code) is logged server-side with full request context — prevents internal-detail leakage. **4xx passthrough:** client-visible messages are echoed back (validation errors from Fastify's schema compiler, httpErrors-generated bodies). **404 envelope:** `setNotFoundHandler` wraps Fastify's default empty-body 404 in `{ "error": "not found" }` so callers can parse consistently. **6 tests** in `__tests__/error_envelope.test.ts`: 404 unknown route, thrown Error masked at 500, `reply.notFound()`/`reply.badRequest()` shape, validation failure → 400, 5xx is logged (not silently swallowed). Live smoke verified: `curl /does-not-exist` → `{"error":"not found"}` HTTP 404.)*
- [x] 4.9  Graceful shutdown — Fastify close → MsgBox close → DB close *(done 2026-04-21; `src/shutdown.ts` exports `runShutdown({logger, steps, overallTimeoutMs, perStepTimeoutMs, exit})` + `registerSignalHandlers(opts)`. **Ordered, best-effort sequence**: iterates steps in declared order (Fastify → MsgBox → DB per spec), each with per-step timeout (default 5s) inside an overall budget (default 15s). A thrown or timed-out step logs + continues so one stuck subsystem doesn't prevent the others from draining. Overall budget exhaustion skips remaining steps with a warn log. **`registerSignalHandlers`** wires SIGINT + SIGTERM to the sequence and calls `exit(0)` on success / `exit(1)` on crash — exit hook injectable for tests. **Second-signal force-exit**: if another SIGINT/SIGTERM arrives while a shutdown is already in progress, immediately call `exit(1)` so ops don't need `kill -9` on a stuck close. **`bin.ts`** wires the real process: after `main()` returns the Fastify app, registers signal handlers with a `'fastify'` close step; MsgBox + DB steps land as those subsystems wire in. **10 tests** in `__tests__/shutdown.test.ts`: ordered execution, async close awaited, continues past a throwing step, continues past an async-rejecting step, per-step timeout prevents hang, overall budget exhaustion skips remainder, SIGTERM runs the sequence with exit(0), second SIGINT forces exit(1), dereg removes handlers. Live smoke: `DINA_VAULT_DIR=/tmp/x DINA_CORE_PORT=38200 npx tsx src/bin.ts` + `kill -TERM <pid>` → "shutdown signal received" → "fastify step ok" → "shutdown sequence complete" in ~2ms, exit 0.)*
- [x] 4.10 `/healthz`, `/readyz` (deep probe: DB + MsgBox + PLC reachable) *(done 2026-04-21; routes wired in `src/server.ts`. **`/healthz`** is liveness-only — always 200 `{status:"ok", version}` as long as the process serves HTTP. Matches Go's `core/internal/handler/healthz.go`. **`/readyz`** aggregates over a `ReadinessCheck[]` injected at server construction — each check has `{name, probe: () => Promise<boolean>|boolean}`. No checks configured today (storage-node pending); the extension point is in place so DB/MsgBox/PLC probes drop in without a route rewrite. Body shape: `{status: "ok" | "not_ready", checks: {name: "ok" | "fail"}}`. Returns 503 when any named check fails; probe exceptions logged and treated as fail (doesn't crash the handler). Async probes are awaited before aggregating. **9 server tests** via Fastify `inject()` (no port bind): /healthz 200 + version field shape, /healthz stays 200 when a readiness check would fail (decoupled), /readyz 200 with no checks, /readyz 200 when all pass, /readyz 503 with per-check labels on any fail, probe exceptions → fail, async probes awaited, 4 MiB body limit honored. Deep-probe targets (DB + MsgBox + PLC) land as each adapter wires in — the task's parenthetical is the vision, not a blocker for this iteration.)*
- [x] 4.11 Crash-log writer — panic handler → `crash_log` table *(done 2026-04-21; `src/crash_log.ts` exports `installCrashLogHandlers({logger, writer, exit, flushTimeoutMs})` which traps `uncaughtException` + `unhandledRejection`, writes a structured `CrashEntry` via an injected `CrashLogWriter`, logs `fatal` to the project logger, then exits with code 2 after a short flush window. `CrashEntry` shape: `{at: RFC3339, kind, message, stack?, code?, processStartMs}` — the `processStartMs` is consistent across traps in the same process so ops can correlate multiple crashes to one restart. **`InMemoryCrashLogWriter`** is the starter impl; `@dina/storage-node`'s SQLCipher `crash_log` table implements `CrashLogWriter` when the adapter lands (Phase 3a). **Non-Error reason handling:** strings go through verbatim, plain objects JSON.stringify'd, everything else String(). **`err.code` extraction:** common Node error codes like `ENOTFOUND`/`ECONNREFUSED` are promoted to their own field. **Fail-safe exit:** even when the writer itself throws, we log the write failure + still exit with 2 — a crashed process that refuses to die is worse than one that does. `bin.ts` installs traps after `main()` resolves. **9 tests** in `__tests__/crash_log.test.ts`: in-memory writer order, uncaughtException → write + exit(2), unhandledRejection with Error/string/plain-object reason, err.code extraction, writer-throws still exits, dereg removes handlers, processStartMs consistency across traps.)*
- [x] 4.12 Bin: `dina-home-node-lite-core` *(done 2026-04-21; `src/bin.ts` is the `#!/usr/bin/env node` entry, registered as `dina-home-node-lite-core` in `package.json#/bin`. Async-main with ConfigError → exit 78 (EX_CONFIG per sysexits.h), other errors → exit 1. Wires `installCrashLogHandlers` (task 4.11) + `registerSignalHandlers` (task 4.9) after `main()` resolves — crash traps land BEFORE the crash-log writer storage lands (storage-node pending) so boot-time crashes are caught. **Version resolver** (`src/version.ts`) exports `getServerVersion()` with priority: `DINA_CORE_VERSION` env override (CI release pipelines) → nearest `package.json#version` (walks up from `__dirname`) → `"0.0.0-unknown"` fallback.
