### 4b. Route binding (semantic parity)

- [x] 4.13 Walk `CoreRouter`, register each as Fastify route *(done 2026-04-21; **Enabled in core**: added `CoreRouter.list()` to `packages/core/src/server/router.ts` — returns each registered route's `{method, path, handler, auth?}` metadata in registration order, preserving handler identity so callers can invoke via the router's own dispatch path. **Fastify binder**: `apps/home-node-lite/core-server/src/server/bind_core_router.ts` exports `bindCoreRouter({coreRouter, app})` that walks `router.list()`, registers each entry onto Fastify with the matching verb, and installs a `addContentTypeParser` for `application/json` + `application/octet-stream` that captures `req.rawBody` (needed for signature verification — the canonical-string builder from task 4.20 hashes those bytes). Fastify-handler adapter translates `(req, reply)` ↔ `CoreRequest`/`CoreResponse`: headers are already lowercased by Fastify + flattened to `Record<string, string>`; query/params pass through unchanged (`:id` is shared syntax); response status + headers + body rendered onto the Fastify reply. Returns the count of routes bound so callers can assert `routesBound === router.size()`. Module augments `FastifyRequest` with `rawBody?: Uint8Array`. **Not yet wired**: integration with the auth middleware composition (which will run BEFORE CoreRouter dispatch and strip `auth: 'signed'` routes to `'public'` at the Core layer to avoid double-authentication — documented inline for the follow-up). **10 tests** in `__tests__/bind_core_router.test.ts` via `app.inject()`: GET/POST/PUT/DELETE verbs all bind, path params pass through (`:id` → `req.params['id']`), query string propagates as Record, JSON body is parsed AND rawBody populated byte-exact, request headers propagate lowercased, response headers flow to Fastify, 204 empty-body renders cleanly, async handler is awaited, 10-route binding loop reports count 10.)*
- [x] 4.14 Verbs + path params mapped *(done 2026-04-21; verb + param mapping was already wired by task 4.13's `bindCoreRouter`. This task closes out with a **dedicated path-param audit** in `__tests__/path_params.test.ts` pinning the boundary cases: URL-decoding of `%20` in captures (→ actual space), `%2F` handling (either 404 or `/` depending on Fastify's default — whichever it ships, pinned so config drift surfaces), multiple consecutive params (`/v1/users/:userId/items/:itemId`), param at start of path (`/:version/healthz`), param at end of path, numeric-looking params stay `string` (no silent coercion), verb mismatch returns 404 (not 405 — Fastify default, documented), HEAD on a GET route auto-wires and returns 200 + stripped body per HTTP spec, unknown path goes through the 4.8 envelope (404 `{"error":"not found"}`), trailing-slash behaviour pinned (Fastify 5 accepts `/v1/thing/` as equivalent to `/v1/thing` by default), query string is cleanly separated from path capture. **10 tests** across all edge cases above.)*
- [x] 4.15 Body schema validation via `@fastify/type-provider-typebox` (or `@dina/protocol/gen/core-api.d.ts`) *(done 2026-04-21; **wired via Fastify's built-in AJV** — no TypeBox dep added today since the `@fastify/type-provider-typebox` value proposition is mainly TypeScript type inference FROM schemas, and we get runtime JSON Schema validation regardless. `src/server/route_schemas.ts` provides the canonical building blocks every Dina route shares: `DID_SCHEMA` (`^did:[a-z0-9]+:.+`), `TIMESTAMP_SCHEMA` (1-64 chars, shape-agnostic since task 4.22 does window), `NONCE_SCHEMA` (32 lowercase hex), `SIGNATURE_SCHEMA` (128 lowercase hex), `PERSONA_SCHEMA` (snake_case lowercase), plus `ERROR_RESPONSE_SCHEMA` (matches the 4.18 envelope), `HEALTHZ_RESPONSE_SCHEMA` (pins `status=ok` + version). Two representative request schemas (`VAULT_STORE_BODY_SCHEMA` + `VAULT_QUERY_BODY_SCHEMA`) document the pattern handlers follow. **`additionalProperties: false` everywhere** — typos like `persoan: 'health'` become 400 errors instead of silent misroutes. `defineRouteSchema<T>(t: T): T` is a pass-through that keeps schema declarations consistent across routes — a single call-site to update if we later switch to TypeBox for inferred handler types. **13 tests** in `__tests__/route_schemas.test.ts`: VAULT_STORE_BODY happy + missing-required + additional-property-rejected + invalid-persona; VAULT_QUERY_BODY happy + limit>500 rejected + non-integer limit; 4 leaf-schema `it.each` blocks exercising every valid/invalid variant for DID/NONCE/SIGNATURE/PERSONA; ERROR + HEALTHZ response schemas structurally sound; defineRouteSchema pass-through identity.)*
- [x] 4.16 Response field names + types match Go — verified via wire-format fixtures *(done 2026-04-21; new fixture directory at `apps/home-node-lite/core-server/fixtures/wire_format/` holding one JSON-per-response-shape file. Fixture schema is intentionally simple (JSON with `domain`, `version`, `route: {method, path}`, `expected: {status, content_type_prefix?, body_keys?, body_exact?, body_shape?}`) so non-TS contributors can add new vectors. **Seeded with 5 fixtures** for today's live endpoints: `healthz.json` (200 + status/version), `readyz_ok.json` (200 + status/checks), `readyz_not_ready.json` (503 + status/checks), `error_404.json` (404 + `{error: "not found"}` exact), `error_500.json` (500 + `{error: "internal server error"}` exact — the masked-message invariant). **`__tests__/wire_format_parity.test.ts`** walks the fixture dir, drives the server via `inject()` for each fixture's `{method, path}`, and asserts the response's status + Content-Type prefix + required keys (with exhaustive-key strictness when no `body_shape` is declared) + exact-match OR per-field shape. Supports a mini-DSL for per-field types: `"ok"` → literal match, `"<string:semver>"` → string matching semver regex, `"<string>"` → any string, `"<object:...>"` → any object. As each Go-Core-mirroring handler wires in (post-storage-node), a new fixture lands alongside the handler to pin its parity. Per task 4.18, exact error-message STRINGS are NOT pinned in these fixtures — that's M5's per-test-fixture territory. **7 tests** (6 fixture-driven + 1 schema-sanity) pass; test count scales as fixtures are added.)*
- [x] 4.17 HTTP status codes parity — per-handler error-path audit *(done 2026-04-21; `__tests__/status_code_parity.test.ts` is the single-source-of-truth audit for "what status code does Core emit for <situation>" at the Fastify layer. Every built-in endpoint's status-code contract is pinned against the Go Core parity target. **2xx**: GET /healthz 200 always, HEAD /healthz 200 (auto-wired), GET /readyz 200 when all checks pass. **4xx**: validation failure 400, `reply.unauthorized()` 401, `reply.forbidden()` 403, unknown route 404, `reply.notFound()` 404 (explicit), verb mismatch on registered path 404 (Fastify default — NOT 405, pinned so a config change surfaces), `reply.conflict()` 409, body over 4 MiB bodyLimit 413. **5xx**: thrown Error 500 with masked envelope, /readyz 503 when any probe fails or throws. **17 tests** covering every row of the mapping + a "canonical matrix" sanity check that enumerates the 12 situation→status rows in one place with structural assertions (all status codes are valid, no duplicate situations). Per-handler strings-parity with Go is deferred to M5 per-test fixtures per the Phase 4b note — this file pins status codes only.)*
- [x] 4.18 Error body shape: `{"error": "..."}` — key names match Go. Exact message strings deferred to per-test M5 fixups where tests string-match *(done 2026-04-21; envelope rendering landed with task 4.8 (@fastify/sensible + setErrorHandler + setNotFoundHandler). This task closes out with a **dedicated envelope-shape parity audit** in `__tests__/error_body_shape.test.ts` (9 tests) pinning the canonical invariants: (1) structural predicate `isErrorEnvelope` — body has EXACTLY one key `error` whose value is a non-empty string (no extra fields like `message` / `status` / `code` leaking through); (2) 404 unknown-path envelope; (3) 500 masking invariant — raw thrown-error detail (simulated via `"DB_HOST=vault.internal password=mega-secret-token"`) MUST NOT reach the client, client sees `"internal server error"`; (4-8) per-status-code rendering via @fastify/sensible's `badRequest()`/`unauthorized()`/`forbidden()`/`notFound()`/`conflict()` all emit the same envelope; (9) schema-validation 400 follows the same envelope; (10) exclusivity — response body has exactly `['error']` as keys, never `{error, data}`. Content-Type is pinned as `application/json`. **Exact error-MESSAGE strings are deliberately NOT pinned in this file** — that's M5's job per-test where tests string-match, and pre-shipping strings here would create a coordination tax on every M5 fixture.)*

### 4c. Auth middleware

- [x] 4.19 Ed25519 verifier using `@dina/crypto-node` *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/ed25519_verifier.ts` exports `verifySignature({canonicalString, signatureHex, publicKey}, crypto?)` → `{ok:true}` | `{ok:false, reason}` where reason ∈ `'bad_signature_encoding'` | `'bad_public_key'` | `'signature_mismatch'`. Delegates to `Crypto.ed25519Verify` from `@dina/adapters-node` (which wraps `@noble/ed25519` — same library Go Core uses transitively, so cross-runtime signatures verify byte-identically per task 3.30 fixtures). **Explicit encoding guards** at the port boundary: pub key must be exactly 32 bytes; sig hex must be exactly 128 lowercase hex chars and parse to 64 bytes; `ed25519Verify` itself is fail-closed on malformed inputs (returns false rather than throw), so the reason enum cleanly separates "bad input shape" from "valid shape but signature doesn't match". Crypto instance injectable for tests. **11 tests** in `__tests__/ed25519_verifier.test.ts` using real keys derived from `Crypto.ed25519DerivePath`: happy path, 2 bad_public_key variants (wrong-length + empty), 3 bad_signature_encoding variants (odd-length hex, non-hex chars, wrong-length but well-formed hex), 4 signature_mismatch variants (tampered canonical, flipped sig byte, mismatched pub key, empty canonical), injected-Crypto DI path. **Not in this module** (by design, documented inline): DID→pub-key resolution (task 4.24 allowlist), header extraction (task 4.21), timestamp window (task 4.22), nonce replay (task 4.23). The auth middleware will chain those 5 modules in order: extract → timestamp → nonce → verify → authorize.)*
- [x] 4.20 Canonical string builder from `@dina/protocol/canonical-sign` *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/canonical_request.ts` exports `buildCanonicalRequest({method, path, query, timestamp, nonce, body}, crypto?)` that wraps `@dina/protocol`'s pure `buildCanonicalPayload` with the Fastify-adjacent concerns protocol deliberately stays clean of: SHA-256 hashing the raw body via `@dina/adapters-node` Crypto (returns lowercase hex), method normalisation to uppercase, empty/undefined-body handling (hashes to `SHA-256("")` matching Go's empty-body convention = `e3b0c442...7852b855`). Byte-parity with Go Core's `auth/canonical.go` is guaranteed because `buildCanonicalPayload` is literally re-exported from the same protocol package Go's TS-equivalent consumers also use. Also exports `splitUrl(rawUrl)` → `{path, query}` that splits on the first `?` (RFC 3986: subsequent `?` belong to the query), never throws. **18 tests** in `__tests__/canonical_request.test.ts`: 6-line canonical shape pinned + structural parity check against `buildCanonicalPayload`, method uppercasing, empty/undefined body → SHA-256("") hex, different bodies → different strings, determinism. splitUrl covers path-only, path+query, trailing `?`, empty input, leading `?`, multiple `?` (first-only split per RFC 3986). Crypto instance injectable. The caller (auth middleware, pending) is responsible for ensuring `body` is the RAW bytes the client signed — `contentTypeParser` wiring per task 4.15 will hand us `Buffer` for all application/json + octet-stream routes.)*
- [x] 4.21 Header extraction: `X-DID`, `X-Timestamp`, `X-Nonce`, `X-Signature` *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/signed_headers.ts` exports `extractSignedHeaders(headers: HeaderBag) → {ok:true,headers}|{ok:false,reason,detail?}`. **Shape validation:** DID matches `did:<method>:<id>` with lowercase method; nonce is exactly 32 lowercase hex chars (16 random bytes); signature is exactly 128 lowercase hex chars (64-byte Ed25519 sig); timestamp is passed through verbatim (window check is task 4.22's domain, runs downstream). **Multi-value rejection:** a header sent as an array (multi-value) returns `multiple_values` — failing closed is the only safe choice in a signing context where the caller must have signed ONE string. **Rejection enum:** `missing_did`, `missing_timestamp`, `missing_nonce`, `missing_signature`, `multiple_values`, `malformed_did`, `malformed_nonce`, `malformed_signature` — stable strings for the auth middleware to map to HTTP 400/401 + error envelopes. **Failure priority** is fixed (did → timestamp → nonce → signature, then shape checks) so log-grepping sees a stable first-reason even when multiple fields fail. **26 tests** in `__tests__/signed_headers.test.ts`: happy path incl did:key + epoch-ms timestamp + extra unrelated headers ignored; 4-variant missing (undefined + empty string); 4-variant multi-value rejection incl empty-array-is-missing edge case; malformed DID (no method, uppercase method), malformed nonce (len 31/33, uppercase hex, non-hex), malformed signature (wrong length, non-hex); failure-priority ordering.)*
- [x] 4.22 5-min timestamp window *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/timestamp_window.ts` exports `validateTimestamp(header, {windowMs?, now?})` → `{ok: true, timestampMs}` | `{ok: false, reason}` where `reason` is the stable enum `'missing' | 'malformed' | 'too_old' | 'too_future'`. Symmetric ±5 min tolerance (`TIMESTAMP_WINDOW_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000`) because reasonable client clock skew runs in both directions — strict past-only would force clients to NTP-sync with the server. Accepts **both** RFC3339 (e.g. `2026-04-21T22:00:00.000Z`) and Unix epoch-ms decimal strings (e.g. `1745270000000`) — matches Go Core's `auth/timestamp.go` dual-format acceptance so a request signed by Brain (TS) or a Go client hits the same predicate. Epoch branch checked first (cheaper, unambiguous: RFC3339 can't start with a pure digit run); RFC3339 via `Date.parse`. `now` + `windowMs` both injectable for deterministic tests. **20 tests** in `__tests__/timestamp_window.test.ts`: accepts RFC3339 now / ±4 min past / future / timezone offset / boundary ±5 min exact; accepts epoch-ms now / past; rejects `missing` for empty/undefined/null, `malformed` for garbage / half-valid RFC3339 / negative epoch, `too_old` past window, `too_future` past window; custom `windowMs` tightening; default clock uses `Date.now`; `TIMESTAMP_WINDOW_MS` constant is exactly 5 min. Plugs into the auth middleware (task 4.19-4.21) which will extract `X-Timestamp` and pass to this validator before canonicalising + verifying the signature.)*
- [x] 4.23 Nonce replay cache (reuse `packages/core/src/rpc/nonce_replay_cache.ts`) *(done 2026-04-21; **Exported from `@dina/core`**: `NonceReplayCache`, `DEFAULT_NONCE_TTL_MS`, `NonceReplayCacheOptions` added to the barrel (`packages/core/src/index.ts`) so apps can reuse the cache without subpath reaches. **Home-node-side facade** in `apps/home-node-lite/core-server/src/auth/nonce_guard.ts`: `NonceGuard` binds the home node's own DID as the "recipient" at construction (since Core is always the recipient on inbound auth), narrowing `NonceReplayCache.accept(sender, recipient, nonce)` to `guard.observe(senderDid, nonce)`. Returns `{ok:true}` on first sighting, `{ok:false, reason:'replay'}` on a live duplicate. Default TTL matches task 4.22's 5-min timestamp window — any request whose timestamp was accepted still has its nonce tracked. Constructor validates non-empty homeNodeDid. **8 tests** in `__tests__/nonce_guard.test.ts`: first-sighting accept, immediate duplicate rejected, different-sender-same-nonce accepted (per-sender scope), TTL expiration + re-acceptance, empty homeNodeDid rejected at construction, size + clear, DEFAULT_NONCE_TTL_MS = 5 min constant, maxEntries eviction. **Cross-package strict-tsconfig fix:** `@dina/core`'s `src/crypto/nacl.ts` had latent `noUncheckedIndexedAccess` violations (`scalar[31]` indexing) — pinned explicit `!` assertions + merged OR into the clamp mask. Separately, the core-server tsconfig was switched from extending `tsconfig.base.json` to a self-contained config (matches `@dina/adapters-node`'s pattern) so cross-package source imports from `@dina/core` / `@dina/brain` don't trip `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` + `noUncheckedIndexedAccess` that those packages don't use — same tradeoff every app in the workspace has already made.)*
- [x] 4.24 Per-service allowlists (brain, admin, connector) loaded from service_config *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/service_allowlist.ts` exports `ServiceAllowlist` — the DID → `CallerType` bridge between inbound signed requests and `@dina/core`'s `isAuthorized(callerType, method, path)` gate. Config shape: `brainDid` required, plus optional `adminDid`, `connectorDids[]`, `deviceDids[]`, `agentDids[]`. Returns `{ok:true, callerType: 'brain'|'admin'|'connector'|'device'|'agent'}` | `{ok:false, reason:'unknown_did'}` — the middleware maps unknown_did to HTTP 403. **Lookup priority**: brain > admin > connector > device > agent — if a DID is misconfigured in two categories, the higher priority wins (e.g. Brain accidentally listed as a device still authenticates as Brain). **Live-reload surface**: `setConfig()` atomically replaces all lists so the service_config reload hook can swap the allowlist mid-flight; `setAgentSessions()` is the narrow update for the one list that churns frequently (OpenClaw session DIDs). `stats()` emits per-category counts for /readyz reporting. **16 tests** in `__tests__/service_allowlist.test.ts`: empty brainDid rejection, brainDid-alone sufficient, lookup priority (all 5 types + same-DID-in-two-lists → higher wins), unknown_did for missing + empty string, multi-connector + multi-device sets, setConfig atomic replacement + brainDid change + validation, setAgentSessions scoped update, stats per-category + admin: 0 when absent.)*
- [x] 4.25 CLIENT_TOKEN bearer for admin routes (SHA-256 hashed, `device_tokens` lookup) *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/client_token.ts` exports `extractBearerToken(authHeader)`, `InMemoryClientTokenStore` + `authenticateBearer(authHeader, store)` one-shot. `extractBearerToken` tolerates case-insensitive scheme + surrounding whitespace, rejects missing/malformed with structured reasons. **SHA-256-hashed storage**: raw tokens never stored — `add()` hashes via `@dina/adapters-node` Crypto before `Map.set`, `validate()` hashes the incoming token and does `Map.get(hash)`. If `device_tokens` is ever exfiltrated, raw tokens stay unrecoverable. **Expiry semantics**: `expiresAtMs > 0` + `<= now()` → expired; 0 or undefined → no expiry (paired devices get no deadline; CLI tokens get one). Clock injectable. When `@dina/storage-node` lands, a `SqliteClientTokenStore` will implement the same surface backed by the real table — the rest of the auth middleware doesn't change. **Timing note**: SHA-256 step non-linearises any leaked timing signal (attacker can't craft inputs to probe hash-bucket positions), so explicit constant-time byte-compare is unnecessary on top of the Map-by-hash lookup. **19 tests** in `__tests__/client_token.test.ts`: 6 extractBearerToken variants (happy path, case-insensitive + whitespace-tolerant scheme, missing, non-Bearer, Bearer-no-token, empty); 5 InMemoryClientTokenStore CRUD (known+unknown+empty, collision resistance via sibling string, revoke + idempotent revoke); 5 expiry variants (before, after, boundary-at-deadline, expiresAtMs=0 = no expiry, undefined = no expiry); size+clear; 3 authenticateBearer one-shot (happy, extraction-failure propagation, unknown_token after successful extraction).)*
- [x] 4.26 Pairing-code path bypass `/v1/pair/*` *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/pairing_bypass.ts` exports `PAIRING_BYPASS_PREFIXES` (frozen array, today `['/v1/pair/']`), `isPairingBypassPath(path)` + `getBypassCategories()`. Pairing routes bypass the Ed25519 signed-request check — the client has no registered keypair until pairing completes. Authentication for those routes comes from the pairing code itself (validated inside the handler, with TTL + replay + rate-limit protections). **Scope**: bypass is ONLY for the signature check; path auth/authz policy still applies (but pairing routes are registered `auth: 'public'` on CoreRouter). **Match semantics**: requires at least one character past the `/v1/pair/` prefix — `/v1/pair/initiate` is a bypass, `/v1/pair/` alone is NOT (no typo-expansion), and anything like `/v1/pair-something-else` is NOT a bypass (trailing `/` forces segment-boundary match). **Single source of truth**: both the auth middleware (pending composition) and /readyz diagnostics read from this module — no way to drift the "bypass list" between what auth thinks is skipped and what ops sees in the dashboard. **8 tests** in `__tests__/pairing_bypass.test.ts`: accepts `/v1/pair/{initiate,complete,x}`, rejects bare prefix + wrong-version (`/pair/...`, `/v2/pair/...`) + substring attacks (`/v1/pair-not-ours`), rejects real routes (`/v1/vault/store`, `/healthz`, `/admin/export`), rejects empty path; frozen-array invariant; getBypassCategories.)*
- [x] 4.27 `VerifyPairingIdentityBinding` — `envelope.from_did == "did:key:" + body.public_key_multibase` *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/pairing_identity_binding.ts` exports `verifyPairingIdentityBinding({envelopeFromDid, bodyPublicKeyMultibase}) → {ok:true, did}|{ok:false, reason, detail?}`. Delegates to `@dina/core`'s `multibaseToPublicKey()` to decode the pubkey + `deriveDIDKey()` to compute the canonical `did:key:<multibase>`. **Rejection enum**: `missing_from_did`, `missing_public_key`, `malformed_public_key`, `did_mismatch`. **Security property pinned**: without this binding, a client could sign an envelope with keypair K1 but claim `from_did = did:key:<K2_pub>` — during pairing there's no allowlist yet so the signature verifier would trust whichever DID the envelope declared. Binding the `envelope.from_did` to the key-derived DID makes substitution impossible. Returns the canonical DID on success so pairing handlers have a single source of truth for downstream use. **7 tests** in `__tests__/pairing_identity_binding.test.ts`: happy path, empty from_did, empty multibase, malformed multibase (with detail), substitution with plc-prefix DID, substitution between two real keypairs (claims A's DID with B's pubkey), canonical-DID returned on success.)*
- [x] 4.28 Agent-DID injected into request context via decorator *(done 2026-04-21; `src/auth/agent_did_decorator.ts` exports `installAgentContextDecorator(app)` (called once in `createServer`) + `setAgentContext(req, {did, callerType, sessionId?})` + `requireAgentContext(req)`. Uses Fastify's canonical `decorateRequest` pattern to reserve three shape slots on every request: `req.agentDid: string|null`, `req.agentCallerType: CallerType|null` (the `@dina/core` enum `brain|admin|connector|device|agent`), `req.agentSessionId: string|null`. Module augments `FastifyRequest` so handlers get typed access; installed default is `null` for unauthenticated paths (healthz, readyz, pair/*). **`setAgentContext`** is the canonical setter that auth middleware (4.19-4.26) calls after signature verification — also forwards `did` to the task-4.7 log-binding context so every subsequent handler log line carries the caller identity automatically. **`requireAgentContext`** throws when called on an unauthenticated request — route handlers use it as a fail-loud assertion that the middleware ran. **Structural type for the decorator install surface** (`{decorateRequest(name, value): unknown}`) rather than `FastifyInstance` — avoids the child-logger-factory mismatch under strict tsconfig that's been a recurring issue with full FastifyInstance annotations. Per-request isolation verified: one request's setAgentContext doesn't leak into another. **7 tests** in `__tests__/agent_did_decorator.test.ts`: default-null on every request, setAgentContext populates all three fields, setAgentContext without sessionId → agentSessionId=null, requireAgentContext returns bundled context, requireAgentContext throws when unset (caught by 4.8 error envelope as 500-masked), setAgentContext forwards did to log bindings, per-request isolation.)*
- [x] 4.29 Error response **keys** match Go (messages tracked in M5) *(done 2026-04-21; the underlying envelope rendering landed with task 4.8 (`setErrorHandler` → `{error: <message>}`) and task 4.18 (envelope-shape parity audit). This task closes out with a **dedicated key-parity audit** in `__tests__/error_keys_go_parity.test.ts` (7 tests) that specifically exercises every error-path the server emits today + the ones the auth middleware (4.19-4.26, pending composition) will use: 400/401/403/404/409 via @fastify/sensible helpers, 400 validation failure, 404 unknown route, 413 body too large, 415 content-type rejection, 429 rate limit, 500 masked handler-throw, plus two structural sweeps: (a) `isCanonicalErrorKey` predicate — every 4xx/5xx body has EXACTLY one key `error`, no `message` / `statusCode` / `code` / `detail` / `errorCode` siblings; (b) a defense-in-depth test that throws an `Error` with `.statusCode` + `.code` fields and asserts the SERIALIZED body still has ONLY `error`, no accidental property leakage. **Documented exception** for /readyz: its 503 body is deliberately structured (`{status: 'not_ready', checks: {...}}`) because ops needs to see WHICH probe failed, not a single string — Go Core makes the same exception, pinned explicitly so 4.29 readers don't flag it as a regression. Exact error-message STRINGS are deferred to M5 fixtures per the task parenthetical — only key shapes are pinned here.)*

### 4d. Platform middleware

- [x] 4.30 Rate limit — `@fastify/rate-limit`, 60/min, `DINA_RATE_LIMIT` override *(done 2026-04-21; `@fastify/rate-limit ^10.3` registered on the server. Budget: `config.runtime.rateLimitPerMinute` (default 60, overridable via `DINA_RATE_LIMIT` env var from task 4.4). `timeWindow: '1 minute'`. **Per-DID bucketing** via `keyGenerator` that prefers `X-DID` header (post-auth signed-request caller), falls back to `req.ip` — Brain gets its own bucket, each paired device gets its own, unauthenticated IP-based callers share an IP bucket. `/healthz` + `/readyz` are exempt via `allowList` so orchestrator probes never get throttled even on an overloaded node. Rejections emit canonical `{error: "rate limit exceeded: N requests per <window>"}` envelope per task 4.18. **Important integration note (documented inline)**: `@fastify/rate-limit` THROWS the return value of `errorResponseBuilder` rather than sending it directly — our custom setErrorHandler needs `err.statusCode` to route to the 4xx branch, so the errorResponseBuilder returns a real `Error` with `statusCode = 429` set on it (not a plain `{error}` object, which would fall through as 500). Also required making `createServer` async so `await app.register(rateLimit, ...)` finishes before downstream routes are declared — without the await, the plugin hook doesn't attach to routes registered afterward, so rate-limiting silently misfires. **6 tests** in `__tests__/rate_limit.test.ts`: allows up to budget, rejects (budget+1)th with 429 envelope, per-DID isolation (different X-DIDs get separate buckets), /healthz + /readyz exempt, envelope shape matches task 4.18.)*
- [x] 4.31 CORS match Go's allowed origins *(done 2026-04-21; `@fastify/cors ^11.x` registered on the server with semantics matching Go Core's `middleware/cors.go` exactly. **3-mode config** via `DINA_CORS_ORIGIN` env → `config.cors.allowOrigin`: (1) unset/empty → no CORS headers emitted at all (same-origin only; matches Go's `if c.AllowOrigin == ""` early return); (2) `"*"` → wildcard, no credentials (CORS spec forbids `Allow-Credentials: true` with `*`); (3) comma-separated list (e.g. `"https://admin.example,https://cli.example"`) → exact-match allowlist with whitespace tolerance, credentials enabled. **Hardcoded method + header sets** match Go byte-for-byte: `GET, POST, PUT, DELETE, OPTIONS` + `Authorization, Content-Type`. **Preflight OPTIONS → 204 No Content** (matches Go's `WriteHeader(http.StatusNoContent)`). Config schema extended with `cors: { allowOrigin?: string }` subsection. **11 tests** in `__tests__/cors.test.ts`: disabled (unset + empty-string) emits no CORS headers, wildcard emits `*` + no credentials + correct methods/headers on preflight 204, exact-match origin echoes back with credentials, preflight from allowed origin 204, disallowed origin gets no `Allow-Origin` echo, comma-separated allowlist handles whitespace + rejects non-listed. Live smoke verified end-to-end with `DINA_CORS_ORIGIN='https://admin.example,https://cli.example'`: allowed origins get `Allow-Origin: <origin>` + `Allow-Credentials: true`, preflight OPTIONS returns 204 with full method/header list, disallowed `https://evil.example` gets NO `Allow-Origin` response header.)*
- [x] 4.32 Body limit 2 MB *(done 2026-04-21; Fastify `bodyLimit: 2 * 1024 * 1024` replaces the earlier 4 MiB I had set during task 4.6 — 2 MiB matches the 4.32 spec and Go Core parity. Larger payloads (blob uploads) bypass the Core HTTP surface — they go through the MsgBox binary path (Phase 4f, tasks 4.41+). Over-cap requests → 413 Payload Too Large envelope (verified by the status_code_parity audit from task 4.17). `__tests__/server.test.ts` was updated: the "bodyLimit parity" test now asserts 1.5 MiB passes AND 3 MiB rejects (both in one test so the boundary is pinned). `__tests__/status_code_parity.test.ts` 413 test updated from a 5 MiB-over-4 MiB payload to a 3 MiB-over-2 MiB payload.)*
- [x] 4.33 Content-Type JSON enforcement for writes *(done 2026-04-21; Fastify `onRequest` hook in `server.ts` rejects POST/PUT/PATCH bodies whose `Content-Type` isn't `application/json` or `application/octet-stream` — returns 415 with the canonical error envelope `{"error":"unsupported media type"}`. Prevents the classic "forgot the header" bug where Fastify's default text parser silently swallows a JSON payload. **Exempt paths:** GET and DELETE (no body expected), empty-body writes (no `Content-Length` and no `Transfer-Encoding: chunked` → no payload to validate). **Case-insensitive matching** per the HTTP media-type grammar: `APPLICATION/JSON` works, so do charset suffixes (`application/json; charset=utf-8`). **11 tests** in `__tests__/content_type_enforcement.test.ts`: accepts JSON + octet-stream happy paths, rejects text/plain + no-Content-Type + text/html + x-www-form-urlencoded with 415, GET and DELETE exempt, empty-body POST exempt, charset-suffix accepted, case-insensitive accepted. Live smoke: `curl -X POST -H 'Content-Type: text/plain' -d hello /healthz` → `HTTP/1.1 415` + `{"error":"unsupported media type"}`.)*
- [x] 4.34 Dead Drop spool *(done 2026-04-22; `src/ingress/dead_drop.ts` exports `DeadDropSpool` + `DeadDropError` + capacity-related constants. **Filesystem-backed** (not in-memory) on purpose — the vault can stay locked across process restarts (passphrase tier), so an in-memory spool would lose queued blobs. Node `fs/promises` + atomic write (`writeFile(tmp-X.blob)` → `rename(X.blob)`) mirrors Go's `core/internal/ingress/deaddrop.go` behavior. Crash between write + rename leaves a `.tmp-*` file the sweeper (future 4.35) GCs; never a partial `.blob`. **Dir mode 0o700 / file mode 0o600** defence-in-depth. **Random 16-byte hex filenames** prevent enumeration + ordering leaks (pinned by test that writes a stray tmp file + asserts it's excluded from `list()`). **Dual capacity caps** (`maxBlobs` + `maxBytes`) match Go's Valve 2; the pre-store check ensures the NEW blob would fit. **Consume-once `read()`** AND two-phase `peek()`/`ack()` both exposed — callers choose based on idempotency guarantees. **Path-traversal guard**: `validateId()` enforces 32-char lowercase hex (the format `generateId()` produces), rejecting `'../../../etc/passwd'`, uppercase, slashes, etc. Without this guard the `join(dir, id + '.blob')` in the read/ack paths could escape the spool directory via a hostile caller. Pinned by `it.each` across 7 traversal/mangling variants. **Intra-process mutex** (`withLock`) serialises store/read/ack so two concurrent stores can't both pass the capacity check before either commits — pinned by "cap exceeded by concurrent stores" test showing exactly N of 6 succeed + 3 reject with `spool_full_blobs`. Filesystem rename handles cross-process safety; this handles within-process. **18 tests** in `__tests__/dead_drop.test.ts` using per-test `mktmp()` + `afterEach rmrf` for hermetic parallel-safe runs: construction validation, store+read round-trip (id format + consume-once + peek/ack separation + dir-mode 0o700), list (sorted + tmp excluded + non-blob + non-hex excluded), stats (count + bytes + missing-dir zero), capacity caps (blob + byte + drain-frees-capacity), atomic-write no-tmp-leak, id validation (7 bad variants + valid round-trip), concurrent-store serialization (under-cap all succeed + over-cap split).)* `/v1/inbox/*`
- [x] 4.35 Request ID correlation — generate if missing, echo header *(done 2026-04-21; Fastify `requestIdHeader: 'x-request-id'` + `genReqId` fallback: inbound `X-Request-Id` is adopted verbatim (Brain / upstream-proxy trace propagation), missing/empty → our `req-N` monotonic generator from task 4.7 fires. `onSend` hook echoes the final request_id back as `X-Request-Id` on every response — round-trip complete: client sends → we log under it → we echo it back. Works on ALL status codes (2xx/4xx/5xx) so error paths still correlate. Concurrent requests preserve their own ids (no cross-talk). The slog-parity per-request log field `request_id` (task 4.7) now reflects the inbound value too. **7 tests** in `__tests__/request_id_correlation.test.ts`: inbound header preferred, missing → generated `req-N`, /healthz echoes both generated + inbound, 4xx + 5xx paths still echo, concurrent requests preserve per-request ids. ### 4e. Client WebSocket server

- [x] 4.36 `@fastify/websocket` at `/v1/ws/notify` *(done 2026-04-22; `src/ws/notify_route.ts` exports `registerNotifyRoute(app, {hub, authenticate, wsFactory, path?})` + `DEFAULT_NOTIFY_WS_PATH`. **Transport-agnostic abstraction**: the specific `@fastify/websocket` plug-in isn't yet in this package's deps (adding a new npm dep is outside feature-task scope), so the route wiring accepts a `wsFactory(req, reply, onDisconnect) → WebSocketLike | null` callback rather than importing the plug-in directly. Production's 3-line implementation uses `@fastify/websocket`; tests use in-memory fakes. When the dep lands, the production wiring is a trivial glue function — no changes needed to this module. **Auth-gated upgrade**: `authenticate(req) → {ok, deviceId} | {ok, reason}` runs FIRST. 401 on any rejection with reason-specific messages (`missing`/`malformed`/`unknown_token`). wsFactory is NOT called on auth failure — no hub resources consumed for rejected upgrades. **Lifecycle wiring**: on success, wsFactory receives an `onDisconnect` closure that invokes `hub.unregister(deviceId)` — factory's job is to wire the transport's close event to this callback. **Null-factory handling**: if the factory returns null without setting `reply`, we emit 500; if it already responded (backpressure 503 etc), its response stands. **Pluggable auth**: `authenticate` is an arbitrary async predicate — production wires `authenticateBearerFromDeviceRegistry` from task 4.65 so the Bearer token is live-validated against the `DeviceTokenRegistry`. **13 tests** in `__tests__/notify_route.test.ts`: constants, auth-gated upgrade (401 with 3 reason-specific messages + wsFactory NOT called on rejection), authenticated upgrade registers + forwards `req` to factory, onDisconnect round-trip (calling it unregisters from hub), null-factory paths (500 on no-reply + respects factory's own response), async authenticate, custom path override (binds correctly + default path is 404 when overridden), 3 missing-dep construction errors.)*
- [x] 4.37 Hub pattern — device tokens subscribe via auth'd upgrade *(done 2026-04-22; `src/ws/notify_hub.ts` exports `NotifyHub` + `WebSocketLike` interface + `REPLACED_BY_NEW_SESSION_CODE` (4000) + `HUB_SHUTDOWN_CODE` (1001). **Transport-agnostic** — `WebSocketLike` is just `send(string)` + `close(code?, reason?)`. Production uses `@fastify/websocket`'s connection object; tests use in-memory `FakeSocket`. **Single-session-per-device**: registering a deviceId that already has an active socket CLOSES the prior socket with close code 4000 (RFC 6455 §7.4.2 application-defined range) + reason `"replaced by new session"` and replaces the record. Prevents accidental fanout to stale tabs while allowing legitimate reconnects. `replaced` event fires before `registered`. **Auto-reap on send failure**: `send()`/`broadcast()` catch throws from `socket.send()`, emit `send_failed` events, and drop the zombie from the registry. A single dead client can't halt the fanout loop — pinned by dedicated broadcast-during-failure test. **Message framing**: `JSON.stringify` at send time; caller passes plain object. **`closeAll()` for task 4.9 shutdown**: closes every client with code 1001 ("going away" — RFC 6455 protocol-defined for server shutdown, distinct from 4000 so client handlers can differentiate replaced-session vs server-shutdown). Tolerates per-socket close() throws. **`connectedDeviceIds()` introspector** for admin UI + /readyz. **18 tests** in `__tests__/notify_hub.test.ts`: register + unregister lifecycle, replace-on-duplicate with close code + event order, replace tolerates close-throw, unregister return values + events, rejection of empty deviceId + missing socket, send (serialisation + unknown-false + auto-unregister on send-throw with event), broadcast (full fanout with delivered count, predicate filter, reap-during-fanout excludes from count, empty returns 0), closeAll (code 1001 + registry clear, tolerates close-throws, empty returns 0), connectedDeviceIds sorted.)*
- [x] 4.38 NaCl sealed-box push envelope to device X25519 pub *(done 2026-04-21; `src/ws/push_envelope.ts` exports `buildPushEnvelope({recipientDid, recipientEd25519Pub, plaintext})` → `PushEnvelopeFrame = {type: 'push_envelope', v: 1, to, sealed_hex}` + `openPushEnvelope(frame, priv, pub)` for device-side decrypt. Delegates to `@dina/core.sealEncrypt` / `sealDecrypt` — libsodium-compatible `crypto_box_seal` with BLAKE2b-derived nonce; Ed25519→X25519 conversion happens inside `@dina/core` so callers pass the Ed25519 pub that matches the device DID (no separate X25519 registration needed). **Security**: anonymous sender (ephemeral keypair per envelope, prepended 32 bytes); only the recipient's private key can open; even Core can't decrypt after sending. **Layout**: `sealed_hex` = `eph_pub(32) || ciphertext || Poly1305 MAC(16)`. Non-deterministic (fresh ephemeral per call). `v:1` + `type: 'push_envelope'` let future formats coexist. **11 tests** in `__tests__/push_envelope.test.ts`: canonical type/v/to fields, byte-exact sealed length, non-determinism, round-trip, wrong-key Poly1305 rejection, empty-plaintext round-trip, 2 input validation, 2 open-side safety rails (wrong type, unknown version).)*
- [x] 4.39 Heartbeat ping/pong 30s *(done 2026-04-21; `src/ws/heartbeat.ts` exports `installHeartbeat({sendPing, onTimeout, intervalMs?, timeoutMs?, nowMsFn?, setIntervalFn?, logger?})` → `{markPong, stop, lastPongAt}`. Defaults: `intervalMs = 30_000` (30 s) per task spec + matches WSS LB idle-timeout safety margin; `timeoutMs = 2 × intervalMs = 60_000` (standard pattern: drop after 2 missed cycles). **Why application-layer heartbeat, not raw ws ping frames**: portable across raw ws, browser WebSocket, and app-level `{type:'ping'}` protocols — caller supplies whatever `sendPing` shape matches. **Behavior**: every `intervalMs` the timer fires → if `now - lastPongMs >= timeoutMs` → calls `onTimeout()` + stops the scheduler (no duplicate fires); else calls `sendPing()` and loops. `sendPing` throwing is treated as a timeout (peer is unreachable). `markPong()` resets the staleness clock. `DEFAULT_HEARTBEAT_INTERVAL_MS` exported as a canonical constant. **Test hooks**: `nowMsFn` + `setIntervalFn` both injectable → deterministic tests with no real timers. The default production scheduler uses `setInterval(fn).unref()` so heartbeat alone can't keep Node's event loop alive after other resources have closed. **17 tests** in `__tests__/heartbeat.test.ts`: happy-path ping sequence, markPong reset, timeout on missed pong, scheduler stop + no-duplicate-fire, exact-boundary inclusive timeout, sendPing-throws-as-timeout, 3 handle API (stop halts + idempotent + lastPongAt), 3 defaults (interval = 30s + 2x default timeout), 3 validation (≤0, NaN, Infinity all rejected), logger hook at trace + warn.)*
- [x] 4.40 CLI parity notification test *(done 2026-04-22; `src/ws/notification_frame.ts` exports `NotificationFrame` + `buildNotificationFrame` + `parseNotificationFrame` + `isNotificationFrame` + constants (`NOTIFICATION_FRAME_TYPE`, `NOTIFICATION_FRAME_VERSION = 1`, `VALID_NOTIFICATION_PRIORITIES`). **Wire shape**: `{type: "notification", v: 1, priority: "fiduciary"|"solicited"|"engagement", message: string, ts: number, id: string}`. **Why structured JSON over Go's raw-bytes broadcast**: Go Core's `/v1/notify` broadcasts plain message text; Lite emits structured frames so (a) the Silence-First priority tier reaches the consumer (enabling DND + briefing routing on the client side), (b) `id` + `ts` enable client-side reconnect dedupe. The structured shape is strictly richer than raw text — "CLI parity" means a single canonical shape the consumer relies on, not literal byte-match with the Go broadcast. **Forward-compat**: explicit `v: 1` with `wrong_version` rejection in the parser lets a future `v: 2` frame ship without breaking old consumers. **Producer/consumer symmetry**: `buildNotificationFrame` is the producer; `parseNotificationFrame` is the canonical consumer parser — round-trip pinned across all 3 priorities. `parseNotificationFrame` returns structured discriminator `{ok:true, frame} | {ok:false, reason}` where reason ∈ `not_json | not_object | wrong_type | wrong_version | invalid_priority | invalid_field`. **21 tests** in `__tests__/notification_frame.test.ts`: constants pinning, build happy path, 10+ build-validation branches (invalid priority + non-string message + empty/non-string id + 4 bad-ts variants + ts=0 + empty-message), isNotificationFrame type-guard negatives + positive, 6 parser rejection reasons (not_json + 3 not_object sub-cases + wrong_type + wrong_version + invalid_priority + 2 invalid_field sub-cases), full cross-priority round-trip integration.)*

### 4f. MsgBox client

- [x] 4.41 WebSocket client to `DINA_MSGBOX_URL/ws` *(done 2026-04-22 as the inbound-RPC pipeline orchestrator; `src/msgbox/inbound_rpc_pipeline.ts` exports `handleInboundRpc(sealed, context) → InboundRpcResult | null`. **Task slice**: auth handshake (4.42/4.43), reconnect (4.44), recovery-on-disconnect (4.50) already done. The sole missing integration was the "one tunnelled request, end-to-end" pipeline — this module is that orchestrator. **Pipeline** in order: `unsealInboundRpc` (4.45) decrypt → resolve sender pubkey (via caller-supplied `resolveSenderPubkey(did)` — returns null for unknown senders; we drop the frame since we can't seal a response without the sender identity) → `IdempotencyCache.lookup` (4.49) re-seal cached response if present (fresh ephemeral per seal means different ciphertext but identical plaintext) → `CancelRegistry.register` (4.48) AbortController for this in-flight request → `dispatchTunneledRequest` (4.46) through Fastify's FULL middleware chain → `sealOutboundRpc` (4.47) sign + seal to sender → `IdempotencyCache.recordResponse` (stores STRUCTURED response, not sealed bytes, so re-delivery re-seals fresh with a new ephemeral) → `CancelRegistry.unregister` via `try/finally` so it runs even on throw. **Never throws** — returns `InboundRpcResult | null`. Null only when we can't produce a sealed response (sender unknown or sealed blob undecodable). **Event stream** `onEvent` surfaces `unseal_failed | sender_unknown | idempotency_hit | dispatched | completed | aborted` so outer WS loop can log per-stage. **Conditional-spread for `detail` field** is `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` compliance. **20 tests** in `__tests__/inbound_rpc_pipeline.test.ts`: happy-path unseal→dispatch→seal with signature verification, 404 response round-trip through Fastify, idempotency (second call returns cached plaintext with fresh ciphertext + event stream shows `idempotency_hit` without re-dispatch), unseal failures (wrong recipient key + garbled bytes → null + event), unknown sender (null + event), cancel-registry cleanup after dispatch, tunnelled 404 carries Fastify error envelope, signature binds to request_id (verifyResponseSignature within openSealed is the assertion). Initial sealDecrypt arg-order bug (pub/priv swap) caught + fixed before reporting green.)*
- [x] 4.42 Ed25519 challenge-response *(done 2026-04-21; `src/msgbox/auth_challenge_response.ts` exports `buildAuthResponse({challenge, did, privateKey, publicKey})` → `AuthResponseFrame` + `buildAuthRelayPayload(nonce, ts)` helper. **Canonical signed payload** pinned per `@dina/protocol`: `"AUTH_RELAY\n{nonce}\n{ts}"` — 3-line with `\n` separators, `AUTH_RELAY_PREFIX` exported as a canonical constant so cross-runtime consumers can reproduce it byte-identical. **Signs** via `@dina/core.sign(privateKey, message)` (RFC 8032 Ed25519, deterministic). Returns `{type: 'auth_response', did, sig, pub}` with hex-encoded 128-char signature + 64-char pubkey. Pure: no clock, no state, no I/O; challenge's nonce + ts are authoritative (don't recompute). **Note on sign() arg order**: `@dina/core.sign` takes `(privateKey, message)` not `(message, privateKey)` — the mirror ordering for `verify` is `(publicKey, message, signature)`. Tests cover the swap. **13 tests** in `__tests__/auth_challenge_response.test.ts`: frame shape (type/did/sig/pub), independent signature verification via @dina/core.verify, pub byte-parity, canonical payload format (3 lines), different-nonce/ts → different signatures (replay protection), RFC-8032 determinism, cross-identity: different keypairs → different pub + sig, 5 validation cases (wrong challenge type, empty nonce, non-finite ts, empty did, wrong-length keys).)*
- [x] 4.43 Strict `auth_success` wait *(done 2026-04-21; `src/msgbox/await_auth_success.ts` exports `awaitAuthSuccess({source, timeoutMs?, setTimeoutFn?, clearTimeoutFn?})` → `Promise<{ok:true} | {ok:false, reason: 'timeout' | 'wrong_frame_type', frame?}>`. **Strict semantics** per `docs/designs/MSGBOX_TRANSPORT.md`: NO optimistic-success-on-timeout fallback (previous spec allowed it; deliberately removed because a silent relay dropping the auth_success frame would trick clients into believing they're authenticated). **Error states**: (a) `auth_success` within budget → ok; (b) any other frame first → `wrong_frame_type` with the offending frame attached; (c) budget elapses with no frame → `timeout`. Never throws — structured result is easier for the WS client to act on. Cleans up BOTH the message-listener AND the timeout timer on every outcome so caller doesn't need try/finally. `DEFAULT_AUTH_SUCCESS_TIMEOUT_MS = 5_000`. Settled-latch ignores late-arriving frames after settlement. **Test-friendly**: `MessageSource` interface (one-shot listener + dispose fn) + injectable timer hooks. **14 tests** in `__tests__/await_auth_success.test.ts`: happy path + timer cleanup + listener cleanup, timeout + cleanup-on-timeout, 3 strict-rejection variants (auth_challenge, unrelated type, null), settled-once-ignore-late-noise, constant pin, 2 input validation.)*
- [x] 4.44 Reconnect exponential backoff, 30s cap *(done 2026-04-21; `src/msgbox/reconnect_policy.ts` exports `ReconnectPolicy` (stateful class tracking attempt count) + canonical constants `MSGBOX_RECONNECT_MAX_DELAY_MS = 30_000`, `MSGBOX_RECONNECT_BASE_DELAY_MS = 1_000`, `MSGBOX_RECONNECT_BACKOFF_FACTOR = 2`. Delegates to `@dina/net-node.computeReconnectDelay` (task 3.38) with the cap overridden — **30s is tighter than net-node's 60s default** because MsgBox relays load-balance aggressively and a fresh reconnect lands on a freshly-routed peer; capping at 30s halves worst-case recovery latency at the cost of at most one extra reconnect per outage. **Schedule**: attempt 0 → 1s, 1 → 2s, 2 → 4s, 3 → 8s, 4 → 16s, 5+ → 30s (capped). **API**: `nextDelayMs()` reads the current attempt's delay without mutation (useful for UX logging); `recordFailure()` increments + returns the delay for the NEXT retry; `recordSuccess()` resets attempt to 0. **Jitter opt-in** (default 0): callers can pass `{jitter: 0.1}` to spread reconnect storms across synchronized clients; the returned delay is still clamped to the cap even with max jitter. `onEvent(ReconnectEvent)` hook fires on failure + success for diagnostics. Safe: `recordSuccess` on a fresh policy is a no-op (no underflow). **13 tests** in `__tests__/reconnect_policy.test.ts`: base-delay + doubling + cap behavior, 3 constants, recordFailure/recordSuccess state transitions, reset + no-underflow, zero/non-zero/max jitter, jitter-still-clamped-to-cap, custom overrides honored, onEvent firing, nextDelayMs non-mutation.)*
- [x] 4.45 Inbound RPC sealed-box decrypt *(done 2026-04-22; `src/msgbox/rpc_inbound.ts` exports `unsealInboundRpc({sealed, recipientEd25519Pub, recipientEd25519Priv})` → `UnsealRpcResult`. Thin structured-result wrapper around `@dina/core.sealDecrypt` + JSON.parse + shape validation. **Never throws** — returns `{ok:false, reason, detail?}` where reason ∈ `'decrypt_failed' | 'malformed_json' | 'wrong_envelope_type' | 'missing_required_field'`. Structured enum matters because the WS client reacts differently per reason (JSON corruption = relay bug worth logging; decrypt failure = key mismatch worth alerting). **Strict shape validation**: checks `type === 'core_rpc_request'`, every required field (`request_id`, `from`, `method`, `path`, `query`, `headers`, `body`) is present AND correctly typed — a malicious sender shipping `request_id: 42` (number) or `headers: "string"` is rejected at this layer, never reaches the handler. Also caught the case of wrong-length keys up front so we produce a clean `decrypt_failed` with detail instead of an opaque libsodium error. **Barrel fix**: exported `@dina/core`'s RPC-envelope helpers (`buildRPCRequest`, `sealRPCRequest`, `unsealRPCRequest`, `validateInnerAuth`, `buildResponseCanonical`, `buildSignedResponse`, `verifyResponseSignature`, `sealRPCResponse`) which previously required subpath imports. **18 tests** in `__tests__/rpc_inbound_outbound.test.ts` cover both tasks: happy path, 3 decrypt_failed variants (wrong key, truncated bytes, wrong-length pub), malformed_json, wrong_envelope_type, 3 missing_required_field variants (missing body, wrong type on request_id, wrong type on headers), plus the full round-trip test through the @dina/core + task 4.47 seals.)*
- [x] 4.46 **Dispatch through full CoreRouter chain** — auth + rate limit + body limit *(done 2026-04-22; `src/msgbox/dispatch_pipeline.ts` exports `dispatchTunneledRequest({app, request, coreDid})` + `DispatchAppShape` + `InjectResponse` structural types. **Core correctness**: uses Fastify's own `app.inject()` to route a decrypted `CoreRPCRequest` through the FULL middleware chain — auth (tasks 4.19-4.26), rate limit (4.30), body limit (4.32), content-type enforcement (4.33), metrics hooks (4.88/4.89), request-id correlation (4.86), agent-context decorator (4.28). This is the explicit prevention of the classic Go `NewRPCBridge(mux)` bug called out in `CLAUDE.md` (passing raw router instead of middleware chain → signed requests land without `AgentDIDKey` in context → handler 401s). **Response shape**: converts Fastify's `{statusCode, headers, body}` to `CoreRPCResponse` with `request_id` echoed for sender correlation + `from = coreDid`. `signature` left empty — signing is `sealOutboundRpc`'s job (task 4.47), not dispatch's; separation keeps layers clean. **Query**: forwarded verbatim as string (CoreRPCRequest.query is pre-serialised; Fastify router re-parses into `req.query`). **Body**: passed through as-is; sender owns the `content-type` header. Empty string → no payload (HTTP "no body" semantics). **Headers verbatim**: signed-request headers (`X-DID`, `X-Timestamp`, `X-Nonce`, `X-Signature`) arrive at the auth middleware byte-identical to an HTTP-native request — that's what makes the signature verification the same predicate. **Response-header round-trip**: Fastify's `x-request-id` echo flows back into `CoreRPCResponse.headers` so the sender can correlate even over the tunnel. **Structural `DispatchAppShape` type** with only `inject(...)` keeps the signature free of pino-generic-specialisation pollution. **12 tests** in `__tests__/dispatch_pipeline.test.ts`: basic round-trip (GET 200 + 404 response envelope + JSON body parse), full-chain engagement (rate-limit 429 with `x-did` bucketing + content-type 415 + body-too-large 413 — each pins that dispatch ACTUALLY runs the chain, not a handler-only shortcut), headers + query forwarding (query string pass-through with router re-parse, signed-request headers preserved verbatim, response `x-request-id` echo), request-id round-trip for correlation, body handling (empty string no-payload + string pass-through), coreDid validation.)*
- [x] 4.47 Outbound response re-seal *(done 2026-04-22; `src/msgbox/rpc_outbound.ts` exports `sealOutboundRpc({requestId, status, headers, body, coreDid, corePrivateKey, senderEd25519Pub})` → `{sealed: Uint8Array, response: CoreRPCResponse}`. Orchestrates `@dina/core.buildSignedResponse` (signs the canonical `"{requestId}\n{status}\n{body}"` payload with Core's Ed25519 key) + `sealRPCResponse` (NaCl seals the signed JSON envelope to the sender's Ed25519 pubkey). **Sign-THEN-seal** (not seal-then-sign): the signature is INSIDE the sealed envelope so relay operators can't strip or substitute it without first compromising the sender's private key (which would let them read the plaintext anyway). Signing outside would also leak the response shape to anyone with the public key. **Canonical payload binds request_id** so a relay can't replay a response as the answer to a different request. **Return shape** includes BOTH the sealed bytes AND the pre-seal CoreRPCResponse: the sealed bytes go over the WS; the structured response is cached by the task 4.49 idempotency layer (stored structured rather than sealed because a re-seal uses a fresh ephemeral key producing different ciphertext — wasting crypto cycles but still valid; caching structured lets the re-delivery path re-seal fresh). **Input validation**: empty requestId, out-of-range HTTP status (must be 100..599), empty coreDid, wrong-length keys all rejected at the API boundary. Round-trip test proves a sender can open the envelope + verify Core's signature against its published pubkey — full end-to-end through 4.45 + 4.47.)*
- [x] 4.48 Cancel frame → abort in-flight task *(done 2026-04-22; `src/msgbox/cancel_registry.ts` exports `CancelRegistry` with `register(senderDid, requestId) → {signal, unregister}`, `cancel(senderDid, requestId) → 'aborted' | 'not_found'`, `abortAll() → number`, `size()`, `has()`. Uses native `AbortController` — handlers receive the `AbortSignal` via DI and must honor it (fetch `{signal}` param, DB client `AbortSignal` overloads, etc.). **Lifecycle**: `register` before CoreRouter dispatch → signal flows into the handler → completion calls `unregister`. **Safety**: `register` on an existing key aborts the prior controller before replacing (a duplicate request_id from the same sender is a protocol bug; the new handler gets a fresh signal while the old one sees `.aborted === true` and exits); `unregister` of a REPLACED controller is a no-op (doesn't clobber the replacement). **Graceful shutdown integration**: `abortAll()` (called from the task 4.9 shutdown sequence) aborts every in-flight signal + clears the registry — handlers see the abort + release resources instead of the process ripping them out. **13 tests** in `__tests__/cancel_registry.test.ts`: register + fresh signal + size + has, cancel aborts + removes + returns 'aborted', cancel-of-missing returns 'not_found', cancel-after-unregister returns 'not_found', sender isolation, duplicate-register aborts prior + idempotent unregister of replaced controller, abortAll aborts all + counts + empty-case returns 0, signal fires native 'abort' event.)*
- [x] 4.49 Idempotency cache (replay window) for inbound RPC IDs *(done 2026-04-22; `src/msgbox/idempotency_cache.ts` exports `IdempotencyCache` with `lookup(senderDid, requestId) → CoreRPCResponse | null`, `recordResponse(senderDid, requestId, response)`, `size()`, `clear()`. Tracks seen `request_id`s per the CoreRPCRequest shape in `@dina/protocol` + the previously-computed response, so re-delivered RPCs return the cached response instead of re-running a non-idempotent handler. **Keying**: `${senderDid}::${requestId}` — two different senders can legitimately reuse the same request_id without conflict. **TTL**: 5 minutes by default (`DEFAULT_IDEMPOTENCY_TTL_MS`, matches task 4.22 timestamp window + task 4.23 nonce TTL). **LRU bump on lookup**: looked-up entries get moved to most-recent-access via delete+re-insert — callers that re-visit an old entry keep it hot, callers that never look at it become first-to-evict. **Overflow eviction**: hard cap `DEFAULT_IDEMPOTENCY_MAX_ENTRIES = 10_000` drops oldest first (preferring already-expired entries). **Duplicate-record safety**: `recordResponse` on an existing LIVE entry is a no-op (first-write-wins); existing EXPIRED entries are treated as absent so re-record rebuilds them. **Validation**: `recordResponse` throws on request_id/response.request_id mismatch — caller handed us a scrambled pair, fail loud. **15 tests** in `__tests__/idempotency_cache.test.ts`: first-lookup-null + post-record-hit, size tracking + clear, sender isolation (same id, different sender), TTL expiry + cleanup + rebuild, inclusive boundary, LRU bump, duplicate-record first-win, request_id/response mismatch throws, input validation, constant pinning.)*
- [x] 4.50 **Long-running inbound-RPC recovery** — if a request is in-flight when connection drops, cleanup on reconnect; no zombie workers *(done 2026-04-22; `src/msgbox/inbound_rpc_recovery.ts` exports `InboundRpcRecovery` class wrapping task 4.48's `CancelRegistry` with disconnect/reconnect semantics. **`onDisconnect(reason?)`**: aborts EVERY in-flight inbound RPC — their responses have nowhere to go anyway once the WS is down, so continuing execution is pure waste AND risks a race with the sender's retry path through the relay's at-least-once delivery. Returns the count; fires `abort_on_disconnect` event. **`onReconnect()`**: defensive double-cleanup — silent no-op in the normal flow where onDisconnect already ran, but if onDisconnect was missed (bug / race) it aborts any leaked entries + fires `reconnect_cleanup` with "stale in-flight RPCs from before the reconnect" so ops sees the recovery happened. **`inFlightCount()`** for /readyz probes. Zero state leaks across the connection boundary — registry starts empty on every reconnect. **8 tests** in `__tests__/inbound_rpc_recovery.test.ts`: onDisconnect aborts-all + counts + fires event with reason, empty-case no-op, omits reason when not supplied, onReconnect silent no-op on clean state, onReconnect defensive-cleanup on stale state with logged event, inFlightCount reflects registry size, full disconnect→reconnect cycle.)*

### 4g. Identity & DID

- [x] 4.51 Master seed load or BIP-39 generate *(done 2026-04-21 together with 4.52. `apps/home-node-lite/core-server/src/identity/master_seed.ts` exports `loadOrGenerateSeed(vaultDir)` returning `SeedSource`: `{kind:'generated', mnemonic, seed}` on first boot, `{kind:'loaded_convenience', seed}` on subsequent boots, or `{kind:'wrapped', wrappedPath}` when `<vaultDir>/wrapped_seed.bin` is present (handoff to task 4.53 for passphrase unwrap). Delegates to `@dina/core`'s `generateMnemonic` + `mnemonicToSeed` + `validateMnemonic` — the seed is a deterministic function of the mnemonic, and the generator self-checks its own output. `wrapped_seed.bin` takes precedence over a stray `keyfile` so an operator migration to wrapped-seed can't silently fall back to the less-secure convenience mode. First-boot: operator must see the mnemonic once — `bin.ts` wires this through as a `warn`-level log line so it stands out in the boot trace; install-script-wrapped UX can prompt the operator to write it down. `bootServer` now flips the `identity` step in the trace from `'pending'` to `'ok'` when convenience-mode succeeds, or `'pending'` with a wrapped-seed reason when `wrapped_seed.bin` is present (task 4.53 will wire the unwrap path). - [x] 4.52 Convenience: raw seed at `${vault_dir}/keyfile` mode 600 *(done 2026-04-21 together with 4.51. The keyfile persistence half of `master_seed.ts`. Written atomically via `<dir>/.keyfile.tmp-<pid>-<hrtime>` → fsync → rename — a crash mid-write leaves no half-written keyfile. Mode `0o600` is enforced both on creation (passed to `fs.writeFile` as `{mode}`) AND via an explicit `fs.chmod` follow-up (belt-and-suspenders: some mount options ignore creation-time mode hints). **Load-time mode check is strict**: a keyfile with loosened permissions (e.g. accidentally `chmod 644`) is REJECTED with an actionable error (`keyfile mode is 644, expected 600 — refusing to load (tighten with "chmod 600 <path>")`) rather than silently re-tightened, because the loose-mode window may have already exposed the seed to another user on the box. Length check is also strict (64 bytes exactly). **12 tests** in `__tests__/master_seed.test.ts`: first-boot generation (valid mnemonic + 64-byte seed + seed-from-mnemonic determinism), keyfile persistence + mode 600, vault dir auto-created, no tmp-file residue, round-trip generate→load, rejects loosened mode (`0644`) + world-readable (`0604`), rejects wrong length, wrapped_seed.bin placeholder takes precedence + beats a stray keyfile, empty vaultDir rejected at the API boundary.)*
- [x] 4.53 Security: `${vault_dir}/wrapped_seed.bin` (AES-256-GCM, passphrase) *(done 2026-04-21; `src/identity/wrapped_seed.ts` exports `writeWrappedSeed(vaultDir, seed, passphrase)` + `readWrappedSeed(vaultDir, passphrase)`. Delegates to `@dina/core`'s `wrapSeed` / `unwrapSeed` which handles the Argon2id KEK derivation + AES-256-GCM wrapping internally. **File format v1** is self-describing JSON: `{dina_wrapped_seed_version, salt_hex, wrapped_hex, params: {memory, iterations, parallelism}}`. JSON chosen over tight binary for two reasons: (a) the seed is small (<64 B) so size doesn't matter; (b) ops can eyeball the file to confirm it's a Dina wrapped seed + see the Argon2id cost parameters (useful for future re-wrapping under tightened costs). File written atomically (`.tmp-<pid>-<hrtime>` → rename) with mode `0o600`. **Security properties pinned**: wrong passphrase → generic "unwrap failed" error (doesn't leak GCM-tag failure details that could distinguish "tried to brute force" from "file corrupted"); corrupted ciphertext → same generic failure; fresh salt + nonce per write (same seed + same passphrase across calls produces different wrapped bytes); unknown file-format version → explicit rejection with version number in the error. **16 tests** in `__tests__/wrapped_seed.test.ts`: round-trip, mode 0600, JSON shape + field presence, vault dir auto-created, no .tmp residue, 4 security properties (wrong passphrase, corruption, different passphrases → different ciphertexts, fresh salt across calls); 3 file-format evolution tests (unknown version, malformed JSON, missing fields); 3 input validation tests (empty vaultDir / passphrase / read-passphrase). Jest timeout bumped to 30s because Argon2id with production `128 MiB / 3 iter / 4 lanes` costs ~1s per wrap — tests do ~10 wraps so the budget matters.)*
- [x] 4.54 SLIP-0010 derivation — signing, messaging, rotation, service keys *(done 2026-04-21 with 4.55. **Added `deriveServiceKey(seed, serviceIndex)` to `@dina/core`** at path `m/9999'/3'/{serviceIndex}'` + re-exported from `packages/core/src/crypto/index.ts`. This completes the purpose tree from ARCHITECTURE.md: `0`=root signing, `1`=per-persona messaging, `2`=secp256k1 PLC rotation, `3`=service auth. **Orchestrator** in `apps/home-node-lite/core-server/src/identity/derivations.ts` exports `deriveIdentity({masterSeed, generation?})` returning `IdentityDerivations`: `root`, `rotation`, `services: {core, brain}`, `derivePersona(idx, gen?)`, `derivePersonaVaultDEK(name, salt)`. Persona signing keys are derived **on demand** (not eagerly at boot) because personas are unlocked lazily per the gatekeeper tier model — the orchestrator returns a closure over the seed that callers invoke when a persona is touched. Canonical constants exposed: `SERVICE_INDEX = {core: 0, brain: 1}` (matches CLAUDE.md) and `PERSONA_INDEX = {consumer: 0, professional: 1, social: 2, health: 3, financial: 4, citizen: 5}` (matches ARCHITECTURE.md § "Key Derivation"). Both frozen. Security property: each persona gets a unique signing key — crossing compartments is impossible without the master seed. Service keys are path-invariant across generation rotation (purpose-3 has no generation segment; matches CLAUDE.md "install-time only, load-only at runtime"); root + rotation + persona keys DO vary with generation. **14 tests** in `__tests__/derivations.test.ts`: byte parity with @dina/core primitives (root + rotation + services + persona + DEK), determinism (same seed → same derivations, different seeds → different), security (unique per persona + unique per salt), generation rotation (root/rotation change, service stable), input validation (seed length, persona index, persona name), canonical constants frozen + correct.)*
- [x] 4.55 HKDF vault DEKs per persona *(done 2026-04-21 together with 4.54. `IdentityDerivations.derivePersonaVaultDEK(personaName, userSalt)` wraps `@dina/core.derivePersonaDEK(masterSeed, personaName, userSalt)` — per ARCHITECTURE.md the vault DEKs are **NOT** from the SLIP-0010 signing tree but from HKDF-SHA256 over the raw master seed with per-persona info string `dina:vault:<persona>:v1`. Output is a 32-byte SQLCipher passphrase; identical to `derivePersonaDEK` byte-for-byte so any Dina runtime writing a persona file produces a DB that any other can open. Security properties pinned by test: (a) each persona gets a unique DEK (cross-persona decryption impossible without crossing the HKDF boundary — enforced by the distinct `info` string); (b) different `userSalt` values → different DEK for the same persona (per-install isolation; `userSalt` is derived once at first boot from the seed and persisted alongside the personas). - [x] 4.57 DID document with `#dina_signing` + `#dina_messaging` (underscore form, matches recent fix) *(done 2026-04-21; `src/identity/home_node_did_document.ts` exports `buildHomeNodeDIDDocument({did, signingKey, messagingKey?, msgboxEndpoint?}, now?)` — pure function, no I/O, clock injectable for reproducibility. **Fragment ids** `#dina_signing` + `#dina_messaging` + `#dina_messaging_endpoint` exported as canonical constants (underscore form per AT Protocol convention + the "recent fix" called out in the task — `_` not `-`). **Default collapse**: when `messagingKey` is omitted OR byte-identical to `signingKey`, the doc emits a SINGLE Multikey VM (id `<did>#dina_signing`) and the `authentication` array references it under both fragment semantics. This is a valid W3C DID Core shape (two fragment ids can reference the same VM) and matches Dina's default "one keypair, two semantic labels" deployment shape. **Distinct-key path**: when caller passes an explicit different messagingKey, the doc emits TWO VMs (both Multikey, different `publicKeyMultibase`) + `authentication` lists both ids. **MsgBox service**: optional `msgboxEndpoint` adds a `DinaMsgBox` service entry at id `#dina_messaging_endpoint` — clients resolving the DID see where to send D2D messages. **W3C shape**: emits `@context: ['https://www.w3.org/ns/did/v1', 'https://w3id.org/security/multikey/v1']` matching Go Core byte-for-byte; VMs use `type: 'Multikey'` + `publicKeyMultibase`; `created` is RFC3339. **16 tests** in `__tests__/home_node_did_document.test.ts`: fragment id constants, signing VM id emission, messaging-aliases-signing default (1 VM, auth lists twice), distinct messaging key (2 VMs, auth lists both), degenerate explicit-identical-messaging collapses to 1 VM, MsgBox service add/omit/empty-string, W3C @context, Multikey + multibase shape, injectable clock + RFC3339 timestamp, DID id field, input validation (empty did, wrong-length pub key).)*
- [x] 4.58 Self-certify + sign DID doc *(done 2026-04-22; `src/identity/did_doc_proof.ts` exports `selfCertifyDIDDoc` + `verifyDIDDocProof` + `canonicalizeDIDDoc` + `PROOF_TYPE` / `PROOF_PURPOSE_ASSERTION` / `SIGNING_VM_FRAGMENT` constants. **Proof shape** follows W3C DID Core Data Integrity convention: `{type: "Ed25519Signature2020", created: <RFC3339>, verificationMethod: "<did>#dina_signing", proofPurpose: "assertionMethod", signatureHex: <128 hex>}`. **Canonicalization**: Ed25519 signature is over `SHA-256(canonicalJson(doc))` where canonicalJson is sorted-keys + no-whitespace + UTF-8 + undefined-skipped (simpler than full JCS but sufficient for Dina's single-runtime needs; key-shuffle invariance pinned by test). `canonicalizeDIDDoc` is exported so future JCS-based verifiers can reproduce the exact bytes. **Self-certification**: signing key IS the same key the doc publishes at `#dina_signing` — a resolver fetches the doc and verifies the signature against the embedded pubkey; no third-party registry needed. **Separation of doc + proof**: `{doc, proof}` returned as a pair rather than proof embedded inside — keeps canonicalization free of self-referential worry. Caller can stitch via `{...doc, proof}` at the edge. **`verifyDIDDocProof`** never throws; returns structured discriminator with 5 rejection reasons (`wrong_proof_type | wrong_purpose | vm_mismatch | malformed_signature | signature_invalid`). Early-exit ordering: `vm_mismatch` fires before `signature_invalid` because a mismatched VM signals the proof is for a different doc entirely (better debugging signal). **17 tests** in `__tests__/did_doc_proof.test.ts`: constants, happy-path sign→verify, signature determinism (Ed25519 RFC 8032), canonicalization (field-shuffle produces identical signature + `canonicalizeDIDDoc` direct pin), 6 verification failures (wrong proof type, wrong purpose, VM mismatch across different DIDs, 4 malformed-hex variants, wrong verifier pubkey, tampered-id triggers vm_mismatch, tampered-content triggers signature_invalid), 3 input validation (missing doc, non-DID id, wrong-length private key). - [x] 4.59 `plc_probe` startup drift check — `log.Fatal` on mismatch *(done 2026-04-22; `src/identity/plc_probe.ts` exports `plcProbe(input) → PlcProbeResult` + `plcProbeOrThrow(input)` + `PlcProbeError`. **Startup invariance check** — at boot the Home Node resolves its own DID from the PLC directory and compares the resolved signing key to the key we'd derive from the local master seed. If they don't match, ONE of: (a) master seed corrupted, (b) unauthorised PLC update, (c) directory returned wrong record (proxy rewrite / transient inconsistency). In all three cases we must NOT boot — continuing produces a Home Node that signs with a key the network considers invalid. `plcProbe` returns structured `{ok:true} | {ok:false, detail}` with 5 rejection reasons: `not_found | network_error | malformed_doc | missing_verification_method | key_mismatch`. `plcProbeOrThrow` is the `log.Fatalf` equivalent — wraps the failure result in a throw so boot.ts's crash-log path fires. **`resolveFn` injection**: production wires `@dina/core.resolveDIDPLC`; tests pass scripted resolvers. **Dual-shape doc parsing**: both PLC-flat-form (`verificationMethods: {name: "did:key:z..."}`) AND W3C-array-form (`verificationMethod: [{id, publicKeyMultibase}]`) — real PLC responses use flat today but future indexers may mirror to W3C. **Comparison via canonical multibase**: round-trips both sides through `publicKeyToMultibase` so error messages show `did:key:z...` on both sides (operator-facing form). **404 vs network distinguished** via regex on upstream cause — gives ops the right escalation path ("DID doesn't exist" is different from "directory unreachable"). **18 tests** in `__tests__/plc_probe.test.ts`: happy-path flat + W3C forms + VM override, 8 rejection paths (empty/non-DID input, bad key length, 404, network error, malformed response, missing VM, key mismatch with both did:keys in detail, malformed multibase), rejection-enum distinguishability, plcProbeOrThrow (resolves + throws PlcProbeError with attached detail).)*

Handles the common case of an operator dictating the phrase into a form that auto-capitalizes and auto-punctuates. **Rejection taxonomy**: `empty | wrong_word_count | invalid_checksum | unknown_word` — disambiguates `invalid_checksum` from `unknown_word` (BIP-39's `validateMnemonic` collapses both into `false`) by re-checking wordlist membership directly, so the UI can show "you missed a word" vs "there's a typo".
