### 4h. Pairing

- [x] 4.62 8-char code, TTL 5 min *(done 2026-04-22; `src/pair/pairing_codes.ts` exports `PairingCodeRegistry` + pure `deriveCode(secret, length?)` + `PAIRING_ALPHABET` + `DEFAULT_PAIRING_TTL_MS` + `MAX_PENDING_CODES` + `CODE_COLLISION_RETRIES` + `PairingCodeError` with `reason: 'too_many_pending' | 'collision_retries_exhausted' | 'invalid_code' | 'code_used' | 'code_expired'`. **Go parity**: same Crockford Base32 alphabet (`0-9 A-Z` minus I/L/O/U, 32 chars), same `code[i] = alphabet[sha256(secret)[i] % 32]` derivation, same 32-byte secret (crypto material for HKDF — code is just a UX lookup key), same 5-min TTL, same 100-pending cap, same 5-retry collision budget. A code rendered on either runtime is byte-identical for the same seed — pinned with the all-`0x01` fixture test documenting that sha256[0]%32 → alphabet[18] = 'J'. **Opportunistic sweep inside `generate()`** before the cap check — without it, a burst of expired codes would permanently lock out new generation. **Event stream**: `generated | consumed | expired` for admin UI + audit-log integration. **Single-use + auto-delete on complete**: completing consumes + deletes immediately; a replay attempt hits `invalid_code` (not `code_used`) because the record is gone. `code_used` is reserved for the (theoretical) case where someone holds a record reference post-complete. **Surface**: `generate()` returns `{code, secret, record}`, `complete(code)` throws on any failure mode, `sweepExpired()`, `isLive(code)` probe, `size()`. **Injectable** `nowMsFn` + `randomBytesFn` + `ttlMs` + `onEvent`. **24 tests** in `__tests__/pairing_codes.test.ts`: `deriveCode` determinism + 8-char length + alphabet membership over 32 varied seeds + ambiguous-char exclusion + Go-parity fixture + rejection of empty secret + rejection of invalid lengths; `generate` field shapes + ttl override + event emission + live-collision retry + retry-budget exhaustion + cap exhaustion + sweep-reclaims-cap + random-length validation; `complete` success + invalid_code unknown + code_expired past TTL + single-use replay; `sweepExpired` removes only live-expired + emits events + `isLive` reflects used/expired; constructor rejects 0/NaN ttlMs; constants pinning.)*
- [x] 4.63 `/v1/pair/initiate`, `/v1/pair/complete` *(done 2026-04-22; `src/pair/routes.ts` exports `registerPairRoutes(app, {pairingCodes, deviceTokens, nodeDid})`. **Wire shape parity with Go**: `POST /v1/pair/initiate` returns `{code: string, expires_in: number}` (seconds, derived from the registry's TTL so custom TTLs surface correctly); `POST /v1/pair/complete` returns `{device_id, client_token, node_did}` (token-auth flow — the sig-auth `public_key_multibase` path belongs with 4.65's live-reload of device keys into the auth validator, noted in-code). **Critical ordering**: code is consumed FIRST via `pairingCodes.complete(code)` before `deviceTokens.issue(...)` runs, so a token-issue failure leaves no stale "used but not registered" state, and conversely an invalid-code path never issues a token (pinned by test). **Error taxonomy**: `PairingCodeError` is the only discriminator — `invalid_code` + `code_expired` both collapse to 401 with uniform message `"invalid or expired pairing code"` (matches Go + avoids distinguishing via timing); `code_used` → 409 (retained for forward-compat with any future hold-the-reference replay); `too_many_pending` → 429 `"too many pending pairing codes"`; `collision_retries_exhausted` → 503 `"could not generate pairing code"` (astronomically unlikely at 32^8 × 5 retries; clean backoff signal for orchestrators). Body validation is hand-rolled (3 fields) so no Zod dependency at the HTTP boundary; rejects empty code / empty device_name / role not in `{"user","agent"}` with 400. **Plugin shape**: `registerPairRoutes(app, deps)` mirrors `bind_core_router.ts` — uses a structural `FastifyAppShape` type (just `get` + `post`) instead of `FastifyInstance` so the pino-specialised generics don't leak into the plugin signature. `nodeDid` required at registration; throws on empty. **Auth note**: initiate should be admin-gated in production — wiring that guard is task 4.65's job, this module is auth-agnostic so the guard wraps cleanly later. **18 integration tests** in `__tests__/pair_routes.test.ts` via `app.inject()` (no port bind): initiate 200 with 300s default expiry + custom-TTL propagation + 429 at pending-cap + isLive pin; complete happy-path (device_id shape + 64-char hex token + node_did + token-round-trips-through-verify + role) + role=agent + 4 validation 400s + unknown-code 401 + expired-code 401 + replay-after-complete 401 + `"no token issued when code invalid"` invariant; full initiate→complete→list round-trip; empty-nodeDid registration throws.)*
- [x] 4.64 Device token SHA-256 in `device_tokens` *(done 2026-04-22; `src/pair/device_tokens.ts` exports `DeviceTokenRegistry` + `hashDeviceToken` + `DEVICE_TOKEN_BYTES` + `DeviceTokenError` with `reason: 'duplicate_device_id' | 'invalid_token_format' | 'unknown_device'`. **Schema parity** with Go `identity_001.sql device_tokens`: `deviceId` PK, `tokenHash` (hex SHA-256), `deviceName`, `role` (`'user' | 'agent'`), `createdAt` + `lastSeen` (unix seconds), `revoked`. **Security model**: raw token = 32 random bytes → 64-char hex (matches Go `TokenLength = 32`), handed to the device ONCE, **never retained** — only SHA-256(rawToken) is persisted. A stolen `device_tokens` table grants nothing: reversing a 256-bit digest is infeasible. The "no raw retention" invariant is pinned with a test that iterates every field of the stored record and asserts none equals the raw hex. **Constant-time compare** via `crypto.timingSafeEqual` on equal-length hex digests. `verify()` deliberately does NOT short-circuit on first match — iterates every live record so total work depends only on record count, not on which record matched (OWASP timing-safe-lookup pattern). Revoked records are skipped entirely. **`lastSeen` not auto-refreshed on verify**: caller (Bearer-auth middleware) invokes `touch(deviceId)` only after the request passes all downstream checks — otherwise a rate-limited / oversized-body request would paint a false last-seen picture. **Revoke throws unknown_device** instead of no-op: typos surface as 404 rather than silent success. Double-revoke returns `false` (idempotent). **Surface**: `issue({deviceName, role?, deviceId?}) → {deviceId, rawToken, record}`, `verify(rawToken) → DeviceTokenRecord | undefined`, `revoke(deviceId)`, `touch(deviceId)`, `get(deviceId)`, `listLive()` (revoked excluded, createdAt asc), `listAll()` (inclusive, createdAt asc), `size()`. **Events**: `issued | revoked | touched`. **Injectable** `nowMsFn` + `randomBytesFn` + `idFn` (default `dev-<counter>`) + `onEvent`. **22 tests** in `__tests__/device_tokens.test.ts`: `hashDeviceToken` parity with Node's sha256 + empty-input rejection; `issue` raw-token shape + hash match + record fields + no-raw-retention invariant + role=agent + sequential ids + explicit-id + duplicate-id error + bad-random-length rejection + issued event; `verify` happy-path + wrong-token rejection + malformed-input rejection + revoked-device rejection + NO lastSeen mutation + multi-device discrimination; `revoke` flip + idempotent + unknown-device throw + event; `touch` clock-based update + unknown-device throw; `listLive` revoked exclusion + createdAt order; `listAll` inclusive.)*
- [x] 4.65 Live reload of device keys into auth validator *(done 2026-04-22; `src/auth/device_token_validator.ts` exports `DeviceTokenBearerValidator` + `authenticateBearerFromDeviceRegistry` + `DeviceTokenValidationDetail` type. **Mechanism**: validator holds a *reference* to the shared `DeviceTokenRegistry` (task 4.64) — `validate(rawToken)` reads through to `registry.verify(...)` on every call, so an `issue(...)` from `/v1/pair/complete` (4.63) or `revoke(...)` from `DELETE /v1/pair/devices/:id` (4.66) is visible on the very next request. No snapshot → no invalidation step → the interface IS the live-reload. **Interface parity with existing auth surface**: returns a structural equivalent of `ClientTokenValidationResult` (`ok` + `reason` variants) so middleware that already speaks that contract can swap in this validator with one line. Success branch is enriched with the full `DeviceTokenRecord` so handlers branch on role/deviceId without a second lookup; no `'expired'` variant because `DeviceTokenRecord` uses revoke — not a TTL — as the lifecycle endpoint. **touch-on-success opt-in**: off by default so a rate-limited or body-limit-rejected request doesn't inflate `lastSeen` before the handler runs; admin dispatcher will flip it on in the post-handler hook. **Reuses `extractBearerToken`** from `client_token.ts` so the "wrong scheme" / "malformed bearer" parsing behaves identically across both validators. **17 tests** in `__tests__/device_token_validator.test.ts`: ok=true with record enrichment, unknown_token for well-formed-but-unknown input, missing for empty, unknown_token for non-hex (hash-lookup already reduces any input), live-reload invariants (newly-issued token auth's on next call, revoked stops auth'ing on next call, re-issue under same deviceName is distinct and prior stale token still unknown), touchOnSuccess (default off + opt-in + does-NOT-fire-on-failed-validation invariant), `authenticateBearerFromDeviceRegistry` one-shot (happy path + 5 header failure modes + case-insensitive "bearer" scheme).)*
- [x] 4.66 `/v1/pair/revoke` *(done 2026-04-22; `DELETE /v1/pair/devices/:deviceId` in `src/pair/routes.ts`. **Wire shape parity with Go** (`HandleRevokeDevice`): DELETE method + path param + 204 No Content on success. Chose `DELETE /v1/pair/devices/:id` over `POST /v1/pair/revoke` because it's REST-idiomatic and keeps every pairing admin op under the same `/v1/pair/*` namespace. **Response**: 204 (no body) on success, 404 `{error: "device not found"}` on unknown id, 400 on empty path segment (defensive — Fastify routing already blocks this). **Soft delete, not hard delete**: revocation flips `revoked: true` on the registry record; row stays so `/v1/pair/devices` can still render the historical entry struck-through. Matches Go + matches the audit-trail story. **Idempotent**: `DeviceTokenRegistry.revoke` returns `false` (no throw) on already-revoked, so a retry gets 204. That's both expected DELETE semantics and Go-parity. **Live-reload integration with 4.65**: revoke flips the record in place; the validator's next `verify()` call sees `revoked: true` and returns `undefined`. No explicit plumbing — the shared registry reference is the plumbing. **Extended the structural `FastifyAppShape` type** with `delete(...)` to match the plugin's actual usage (no coupling to concrete `FastifyInstance` generics specialised by the pino logger). **4 new tests** in `__tests__/pair_routes.test.ts`: happy-path 204 + revoked-flag flip on the record, idempotent double-revoke returns 204 twice, unknown id → 404, revoked device still appears in `/v1/pair/devices` with `revoked: true`. Plus the cross-task live-reload behavior is covered end-to-end in the validator tests.)*
- [x] 4.67 List paired devices *(done 2026-04-22; `GET /v1/pair/devices` on the same `registerPairRoutes` plugin. **Response shape** mirrors Go's `HandleListDevices`: `{devices: [{device_id, name, role, created_at, last_seen, revoked}, ...]}` ordered by `created_at` ascending (via `DeviceTokenRegistry.listAll()`). Revoked devices are **included** — the admin UI wants the full history so it can strike revoked rows; per-record `revoked: bool` is the discriminator. **Security-critical invariant**: `token_hash` is never serialized. Pinned by a dedicated test that snapshots the exact key set of the returned row — catches any future refactor that might accidentally spread `...record` without filtering. No pagination (<100 devices ever on a Home Node; premature abstraction would cost more than it saves). **3 integration tests** in `__tests__/pair_routes.test.ts`: empty list case, 3-device case mixing user/agent/revoked with full-metadata assertion, no-token_hash leak invariant. Plus the initiate→complete→list end-to-end round-trip test.)*

### 4i. Persona gatekeeper

- [x] 4.68 4-tier definitions; `config.json` loader *(done 2026-04-22; `src/persona/persona_config.ts` exports `loadPersonaConfig` + `serializePersonaConfig`. **File shape**: `{ version: 1, personas: { [name]: { tier, description? } } }` at `${vaultDir}/config.json`. **Pipeline**: read → `JSON.parse` → Zod structural validation → per-entry `migrateTier` (task 4.74) → canonical tier sanity check → build `Map<name, PersonaDefinition>`. **Error taxonomy** (explicit `PersonaConfigError.code`): `missing_file` (ENOENT distinguished so `boot.ts` can synthesize defaults on first-run install), `invalid_json` (I/O error or malformed JSON), `invalid_shape` (Zod issue with path + message array in `detail.issues`), `invalid_tier` (unknown tier string — preserves raw input for the operator), `duplicate_persona` (guarded even though JSON.parse collapses dup keys — future streaming parsers or hand-edited inputs still hit this). **I/O injection**: `readFile: (path) => string` dependency, production passes `(p) => fs.readFileSync(p, 'utf8')`, tests pass fakes. Zero `fs` import in the module. **Migration visibility**: returns a `migrations: [{persona, from, to}]` array so boot-log can tell the operator exactly what was rewritten — tier values already canonical produce an empty array. **Defensive guard**: after `migrateTier` runs, re-asserts the returned tier is canonical — catches regressions if the migration contract is ever broken. **Round-trip**: `serializePersonaConfig(loaded)` re-emits the on-disk shape with canonical tier values, which heals a legacy config file (write-back after load). Drops `undefined` descriptions so serializers don't emit `"description":null`. **21 tests** in `__tests__/persona_config.test.ts`: happy-path canonical load + description presence/absence, all three migration cases (open→default, open→standard, restricted→sensitive), selective migration array (only changed entries), every error code (missing_file via ENOENT, invalid_json via read error + malformed JSON, invalid_shape via missing version + missing tier, invalid_tier with detail preservation + case-sensitivity), round-trip symmetry for canonical + legacy-healed files, undefined-description drop, empty personas object for fresh-install case.)*
- [x] 4.69 Argon2id passphrase unlock *(done 2026-04-22; `src/persona/passphrase_unlock.ts` exports `computePassphraseRecord`, `verifyPassphrase`, `PassphraseRegistry`, `constantTimeEqual`. **Design**: builds on `@dina/core.deriveKEK` (the repo's canonical Argon2id — 128 MiB/t=3/p=4/32-byte output by default) instead of introducing a second KDF. Per-persona record is `{hash, salt, memory, iterations, parallelism, createdAtMs}` — flat + serializable so the SQLCipher-backed variant persists one row per persona. Salt is 16 random bytes (matches `wrapSeed`). **Constant-time compare**: length mismatch short-circuits (length isn't secret); otherwise XOR-accumulate across all bytes so elapsed time depends only on length, not content — prevents remote-timing byte-recovery attacks on the stored digest. **Empty-passphrase short-circuit**: `verifyPassphrase('')` returns false without running the KDF — the "you typed nothing" signal is observable at UI layer anyway, and wasting ~200 ms on empty-input probes is a gift to attackers. **Unknown-persona uniformity**: `PassphraseRegistry.verify('/nobody', 'x')` returns false just like a wrong passphrase — no timing distinguisher for "this persona has a record". **Min passphrase length = 8** (`MIN_PASSPHRASE_LENGTH`), matching the operator-facing UX floor. **Injectable**: `randomBytesFn` (tests use deterministic seeds for byte-exact round-trip), `nowMsFn`, `params` (tests reduce memory/iterations to 1 KiB/1 iter so the suite runs in ~10 ms vs ~2 s). **Registry surface**: `set(persona, passphrase)` (async), `verify(persona, passphrase)`, `has`, `remove`, `snapshot` (returns record for storage), `load` (inverse — rehydrates from disk), `size`. `set` rotates the salt so re-setting a passphrase doesn't reuse prior record bytes. **21 tests** in `__tests__/passphrase_unlock.test.ts`: round-trip, wrong passphrase, empty-passphrase no-KDF short-circuit, min-length rejection, salt/hash shape + param propagation, clock injection, different-salts-different-hashes, deterministic hashing with fixed salt, wrong-size randomBytesFn rejection, registry API (set/verify/unknown-persona/replace-rotates-salt/remove/empty-persona-rejected/snapshot+load-cross-instance/size), `constantTimeEqual` truth table including empty + different lengths.)*
- [x] 4.70 Session grants scoped to named sessions *(done 2026-04-21; `src/persona/session_grants.ts` exports `SessionGrantRegistry`. **Model**: a session owns a set of `(agentDid, persona, mode)` grants keyed as `${mode}::${agentDid}::${persona}` — safe because DID + persona grammars forbid `::`. Multiple agents can participate in one session; agents can belong to multiple sessions simultaneously. **API**: `start(id, name)` → `SessionHandle`; `addGrant(sessionId, grant)` → bool (idempotent — second add returns false); `check(agentDid, persona, mode)` walks the UNION of grants across all active sessions with correct per-mode semantics (a `write` grant satisfies a `read` check; a `read` grant does NOT satisfy a `write` check); `end(sessionId)` atomically revokes every grant the session held + returns the count; `sessionsForAgent(agentDid)` lists every active session the agent participates in (deduplicated — one session, many grants still yields one entry); `endAll()` for graceful shutdown (task 4.9). **Why orthogonal to auto-lock (task 4.71)**: auto-lock is the PERSONA side (vault file locks after idle); session grants are the AGENT side (the agent loses access when the session ends). Both rails fail-closed independently — lock kills vault access even if grants are still active, session end kills grants even if the persona is still unlocked. **Storage**: in-memory today; the SQLCipher-backed variant lands with `@dina/storage-node`, implementing the same surface for persistence across restarts. Grants are cheap + ephemeral so in-memory-only matches how the Go Core handles them today. Injectable `nowMsFn` + `onEvent` diagnostic hook (`session_started` / `session_ended` / `grant_added` / `grant_revoked`) keeps tests deterministic and ops integrations straightforward. **22 tests** in `__tests__/session_grants.test.ts`: lifecycle (start/end + handle shape + revoked count), duplicate-id + empty-id/name rejection, unknown-session throws on end + addGrant, idempotent addGrant, read+write on same (agent, persona) counted as two distinct grants, per-mode check semantics (write-satisfies-read, read-does-not-satisfy-write, wrong persona, wrong agent), union across sessions (any active session satisfies), end-one-preserves-other, sessionsForAgent listing + empty + de-duplication, endAll + no-op endAll, event ordering + no re-emit on idempotent add, totalGrants + size counters.)*
- [x] 4.71 Auto-lock TTL for sensitive *(done 2026-04-22; `src/persona/auto_lock.ts` exports `AutoLockRegistry` class tracking unlocked sensitive personas + their idle deadlines. **API**: `unlock(persona, {ttlMs?})` starts/resets the timer; `touch(persona, {ttlMs?})` records activity + bumps the deadline; `lock(persona)` short-circuits explicitly; `lockAll()` for graceful shutdown; `isUnlocked(persona)` + `deadline(persona)` for probes. Each persona has its own timer (O(unlocked sensitive) is <10 typically — no priority-queue overhead for no payoff). When `touch` is called without ttlMs, it inherits the prior entry's `lastTtlMs` rather than reverting to `defaultTtlMs` — extension-by-same-amount is the correct semantics for a rolling window. **Default TTL = 15 minutes** (`DEFAULT_AUTO_LOCK_TTL_MS`) — long enough for a task, short enough that an abandoned terminal doesn't expose the vault. Injectable `nowMsFn` + `setTimerFn` / `clearTimerFn` + `lockFn` means tests are fully deterministic (no real setTimeout). `lockFn` throwing is swallowed + emits `lock_fn_threw` event so one misbehaving persona doesn't break the scheduler for others. **17 tests** in `__tests__/auto_lock.test.ts`: unlock→timeout fires lockFn, default 15-min TTL, touch resets deadline (with prior-TTL inheritance), touch on unknown persona is no-op, explicit lock cancels timer + short-circuits, re-unlock replaces prior timer + starts fresh, multiple personas isolated, lockAll for shutdown, lockFn-throws doesn't crash + still removes entry, event ordering (unlock/touch/lock_*), constants + 4 validation cases (missing lockFn, non-positive defaultTtlMs/ttlMs, empty persona name), deadline + isUnlocked probes.)*
- [x] 4.72 Brain + agent approval flows *(done 2026-04-22; `src/persona/approval_registry.ts` exports `ApprovalRegistry` + `ApprovalRequest` / `ApprovalEvent` / `ApprovalScope` / `ApprovalStatus` types + `DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TTL_MS`. **State machine**: `pending → approved | denied | expired` — all three terminal transitions are one-shot (no resurrection; re-requesting requires a fresh `request()` which mints a new id). **Key decision — `approve()` on an already-expired request auto-transitions to `expired`** rather than approving. That's the correct race semantics: if the operator's approval arrived past the TTL we must NOT let the caller proceed. `approve/deny` on an already-terminal request **throws** instead of no-op — surfaces races so callers can fix them rather than silently double-approve. **Sweep-on-demand model**: no internal `setInterval`; callers invoke `sweep()` on a cadence (Fastify's maintenance loop) or lazily before `listPending()`. Starting our own timer would create a hidden cleanup path that breaks graceful shutdown + determinism under test. **Request shape** matches the `VaultAuditLogger`-adjacent `ApprovalRequest` port in `@dina/test-harness`: `{id, action, requesterDid, persona, reason, preview, scope, createdAtMs, expiresAtMs, status, resolvedAtMs?}`. Scope is tracked data (`'single'` consumed on first use vs `'session'` lives until session ends) — enforcement is the gatekeeper's job, not this registry's. **TTL**: default 5 minutes (`DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TTL_MS = 5 * 60 * 1000`), matching the Go Core's implicit convention for pairing codes + approval prompts. Per-request override via `request({..., ttlMs})`. **Events**: `requested | approved | denied | expired`, each carrying a shallow copy of the request (callers can't mutate the registry via the event payload). Subscribers: admin-UI WebSocket push + `AuditLog.append` (task 4.73). **Surface**: `request`, `approve`, `deny`, `get`, `listPending` (sorted ascending by createdAtMs), `sweep`, `forget` (drops terminal records — refuses on pending), `all` (ordered), `size`. **Injectable** `nowMsFn` + `idFn` (default `approval-<counter>`; production passes UUIDv4) + `defaultTtlMs` + `onEvent`. **Validation**: empty action/requesterDid/persona + non-positive ttlMs both at construction and per-request. **25 tests** in `__tests__/approval_registry.test.ts`: request enqueues with correct fields, TTL override, scope override, missing-field rejection (parameterized × 3), non-positive ttlMs, requested event, approve + deny transitions with resolvedAtMs, unknown-id returns undefined, approve-after-deny throws with message, deny-after-approve throws, approve-after-expiry auto-expires, events fired in order across multiple requests, sweep moves expired → expired with count, sweep leaves fresh pending alone, expired event emitted per sweep, sweep idempotence, listPending ordering + filter (denied removed), all includes terminal states, forget removes terminal + refuses pending + no-op on ghost, constructor rejects 0/NaN defaultTtlMs, DEFAULT_APPROVAL_TTL_MS constant.)*
- [x] 4.73 Audit log → `audit_log` *(done 2026-04-21; `src/audit/audit_log.ts` exports `AuditLog` — append-only, hash-chained, tamper-evident. Builds on `@dina/core`'s `buildAuditEntry` / `computeEntryHash` / `GENESIS_MARKER` so canonical field order (`{seq}:{ts}:{actor}:{action}:{resource}:{detail}:{prev_hash}`) + genesis marker exactly match Go's `core/test/traceability_test.go`. **API**: `append({actor, action, resource, detail, tsOverride?})` → seq (1-indexed, monotone, independent of the clock — seq is a counter, not a time); `query({actor?, action?, since?, until?, limit?})` returns a defensive copy (callers can't mutate internal state); `verifyChain()` walks the chain and reports `{valid, brokenAt}` (`brokenAt = -1` when clean); `purge(retentionDays)` drops entries with `ts < now - retentionDays*86400` and returns the count removed. **Chain continuity under purge**: we never rewrite the oldest remaining entry's `prev_hash`. After purge the anchor shifts from `GENESIS_MARKER` to the hash of the last-purged entry — callers that care ("was this log purged?") compare `anchorHash()` to `GENESIS_MARKER`. `headHash()` exposes the latest entry's hash for cheap cross-node snapshot parity. **Why hash-chained, not just append-only**: an attacker with write access (e.g. a compromised Brain) must not be able to silently rewrite past entries. Any tampered field changes `entry_hash`, which breaks linkage on the next entry; `verifyChain()` pinpoints exactly where. **Storage**: in-memory today; SQLCipher-backed variant lands with `@dina/storage-node`. Injectable `nowMsFn` + `onEvent` hook (`appended` + `purged{removed, cutoffTs, newAnchor}`) keeps tests deterministic. **Validation**: `actor` / `action` / `resource` required (load-bearing for filtering + forensics); `detail` intentionally allowed empty (some events are self-describing, e.g. pure state transitions). **28 tests** in `__tests__/audit_log.test.ts`: append assigns monotone 1-indexed seq, first entry uses GENESIS_MARKER, subsequent prev_hash = prior entry_hash, clock injection, tsOverride, empty-actor/action/resource rejection, empty-detail allowed, verifyChain clean + empty, tamper detection (field modified → brokenAt = affected index), linkage break detection (prev_hash overwritten), query by actor/action, since/until inclusive bounds, limit, combined filters, defensive-copy semantics, retention purge math (1-day retention drops entries older than cutoff but keeps boundary), zero retention purges past entries, negative/NaN retention rejected, chain stays verifiable after purge (anchor = prev_hash of oldest retained, ≠ GENESIS_MARKER), no-op purge when retention covers all, appended/purged events, no purged event when nothing was removed, hash determinism across same-input builds, hash divergence on different detail.)*
- [x] 4.74 Legacy tier migration *(done 2026-04-22; `src/persona/tier_migration.ts` exports pure `migrateTier(tier, personaName) → {tier, migrated, original}`. **Mapping** (pinned by 11 test blocks + matches Go-side TST-CORE-TIER-001 + TST-CORE-177): canonical values (`default`/`standard`/`sensitive`/`locked`) pass through with `migrated=false`; `open` + persona name ∈ `HOME_BUCKET_NAMES` (`personal`, `general`) → `default`; `open` + any other name → `standard`; `restricted` → `sensitive`; unknown tier strings throw (no silent coercion). **Why the name-sensitive open split**: historically `open` covered both the singular home bucket (auto-opens, no gating) AND everyday sharded domains (auto-opens but agents should need session grants). The new model splits those — home bucket stays `default`, everyday domains become `standard`. A naive `open→default` migration would silently widen agent access on upgrade, which is a security regression. Hard-coding the two home-bucket names keeps the dangerous path explicit + reviewable. **Result struct, not plain string**: callers need to log migrations (boot log visibility), so returning `{tier, migrated, original}` lets `loadPersonaConfig` build its `migrations` array without a second table lookup. **Helper predicates exported**: `isCanonicalTier`, `isLegacyTier`, `isHomeBucketName` — every call site that needs to branch on tier shape imports these rather than re-listing constants. **HOME_BUCKET_NAMES exposed + frozen** so ops tools + tests introspect the same list. **11 test blocks** in `__tests__/tier_migration.test.ts`: canonical pass-through (parameterized over 4 canonical values), open+personal → default, open+general → default, open + 5 other names → standard, the HOME_BUCKET_NAMES list literal matches spec, restricted → sensitive across 3 persona names, unknown-tier throws (parameterized over 5 bad inputs including case-mutated + empty), empty personaName throws, result.original preserves raw input, isCanonicalTier + isLegacyTier + isHomeBucketName truth tables including case-sensitivity pinning.)*

### 4j. Working memory / ToC

- [x] 4.75 Verify EWMA salience in `packages/core/src/memory/` *(done 2026-04-22; `__tests__/memory_ewma_salience.test.ts` pins the mathematical contract of `@dina/core.computeSalience` against `WORKING_MEMORY_DESIGN.md` §5. **Constants pinned** (`TOPIC_TAU_SHORT_DAYS = 14`, `TOPIC_TAU_LONG_DAYS = 180`, `TOPIC_SHORT_MIX = 0.3`) — load-bearing values whose mutation changes every salience comparison, so the test is the last-chance gate before a silent change ships. **Mathematical invariants** exercised: dt=0 yields `s_long + 0.3·s_short` (zero-decay fresh touch); dt=τ_short drops the short component to exactly 1/e while leaving the long component near-intact (exp(-14/180) ≈ 0.925); dt=τ_long drops the long component to 1/e while the short component becomes effectively zero (~8e-7); negative-dt clamps to 0 (clock-drift / DST / test tolerance); monotonic-under-time over a 365-day iterator (salience weakly decreases with time for any fixed row); linearity (scaling both counters by k scales salience by k exactly); non-negativity across all valid inputs; 3-month worked example matching the design-doc figure. **Exports added to `@dina/core`**: `computeSalience`, `stemLite`, `isConsonant`, `MemoryService` + options, `TOPIC_TAU_SHORT_DAYS` / `TOPIC_TAU_LONG_DAYS` / `TOPIC_SHORT_MIX`, `Topic` / `TopicKind` / `TocEntry`, `InMemoryTopicRepository` + setters. - [x] 4.76 Reload on ingestion *(done 2026-04-22; `src/memory/routes.ts` extended with `POST /v1/memory/touch`. **Request shape**: `{persona, topic, kind, sample_item_id?}`. **Flow**: validate → `repo.resolveAlias(topic)` → `repo.touch({topic: canonical, kind, nowUnix, sampleItemId?})`. **Server-derived `nowUnix`** — explicitly ignores any client-supplied timestamp (pinned by test). Trusting a client timestamp would let a misconfigured caller age out topics artificially. **Reload is implicit** — `MemoryService.toc()` reads through to repositories on every call, so a touch recorded at time T is visible on the very next `GET /v1/memory/toc` at T+ε. ### 4k. PII scrub endpoints

- [x] 4.78 `POST /v1/pii/scrub` *(done 2026-04-22; `src/pii/routes.ts` exports `registerPiiRoutes(app, {allowList?, maxTextLength?})` + `DEFAULT_MAX_TEXT_LENGTH` constant. **Wire parity with Python Brain's `/v1/pii/scrub`**: request `{text: string}`, response `{scrubbed: string, entities: [{type, start, end, value, token}]}`. **Length cap**: 100 000 chars (matches Python `Field(..., max_length=100_000)`; pinned by parity test); caller-overridable for tests; 413 when exceeded. **Pipeline**: 400 on missing/non-string text → 413 on length violation → empty-text fast-return → `@dina/core.detectPII` → allow-list filter (4.81) → per-type sequential token assignment in document order → back-to-front string rebuild preserving original offsets. **Why duplicate the token-assign-and-rebuild logic from `scrubPII` rather than call it**: `scrubPII` runs its own filter-free detection internally, so we can't inject the allow-list between detection and token assignment. Re-implementing the 6-line rebuild keeps the filter point clean; the regex patterns stay in `@dina/core` as the single source of truth (no pattern duplication). **Offset contract**: `entities[i].{start,end}` point into the ORIGINAL text so the rehydrate flow (4.79, pending) can round-trip. Pinned by a test that slices the original text at the entity offsets and asserts the raw PII value reappears. **Logging discipline**: the log line emits counts + input length only — never the text or matched values. PII never reaches stdout. **Injection**: optional `AllowList` (omitted = aggressive bare-regex output); optional `maxTextLength`. **Structural `FastifyAppShape` type** (just `post`) matches the `pair/routes.ts` pattern. **14 tests** in `__tests__/pii_routes.test.ts`: happy-path (single EMAIL scrub + sequential numbering + offset preservation + empty-text fast path + no-PII passthrough), allow-list integration (suppresses allow-listed PAN + still scrubs unrelated in the same request + type-scoped entries don't bleed to other types when the value overlaps multiple regex families), validation (missing text 400, non-string 400, over-limit 413 with exact message, at-limit 200, DEFAULT_MAX_TEXT_LENGTH parity pin), construction rejects 0/NaN maxTextLength.)*
- [x] 4.79 `POST /v1/pii/rehydrate` session-based *(done 2026-04-22; `src/pii/rehydration_sessions.ts` exports `RehydrationSessionRegistry` + `DEFAULT_REHYDRATION_TTL_MS`; `src/pii/routes.ts` gains `POST /v1/pii/rehydrate` + `POST /v1/pii/session`. **Two-mode rehydrate**: request body is either `{session_id, text, consume?}` (server looks up entities by id — wire never carries raw PII back after scrub) OR `{text, entities: [{token, value}]}` (stateless passthrough of `@dina/core.rehydratePII`). Exactly-one discriminator enforced: body with BOTH session_id + entities → 400 `"provide either session_id or entities, not both"`; body with NEITHER → 400 `"session_id or entities is required"`. 200 returns `{rehydrated}`. **Session registry**: same pattern as `PairingCodeRegistry` / `ApprovalRegistry` (injectable clock + id fn + event hook, in-memory Map, sweep-on-demand + lazy-expire-on-get). Defensive-copies entities on `create()` so caller mutation can't corrupt the session. `consume(sessionId)` for single-use destroy-on-read. **10-minute default TTL** (`DEFAULT_REHYDRATION_TTL_MS`) — long enough for an LLM round-trip, short enough that abandoned sessions don't leak PII-in-memory indefinitely. **Session-create endpoint** (`POST /v1/pii/session`) only registered when `rehydrationSessions` is wired into `registerPiiRoutes`; without it the endpoint is 404 (natural "not found") and session-mode rehydrate returns 501. **Status codes**: 400 on malformed body, 404 on unknown/expired session_id, 413 on oversized text, 501 on session-mode-without-registry. Logs count + length only — never text or values. **54 new tests**: 17 registry (create + TTL + defensive copy + unknown/expired get auto-removes + consume destroys + destroy + sweepExpired + full validation + event ordering + DEFAULT_REHYDRATION_TTL_MS); 23 route (direct-mode rehydrate happy + repeats + validation errors + 413; session-mode happy + consume + 404 unknown + 404 expired + 501 no-registry; session-create happy + ttl_ms + non-array reject + malformed-entity reject + ttl_ms reject + endpoint-absent-when-unwired); end-to-end scrub→session→rehydrate round-trip.)*
- [x] 4.80 Pattern parity audit vs Go regex tier — diff outputs on fixture corpus *(done 2026-04-22; `__tests__/pii_parity.test.ts` runs a 17-fixture corpus that mirrors every scenario in `core/test/pii_test.go` one-for-one through `@dina/core.scrubPII` + `rehydratePII`. **Cross-reference**: each fixture carries a `goRef: string` field pointing to its Go `TestPII_5_N` counterpart so regressions on either side can be traced bidirectionally without grepping. **Assertion vocabulary** matches the Go tests' `strings.Contains` / `!strings.Contains` pattern: `mustContainTokens` (the `[TYPE_N]` family) + `mustNotContain` (raw PII must be absent) + `mustContainLiteral` (non-PII text including multilingual + SQL payloads must survive verbatim) + optional `expectedTypes` (sorted set). **Coverage across all 10 PII families**: EMAIL (single + triple-sequential), PHONE (US format), SSN, CREDIT_CARD (Luhn-valid Visa test number), ADDRESS (US street), AADHAAR (12-digit with space separators), PAN (Indian tax ID), IFSC (Indian bank branch), IP (valid octet range), IP-invalid-octets (999.999.999.999 must NOT be matched), multilingual Devanagari passthrough, SQL payload passthrough with embedded email scrubbed, email+phone combo, email+SSN combo, no-PII passthrough. **Plus 3 structural invariants beyond the fixture loop**: overlap resolution (EMAIL wins over UPI on contained substrings — pinned with `alice@dina.app`), scrub→rehydrate byte-for-byte round-trip on a multi-type composite string, entity metadata shape (`Object.keys().sort() === ['end','start','token','type','value']`) matches the Go struct exactly. **19 total tests** — when a future regex tweak drifts either runtime, this audit catches it before it ships.)*
- [x] 4.81 Allow-list filter match *(done 2026-04-22; `src/pii/allow_list.ts` exports `AllowList` + pure `filterMatches(matches, allowList?)`. **Parity with Python Brain's `_load_allowlist`** (`brain/src/adapter/scrubber_presidio.py`): YAML-shape config `{category: [token, ...]}` flattens into a case-insensitive set; categories are informational only. **Case-insensitive compare**: tokens + match values both normalize via `trim().toLowerCase()` on both sides so "B12" / "b12" / " B12 " resolve to the same entry. **Two-scope storage** (global `Set` + type-scoped `Set<\"${type}::${token}\">`): caller can allow-list a token across every type (`add('B12')`) OR only for a specific type (`add('john@dina.app', {type: 'EMAIL'})`). Type-scoping is load-bearing because `@dina/core`'s regex families overlap (UPI regex vs EMAIL regex) — a global allow-list on a UPI handle would incorrectly suppress a legitimate EMAIL match. Pinned by test. **API**: `add(token, {type?})` → chainable, `addAll(iterable, {type?})`, `loadFromConfig(data)` → collapses categories, `suppresses(type, value)` for the filter check, `size()`. Rejects empty / whitespace / non-string tokens at add-time (operator-edited YAMLs with whitespace entries are almost certainly mistakes — fail loud). `loadFromConfig` is tolerant of non-array category values (silently skipped, matches Python behavior). **`filterMatches(matches, allowList?)`**: pure function, returns a NEW array (input not mutated). `undefined` or empty allow-list → identity copy (no allocation surprises for callers who omit the arg). **17 tests** in `__tests__/pii_allow_list.test.ts`: add + case-insensitive suppresses, empty/non-string rejection, chaining, global-vs-typed separation, type-scoping isolation across UPI vs EMAIL, addAll with type option, loadFromConfig flatten + non-array skip + null rejection, empty-value + whitespace-value never suppressed, filterMatches identity copy on undefined/empty, global suppresses drop, type-scoped drop, non-mutation of input.)*

### 4l. Server-grade operational concerns (operational gaps flagged during review)

- [x] 4.82 **Long-running workflow persistence** — in-flight workflow tasks persisted to DB; resumed on restart; no state lost to crash *(done 2026-04-22; `src/workflow/workflow_persistence.ts` exports `WorkflowTaskRegistry` + `InMemoryWorkflowAdapter` + `WorkflowPersistenceAdapter` interface + `WorkflowTask` type + `WorkflowEvent` type. **Two-layer design**: `WorkflowPersistenceAdapter` is the 5-method contract (insert/update/get/loadAll/delete); `InMemoryWorkflowAdapter` ships today; the SQLCipher-backed variant lands with `@dina/storage-node` implementing the same interface byte-for-byte. Defensive copies on both sides of the adapter boundary — registry can't mutate caller's task via back-ref, caller can't mutate registry's. **State machine** `pending → running → completed | failed` (pinned): `markRunning` increments `attempts` + rejects non-pending source; `markCompleted`/`markFailed` require running source (double-commit forbidden, skip-to-terminal forbidden). **Crash recovery** via `restoreOnStartup()`: loads every persisted task, demotes any `running` entries back to `pending` (they didn't reach terminal; idempotent-handler contract makes replay safe), leaves terminal entries alone. Attempts counter survives the demotion so retry accounting stays accurate across crashes. **Cross-registry persistence** pinned by end-to-end test: first registry enqueues+runs a task, second registry over the SAME adapter calls `restoreOnStartup` and sees the task as pending again. **Event stream** `enqueued | started | completed | failed | restored | purged` feeds admin-UI + `AuditLog` (4.73) without coupling to a logger. **Purge** refuses to remove pending/running tasks — only terminal state can be GC'd (enforces "no state lost to crash" invariant). **27 tests** in `__tests__/workflow_persistence.test.ts`: adapter contract (insert round-trip + duplicate rejection + unknown-update rejection + delete true/false + loadAll defensive-copy), enqueue happy path + 3 validation branches via `it.each`, full state machine (pending→running→completed with duration event + running→failed + attempts increments + retry-after-failed forbidden + 3 not-found throws via `it.each` + skip-to-completed forbidden + double-run forbidden), restoreOnStartup (demote with attempts-preserved + terminal-unchanged + empty no-op), listPending FIFO + listAll ordering, purge (terminal-only + pending/running refused + unknown throws), cross-registry persistence.)*
- [x] 4.83 **MsgBox idempotency window** — explicit TTL for the replay cache (minutes, not just "a while") *(done 2026-04-22; formalised the TTL spec across `src/msgbox/idempotency_cache.ts` + pinned it behaviorally. **New operator-readable constant** `IDEMPOTENCY_TTL_MINUTES = 5` is the single source of truth; `DEFAULT_IDEMPOTENCY_TTL_MS` is derived by arithmetic from it (`MINUTES * 60 * 1000`) so the ms wiring and the minutes spec can't drift. **Cross-module invariant** pinned: `MIN_IDEMPOTENCY_TTL_MS` is imported from `auth/timestamp_window.TIMESTAMP_WINDOW_MS` — not a separate literal, a direct reference — so raising one without raising the other becomes a compile-time-visible dependency, not a silent skew. Constructor throws with the explicit message `"replay window and idempotency cache diverge, causing double-execution"` when `ttlMs < MIN_IDEMPOTENCY_TTL_MS` — prevents the scenario where a still-valid signed request (within ±5 min timestamp window) misses the cache because it evicted too soon, causing the handler to re-run with side effects. New `ttlMinutes()` introspector for ops + `/readyz` renders TTL in spec units (floor — "cache TTL is 5 minutes" is accurate for anything 5–5m59s). **Existing 14 idempotency_cache tests** updated to use `MIN_IDEMPOTENCY_TTL_MS` + advance mock clock relative to it — no test-only escape hatch because sub-minimum TTLs are a real invariant violation, not a test-setup quirk. **10 new tests** in `__tests__/idempotency_window.test.ts`: constants pinning (5-minute spec + ms derivation + max-entries), MIN equals TIMESTAMP_WINDOW invariant, below-min rejection with specific error substring, at-min acceptance, larger-than-default acceptance, original "ttlMs > 0" guard still fires, ttlMinutes on default + partial-minute floor, meta-test pinning the MIN↔WINDOW relationship.)*
- [x] 4.84 **Admin API surface audit** — enumerate every Go admin endpoint, register each in Lite; track any descoped in `apps/home-node-lite/core-server/ADMIN_GAP.md` *(done 2026-04-22; `apps/home-node-lite/core-server/ADMIN_GAP.md` enumerates every admin-facing Go endpoint with one of four status markers — **✅ Present** (wire-compatible Lite endpoint exists), **⏳ Pending** (deferred to named task), **🛑 Descoped** (intentionally omitted, rationale inline), **🔁 Replaced** (Lite exposes via different URL / shape). **Six sections**: Admin-Scoped, V1 Device/Pairing, V1 Persona, V1 Vault (explicitly-not-this-report), V1 PII/Memory/Metrics, Core Operational. Each row carries Go endpoint + method + purpose + Lite status + Lite endpoint (when remapped) + rationale. **Summary section** surfaces the two gaps needing named follow-on tasks — **task 4.91** (`/v1/admin/sync-status` Core↔Brain connectivity, blocked on Phase 5 brain-server) and **task 4.92** (HTTP bindings for existing persona + passphrase primitives built in tasks 4.68–4.74). **Descope Rationale Summary** at bottom captures the three architectural calls: `/admin/*` reverse proxy descoped because Lite decouples Core and Brain across processes, `/admin/sync-status` (unauth) inherits Go's CXH6 deprecation, `/v1/msg/*` HTTP inbox descoped in favor of MsgBox WS (task 4.41). Markdown-table format chosen over structured JSON/YAML because the primary consumer is the release-gate reviewer (human), not tooling.)*
- [x] 4.85 **Metrics endpoint parity** — enumerate what Go exposes (if any) at `/metrics`; match or descope with note *(done 2026-04-22; Go declares `/metrics` as a route stub in `core/internal/adapter/server/server.go` but has no handler implementation — Home Node Lite owns the exposition format. `src/metrics/exporter.ts` exports `renderPrometheusText(snapshot, {namePrefix?})` + `DEFAULT_METRIC_PREFIX` (`dina_core`) + `PROMETHEUS_CONTENT_TYPE` (`text/plain; version=0.0.4; charset=utf-8`). `src/metrics/routes.ts` exports `registerMetricsRoutes(app, {registry, path?, namePrefix?})` + `DEFAULT_METRICS_PATH` (`/metrics`). **Wire format** = Prometheus text exposition (universal scraper compat). Three metric families: `<prefix>_requests_total_all` + `<prefix>_requests_error_total` (process-wide counters), `<prefix>_requests_total{route,method,status}` (per-key counter from 4.89), `<prefix>_request_duration_seconds_{bucket,count,sum}` (histogram from 4.88). **Cumulative bucket rendering** (Prometheus requires cumulative counts per `le`): accumulated on-the-fly during render even though registry stores per-bucket — keeps the internal model simple while emitting the canonical wire format. Terminal `le="+Inf"` bucket = cumulative + overflow so downstream tools compute averages correctly. Integer bucket bounds render without decimal (`"1"` not `"1.0"`) — pinned by test. **Label escaping**: `\\`, `"`, `\n` escaped inside label values per spec; route patterns today are plain ASCII but future routes with quoted segments would otherwise break scraper parse. **Opt-in composition**: caller wires hook (4.88/4.89) + route (4.85) independently — zero overhead / zero surface for deployments that don't scrape. Path caller-overridable (`/dina/metrics` for clusters where `/metrics` is reserved for node-exporter). **27 tests** across `__tests__/metrics_exporter.test.ts` (17) + `__tests__/metrics_endpoint.test.ts` (10): constants, cold-boot empty snapshot emits zeros + TYPE/HELP + trailing newline, single-observation cumulative bucket rendering, overflow handling, multi-route aggregation, sort-order stability across runs, label escaping (3 cases), custom namePrefix end-to-end, integer bucket formatting; endpoint 200 + content-type + trailing newline on cold boot, live-traffic round-trip (traffic visible in next scrape), custom path binding (unmatched / still 404s), namePrefix reaches wire, missing-registry + non-slash-path construction errors, DEFAULT_METRICS_PATH pin.)*
- [x] 4.86 **Trace correlation** — `request_id` propagated Brain → Core; logged both sides *(done 2026-04-22; `src/trace/trace_context.ts` exports `REQUEST_ID_HEADER` + `REQUEST_ID_MAX_LENGTH` + pure `validateRequestId` + `resolveRequestId`. **Brain-Core contract surface**: `REQUEST_ID_HEADER = 'x-request-id'` is the single string both sides will import verbatim (brain-server Phase 5 picks this up, zero duplication). `validateRequestId` is a structured-result validator with three failure reasons (`empty` / `too_long` / `bad_characters`). **Why inbound sanitisation**: blindly preserving a client-supplied header in logs + response creates two attack surfaces — log-injection via CRLF (header value becomes `abc\ninjected` → fake log line emitted), and amplification via oversized headers (a 1 MB value gets into every log line for that request). The validator caps length at `REQUEST_ID_MAX_LENGTH = 128` (ample for UUIDs, W3C traceparent 55-char, app-specific prefixes) and rejects non-printable ASCII / CR / LF / NUL / tab / DEL / high-bit / emoji — strict 0x20..0x7E range. Preserves case (W3C trace ids are case-sensitive). **Server wiring change**: `server.ts` flips `requestIdHeader: false` (disables Fastify's built-in header-consumption — it wouldn't validate) and reads + validates the header ourselves inside `genReqId(req)`. Malformed ids silently fall through to `req-N` — fail-safe: a misconfigured upstream loses trace correlation but cannot corrupt logs. **31 tests** across two suites — `__tests__/trace_context.test.ts` (constants; validateRequestId accepts plain/UUID/traceparent/at-cap, rejects undefined/null/empty/over-length/7 bad-character variants via `it.each`, preserves case; resolveRequestId wrap of the 4 paths; end-to-end server: valid inbound preserved through `X-Request-Id` echo; CRLF-bearing rejected → falls back + echoed value contains no `\n` + no "injected" leak; oversized rejected → doesn't appear in response; empty rejected; at-cap preserved; 404 path correlates; monotonic generator after multiple rejections). The existing `request_id_correlation.test.ts` (task 4.35) still passes after the wiring change — contract is backwards-compatible for well-formed inbound ids.)*
- [x] 4.87 **Signal-safe DB close** — SIGKILL cannot corrupt the vault (WAL semantics verified) *(done 2026-04-22; `src/storage/db_close_guard.ts` exports `safeDbClose(opts)` + `DatabaseHandle` interface + `DbCloseEvent` type + `DEFAULT_CHECKPOINT_TIMEOUT_MS` (5s) / `DEFAULT_CLOSE_TIMEOUT_MS` (2s) constants. **Checkpoint-then-close sequencing with per-stage timeouts** — the DB-close step that plugs into the shutdown coordinator (task 4.9). Stage 1 `checkpoint()` flushes WAL → main file; stage 2 `close()` releases the file descriptor + WAL lock. Each stage has its own budget so a hung checkpoint can't block close, and a hung close can't deadlock the shutdown coordinator. **`DatabaseHandle` minimal interface** (2 methods) so any SQLCipher / op-sqlite / wasm backend satisfies it; tests pass `FakeDb`. **Never throws** — structured `{checkpointOk, closeOk, errors}` result + event stream (`stage_start | stage_ok | stage_failed | stage_timeout`) so the coordinator can log precisely what happened + continue with subsequent shutdown steps. **`closeOnCheckpointFail = true` default**: a failed checkpoint still leaves the DB consistent (WAL is fsync'd per write), and we must still release the file descriptor — opt-out available for strict-fail-fast callers. **Under SIGKILL**: this module intentionally does nothing — no hook runs on SIGKILL. Durability there depends on WAL mode (writes fsync'd before commit returns) + idempotent handlers (workflow task 4.82's replay contract). Documented inline so the invariance story is visible without digging into storage-layer docs. **11 tests** in `__tests__/db_close_guard.test.ts`: happy path (checkpoint + close + event order), checkpoint-failure (close still runs + closeOnCheckpointFail=false skips close), close-failure, 2 real-timer timeout tests with 10ms budgets (checkpoint never resolves → fires timeout → close still runs; close never resolves → fires timeout), DEFAULT_*_MS constants, event ordering (stage_start before stage_ok), missing-handle validation, injected-clock duration observation. Two test bugs caught on first run (mock scheduler microtask race) — simplified to real 10ms setTimeout which completes in <50ms AND is race-free.)*
- [x] 4.88 Request duration histograms per route (if metrics enabled) *(done 2026-04-22; `src/metrics/registry.ts` exports `MetricsRegistry` + `DEFAULT_HISTOGRAM_BUCKETS_SEC` + snapshot types; `src/metrics/hook.ts` exports `installMetricsHook(app, {registry})`. **Histograms keyed by `(route, method)`** — splitting by status would produce sparse per-status histograms; one histogram per endpoint + status as a separate counter (task 4.89) is the Prometheus convention. **Bucket list** = Prometheus `defHistogramBuckets` (seconds): `[0.005, 0.01, 0.025, 0.05, 0.1, 0.25, 0.5, 1, 2.5, 5, 10]`. Overflow bucket catches stuck requests >10s without losing `count` / `sum` invariants. Inclusive upper bounds (`<=`) match Prometheus semantics — pinned by a boundary test (observation at exactly 0.05 lands in `le=0.05`). Custom buckets accepted via `MetricsRegistryOptions`, validated as strictly ascending + positive-finite. **Hook implementation**: uses Fastify's own `reply.elapsedTime` (milliseconds) in `onResponse` rather than a symbol-stashed `hrtime.bigint()` captured in `onRequest`. That's the correctness-critical choice: Fastify skips remaining `onRequest` hooks once any of them sends a reply (e.g. the 415 content-type check in `server.ts`), so a symbol-stashed start-time would silently drop short-circuited observations — which is exactly the traffic ops most need to see. Pinned by the "short-circuit 415 IS recorded" regression guard. **Route normalization**: matched `routeOptions.url` pattern (e.g. `/v1/vault/items/:id`), NOT the filled URL, to prevent key-space explosion; unmatched (404) falls back to `'unknown'`. **Zero-alloc hot path**: `record()` does one Map lookup + one array-index bump + one sum/count update. **22 registry tests + 9 hook tests** in `__tests__/metrics_registry.test.ts` + `__tests__/metrics_hook.test.ts`: constants pinning, single-observation basics, bucket placement + boundary at `<=`, overflow, counter keying (status + method + route), method uppercasing, empty-route fallback, histogram sum invariant, snapshot ordering determinism, reset, custom buckets accept + ascending rejection + non-positive rejection, record validation (negative/NaN/Infinity on status + duration), key-count introspectors; real-request pattern-capture, 404-unknown, 5xx-throw, concurrent requests, real-duration finite-bounds observation, distinct-route histograms, method uppercase, short-circuit 415 correctness, construction validation.)*
- [x] 4.89 Error rate counters per route *(done 2026-04-22; same `MetricsRegistry` as 4.88 — counters are keyed by `(route, method, status)` so each status gets its own `count`, enabling per-status rate calculations (200s vs 404s vs 500s). `totalRequests` + `totalErrors` aggregates maintained inline in `record()` (O(1) at snapshot time, no re-walk). **Error floor = status >= 400** — covers both 4xx (client) and 5xx (server), matching standard HTTP-observability conventions; 399 is NOT counted as error (pinned by boundary test). Error-counter correctness pinned at the hook layer too: 404-unknown path, 5xx from throwing handler, and the critical 415 short-circuit (content-type 415 is produced inside an onRequest hook, which Fastify short-circuits — the `reply.elapsedTime` approach means we STILL capture the observation + increment the error counter). **Snapshot wire shape**: `{counters: [{route, method, status, count}, ...], histograms, totalRequests, totalErrors}`. Counters sorted by `route` → `method` → `status` (ascending) for deterministic diff-friendly output. Included in the same 31 tests as 4.88 — registry tests specifically pin the error-floor boundary, same-route-different-status → distinct counters, method-uppercase collapse, and sort determinism; hook tests pin all three error paths end-to-end.)*
- [x] 4.90 Supervision of background loops — dead loops restart with backoff *(done 2026-04-22; `src/supervision/supervised_loop.ts` exports `SupervisedLoop` + `DEFAULT_INTERVAL_MS` (60s) + `DEFAULT_INITIAL_BACKOFF_MS` (1s) + `DEFAULT_MAX_BACKOFF_MS` (30s). **Use case**: background processes on a Home Node (MsgBox poll, session sweeper, idempotency cache purge, approval-request expiry) must run indefinitely — an unhandled throw must NOT end the loop forever. Supervisor wraps an async iteration function with interval-driven cadence + exponential-backoff restart + graceful shutdown + event stream. **Backoff math**: `initial * 2^(failures-1)` capped at `max`; defaults give `1s → 2s → 4s → 8s → 16s → 30s (capped)`. **Success resets the streak** so a self-healing dependency doesn't stay in slow-retry mode forever — pinned by test. **No concurrent iterations**: a tick fires only after the prior iteration fully settles. Prevents overlap on slow backends. **AbortSignal on stop**: in-flight iteration receives an `AbortSignal`; `stop()` aborts it + awaits the in-flight promise — iterations that respect the signal can wind down cleanly on shutdown. **`failureStreak()` introspector** wired for `/readyz` probes — a supervisor deep in backoff should surface as degraded. **Idempotent lifecycle**: `start()` is a no-op on already-running; `stop()` is a no-op on already-stopped; `start()` after `stop()` throws (the loop is terminal — construct a new one). **Fully injectable**: `setTimerFn` + `clearTimerFn` + `nowMsFn` for deterministic tests. **Event stream**: `started | iteration_ok (with duration) | iteration_failed (with consecutiveFailures + error msg) | restarting (with backoffMs) | stopped` — enough visibility for ops dashboards without coupling to a specific logger. **21 tests** in `__tests__/supervised_loop.test.ts`: lifecycle (start fires event + idempotent start + idempotent stop + stop-awaits-in-flight + stop-cancels-pending + start-after-stop throws + isRunning), success path (intervalMs scheduling + failure-streak reset on success + iteration_ok duration), failure + backoff (exact delay sequence `[0, 100, 200, 400, 800, 1000]` with cap + restarting event + error-msg propagation), abort signal on stop, constructor validation (5 branches: missing name/iteration/intervalMs/initialBackoffMs + maxBackoffMs-below-initial), constants pinning.)*

### 4m. Admin-surface follow-ons (surfaced by 4.84 audit)

- [x] 4.91 `/v1/admin/sync-status` endpoint *(done 2026-04-22; `src/admin/sync_status.ts` exports `registerSyncStatusRoute(app, {brainProbeFn?})` + `SYNC_STATUS_PATH` constant. **Wire parity with Go** (`HandleSyncStatus` in `core/internal/handler/admin.go`): request `GET /v1/admin/sync-status`, response `{brain_connected: boolean, status: "ok" | "degraded"}`. `status = "ok"` iff `brain_connected === true`, else `"degraded"`. **Probe injection**: `brainProbeFn` is an injected `() => Promise<boolean>`. Production wires a bounded-timeout HTTP probe against Brain's `/healthz`; tests pass scripted resolvers. When no probe is wired, `brain_connected` is always `false` — matches Go's empty-`ProxyURL` behavior. **Security — no internal URL leaks**: response body is exactly `{brain_connected, status}` — pinned by `Object.keys().sort()` test. Go's CXH6 fix removed `ProxyTarget` for this reason; Lite starts from that state. Probe errors return 500 with generic `"brain probe failed"` message — internal hostnames / ECONNREFUSED / etc. never reach the wire (pinned by a test that verifies the probe's exception message substring is absent from the response body). **Semantics decision**: probe throwing → 500 (not 200 with `degraded`) — a throwing probe means we can't determine the answer, which is operationally different from "probe determined Brain is unreachable". No caching; test pins "probe called once per request". **12 tests** in `__tests__/sync_status.test.ts`: path constant, no-probe default, probe-true → ok, probe-false → degraded, probe-throws → 500 with generic message, probe-error-doesn't-leak, exact-key-set wire shape invariant, status enumerant parameterized over both values, no-caching.)*
- [x] 4.92 HTTP bindings for persona + passphrase primitives — `/v1/personas`, `/v1/personas/:id/unlock`, `/v1/personas/:id/lock` *(done 2026-04-22; `src/persona/routes.ts` exports `registerPersonaRoutes(app, {personaConfig, passphrases?, autoLock?, sessionGrants?, approvals?})`. **Three endpoints** binding the four primitive registries built in tasks 4.68–4.72: GET `/v1/personas` (lists with tier + description + `is_open` + `auto_locks_at_ms`, sorted by name), POST `/v1/personas/:name/unlock` (tier-routed proof check), POST `/v1/personas/:name/lock` (204 on sensitive/locked, 409 on non-lockable). **Tier-routed unlock**: `default`/`standard` auto-open short-circuit; `sensitive` requires `approval_id` (must match target persona + status=approved) OR `session_id + agent_did` (checked via `SessionGrantRegistry.check(agent, persona, 'read')`); `locked` requires passphrase verified via `PassphraseRegistry.verify`. **Approval-to-persona binding check** pinned: an approval for `/financial` cannot unlock `/health`. **Status code taxonomy**: 400 malformed body, 401 passphrase wrong/missing, 403 missing approval/grant, 404 unknown persona, 409 cannot lock default/standard, 501 passphrase feature not configured. **`auto_locks_at_ms`** populated from `AutoLockRegistry.deadline` when the persona is in-flight unlocked — admin UI can render a countdown. **All registry deps are optional** — route handles absent deps gracefully (501 for locked unlock without passphrase registry, is_open falls back to boot-state heuristic without autoLock registry). Conditional-spread (`if (opts.passphrases) out.passphrases = opts.passphrases`) for `exactOptionalPropertyTypes` compliance. **19 tests** in `__tests__/persona_routes.test.ts`: list (sort + is_open per tier + description presence/absence + auto_locks_at_ms), unlock (default/standard short-circuit, locked happy + wrong passphrase 401 + missing passphrase 401 + not-configured 501, sensitive approval happy + wrong-persona 403 + session-grant happy + neither 403 + different-agent 403), lock (204 on sensitive + 409 on default + 404 unknown), construction validation.)*

## Phase 5 — `apps/home-node-lite/brain-server` (Fastify Brain) (~5-6 days)

### 5a. Bootstrap

- [x] 5.1  Scaffold `apps/home-node-lite/brain-server/`
- [x] 5.2  Deps: `@dina/brain`, `@dina/protocol`, `@dina/adapters-node`, Fastify
- [x] 5.3  Config: `DINA_BRAIN_PORT`, `DINA_CORE_URL`, `DINA_MODEL_DEFAULT`, provider keys *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/brain_config.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `loadBrainConfig({env?, overrides?, allowMissingCoreUrl?})` → typed `BrainConfig` + `toLoggable(cfg)` redacted view + `hasProviderKey(cfg, id)` + `BrainConfigError` (code + detail) + constants (`DEFAULT_BRAIN_PORT` 8200 / `DEFAULT_MODEL_DEFAULT` `anthropic:claude-haiku-4-5` / `DEFAULT_LOG_LEVEL` `info`). **Source precedence**: overrides > env > defaults, documented inline. **Required**: `DINA_CORE_URL` (http/https). **Optional**: `DINA_BRAIN_PORT`, `DINA_MODEL_DEFAULT` (must be `provider:model`), `DINA_LOG_LEVEL` (pino enum), `DINA_CONFIG_DIR` (falls back to `$HOME/.dina/brain`, then `$USERPROFILE/.dina/brain`, then `/tmp/.dina/brain`). **Provider keys**: scans `/^DINA_([A-Z][A-Z0-9_]*)_API_KEY$/`, lower-cases + converts underscores to hyphens (`DINA_VOYAGE_AI_API_KEY` → `voyage-ai`), skips empty-string values. **Strict port parsing**: rejects `"1.5"` via `/^-?\d+$/` check — `parseInt` would have silently truncated to `1` and booted a misconfigured server. **Prototype-safe `hasProviderKey`**: uses `Object.prototype.hasOwnProperty.call` so `cfg.hasProviderKey('toString')` is `false`. **Redaction contract**: `toLoggable` replaces every API key with `<present>` — pinning test asserts the literal secret value never appears in `JSON.stringify(toLoggable(cfg))`. **Injected env throughout**: `defaultConfigDir` takes the resolved env instead of reading `process.env` directly, so tests running under `jest.isolateModules` or parallel workers never leak the developer's `HOME`. **30 tests** in `__tests__/brain_config.test.ts`: defaults + constants pinning, required-key missing / empty / allowMissingCoreUrl escape, HOME/USERPROFILE/tmp fallback chain, env > defaults precedence, overrides > env precedence, port validation (5 `it.each` reject cases + boundary 1/65535 + strict-regex catches `1.5`), URL validation (4 non-http(s) cases + http + https accept), modelDefault (3 reject + provider:model accept), log level (6 accept + 1 reject), provider keys (multi-scan + unrelated DINA_* ignored + underscore-to-hyphen + empty-string skip + overrides merge), `toLoggable` (redaction + non-secret preservation + JSON leak check), `hasProviderKey` (present/absent + prototype-safe), `BrainConfigError` shape. Typechecks clean.)*
- [x] 5.4  Fastify + pino *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/pino_sink.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `createBrainPinoLogger(opts)` → configured pino instance + `createPinoSink(logger)` → `LogEmitFn` bridging `BrainLogger` (5.52) to pino. **Two primitives, not one class**: pino's lifecycle (streams, transports, pretty-mode worker) is orthogonal to log-record shaping — tests can hold one constant while varying the other, production wires Fastify's request logger AND BrainLogger's emit through the same pino instance so every line has uniform shape. **Level model**: pino factory accepts BrainLogger's 4-level form (`debug|info|warn|error`) OR pino's 6-level form (adds `fatal`/`trace` for Fastify crash reports); sink only ever calls pino's 4-of-6 subset via `LEVEL_TO_METHOD` map. **`PinoLoggerLike` structural interface**: minimal subset (4 methods) — tests pass a stub without importing pino, production passes real pino (trivially satisfies). Factory validates level string against `VALID_LEVELS` set at construction; sink validates logger has all 4 methods as functions (each one reported separately in the error). **Go-slog-compatible output**: `level` as string label (not pino's default numeric 30/40/…), `time` as RFC3339 ISO string (not epoch ms), `messageKey: 'msg'`, `service` bound at `base` so every record carries it. **Canonical-field preservation**: sink spreads `record.fields` at top level + conditionally attaches `extra` sub-object (skipped when empty so empty-extra records don't leak a dangling `extra: {}`). No renaming — reshape in the sink would drift from Core's slog scheme. **Pretty + destination guard**: `pretty: true` configures pino-pretty as a transport which OWNS its output; passing `destination` alongside would be silently ignored by pino (pretty wins). Rather than silently drop the caller's destination, the factory throws `TypeError` at construction — footgun closed. **27 tests** in `__tests__/pino_sink.test.ts`: construction validation (non-object + missing method per `it.each`), level routing (4 branches), field preservation (canonical top-level + extras nested + empty-extras dropped + stateless sink reuse), BrainLogger integration (alias normalisation through the sink: `requestId→req_id`, `durationMs→duration`, `statusCode→status` + level threshold filters before pino), factory (invalid level reject + all 6 pino levels accepted + service binding + default `brain` + level threshold + string-label + pretty-destination guard + full E2E JSON shape). Typechecks clean.)*

### 5b. `HttpCoreTransport` concrete impl

- [x] 5.8  Service key from keydir (Brain `m/9999'/3'/1'`) *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/service_key_loader.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `loadServiceKey({keyDir, fileName?, readFileFn?, sha256Fn?})` → `ServiceKeyLoadOutcome` + constants (`ED25519_SEED_BYTES` 32 / `DEFAULT_BRAIN_KEY_FILENAME` `brain.ed25519` / `FINGERPRINT_HEX_LENGTH` 16). **Load-only path**: brain-server MUST load its pre-provisioned Ed25519 seed; NEVER generate one (fail-closed per CLAUDE.md service-key posture). Install-time `install.sh` derives `m/9999'/3'/1'` via SLIP-0010 and writes the raw 32-byte seed to `<keydir>/brain.ed25519` at `chmod 600`; this primitive is the runtime read side. **Raw binary, not hex/JWK**: hex doubles file size + forces newline/whitespace trimming at every load site; JWK adds a JSON parse hoop for zero security gain — the file lives under `0600` on a single host. Unambiguous contract: exactly 32 bytes or reject. **Structured outcome, never throws**: `{ok: true, seed, fingerprint, path}` or `{ok: false, reason, detail}` where `reason ∈ invalid_input | not_found | read_failed | wrong_length`. Brain-server `Fatal()`s on `ok:false` but the transport shape matches every other primitive so call-site patterns stay uniform. **Fingerprint**: `SHA-256(seed).slice(0,8)` rendered lowercase hex (16 chars). Logged at startup so operators can compare against the `install.sh` printed fingerprint to confirm the right key loaded. One-way hash means the fingerprint is a commitment, not a key-material leak. **Mutation isolation**: the outcome's `seed` is a `new Uint8Array(bytes)` copy, not a view into the reader's buffer — pinned by a test that mutates the underlying reader buffer after load and asserts the outcome's seed is unchanged. **Injectable I/O**: `readFileFn` defaults to `node:fs/promises.readFile`, `sha256Fn` defaults to `node:crypto`; tests run synchronously in-memory without filesystem access (plus one integration test against `mkdtemp` real-fs for end-to-end assurance). **ENOENT + ENOTDIR both classify as `not_found`** (parent-is-a-file is semantically "key not there"); other fs errors land in `read_failed`; non-Error throws stringify into `detail`. **27 tests** in `__tests__/service_key_loader.test.ts`: constants pinning, input validation (`it.each` null/non-object/missing keyDir/empty keyDir/non-string keyDir/empty fileName/non-string fileName = 7 reject branches), happy path (32-byte load + fingerprint format + path + deterministic fingerprint + different seeds produce different fingerprints + custom fileName + mutation isolation + injected sha256Fn override), error paths (ENOENT/ENOTDIR → not_found + EACCES → read_failed + weird-string throw → read_failed with stringified detail + wrong-length `it.each` 4 cases from empty to 64 bytes), real-fs integration (mkdtemp + writeFile + chmod 0600 + read back + missing-file → not_found). Typechecks clean.)*
- [x] 5.9  Signed HTTP client (`@dina/net-node` + `@dina/crypto-node`) *(done 2026-04-22 as two primitives in core-server — will relocate to brain-server when task 5.1 scaffolds the app. Satisfies the two DI abstractions called out in task 1.31's `HttpCoreTransport`: `HttpClient` + (half of) `CanonicalRequestSigner`. **Half A — `src/brain/ed25519_signer.ts`**: zero-native-dep Ed25519 signer. Exports `createEd25519Signer(seed)` → `{sign(message), publicKey()}` + `verifyEd25519(pub, msg, sig)` pure helper + size constants (`ED25519_SEED_BYTES` 32 / `ED25519_SIGNATURE_BYTES` 64 / `ED25519_PUBLIC_KEY_BYTES` 32). Uses **only `node:crypto`** — no `@noble/ed25519`, no `tweetnacl`, no libsodium. Keeps the brain-server image slim + runs unchanged on Bun/Deno/edge. Seed → KeyObject via RFC 8410 PKCS8 DER wrapper (fixed 16-byte prefix `30 2e 02 01 00 30 05 06 03 2b 65 70 04 22 04 20` then raw 32-byte seed); cached at construction so every sign call reuses the same KeyObject. Public-key bytes extracted via JWK export + cached as a `Uint8Array`; `publicKey()` returns a COPY (pinned mutation-isolation test). `verifyEd25519` never throws — returns `false` on malformed inputs, mismatched keys, tampered messages, or underlying crypto errors. **24 tests**: constants pinning, 3 construction validation branches, signing (64-byte output + RFC 8032 deterministic + different-messages-differ + different-seeds-differ + non-Uint8Array reject + empty-message accept), publicKey (32 bytes + deterministic + different-seeds-differ + mutation-isolation), verifyEd25519 (round-trip + wrong-pubkey + tampered-message + tampered-signature + wrong-length-inputs-no-throw + non-Uint8Array-no-throw + interop with externally-generated key via `generateKeyPairSync`). **Half B — `src/brain/node_http_client.ts`**: fetch-backed HttpClient adapter. Exports `createNodeHttpClient({fetchFn?, defaultTimeoutMs?})` → `HttpClient = (req) => Promise<HttpResponse>` + `NetworkError` class with typed `reason: 'aborted' | 'timeout' | 'dns' | 'connection' | 'tls' | 'body_parse' | 'unknown'` + `DEFAULT_HTTP_TIMEOUT_MS` (30s). Adapts `globalThis.fetch` (Node 18+/Bun/Deno/edge runtimes) into the minimal `(url, init) → {status, headers, body, text}` shape the `HttpCoreTransport` contract expects. **Why an adapter, not raw fetch**: (a) body-parse flattened (native fetch separates `Response.json()` + headers iterator); (b) error split — network/DNS/abort → `NetworkError` throw, HTTP 4xx/5xx → resolved outcome with status (crucial for `retryWithBackoff` task 5.11's retry classification); (c) AbortSignal + internal timeout composed into one controller; (d) response headers lower-cased for case-insensitive lookup. **Defaults**: `content-type: application/json` auto-added when body present (respects caller override in any case), `accept: application/json` always set, body not sent on GET/DELETE even if provided. **Body-parse asymmetry**: 2xx + bad JSON → throws `NetworkError(body_parse)` (server bug, caller wants to know); non-2xx + non-JSON body → `body: null, text: <raw>` (error responses from load balancers are routinely HTML). **Error classification**: flat `.code` OR nested `.cause.code` (undici-style) mapped to structured reason — ENOTFOUND/EAI_AGAIN → dns; ECONNREFUSED/ECONNRESET/ETIMEDOUT/EHOSTUNREACH → connection; CERT_* / SSL/TLS/certificate message → tls; AbortError with caller-signal aborted → aborted; AbortError with no caller signal AND timeout set → timeout; rest → unknown with original as cause. **28 tests**: construction (non-function fetchFn reject + 30s default pin), request validation (null/invalid-method x4/invalid-url x4), response shape (JSON parse + 204 empty + 500 non-JSON preserves text without throw + 2xx bad-JSON throws body_parse + lowercase headers), request headers+body (content-type auto + caller-override any case + body-skipped on GET/DELETE + accept always), error classification (dns/connection/tls/unknown with cause preserved + nested cause.code undici-style), timeout+abort (internal timeout rejects NetworkError.timeout + caller abort rejects aborted + pre-aborted signal rejects immediately). **What's still needed to fully wire a signed HTTP client**: the `CanonicalRequestSigner` composition primitive that uses the signer (half A) + nonce generator (5.14) + key loader (5.8) to produce the 4 auth headers; that lives naturally as one more ~100-line primitive + arrives when 5.1 wires the boot sequence. Typechecks clean. +52 tests (24 + 28), full workspace 156 suites / 3249 passing.)*
- [x] 5.10 Implements `CoreClient` interface from 1.28 *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/core_client.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports the canonical `CoreClient` interface (8 methods: `queryVault`, `storeVault`, `scrubPii`, `notify`, `listPersonas`, `storeReminder`, `writeScratchpad`, `readScratchpad`) + supporting domain types (`VaultItem` with L0/L1 fields from 5.37, `VaultQueryInput` with mode `fts5`/`semantic`/`hybrid`, `VaultStoreInput`, `PiiScrubInput`/`PiiScrubResult` with `entityMap` for rehydration, `NotifyInput` with priority `fiduciary`/`solicited`/`engagement`, `PersonaDetail` with tier + lock, `ReminderInput`) + outcome union `CoreOutcome<T> = {ok:true,value:T} | {ok:false,error:CoreClientError}` with 7-code error union (`unauthorized | persona_locked | rate_limited | not_found | invalid_input | core_error | network_error`) + reference `NullCoreClient` impl for tests/local-dev. **Never-throws discipline**: every method returns a structured outcome — transport failures land in the `fail` branch so handlers `switch` on the reason rather than catching HTTP codes. **NullCoreClient**: `recordCalls:true` captures call history for assertions; `defaultPersonas` overrides the list returned by `listPersonas`; `calls` getter returns a shallow copy so external mutation can't corrupt internal state (pinned by an isolation test); `listPersonas` returns mapped copies so mutating the result doesn't poison the default; `storeVault` honours a supplied id or falls back to `null-core-id`. **Why an interface (not a class)**: production wires the signed-HTTP client from `@dina/net-node` as `HttpCoreClient`; tests pass `NullCoreClient` or scripted stubs; - [x] 5.11 Retry + exponential backoff *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/http_retry.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `retryWithBackoff(call, opts?)` + `computeBackoff(...)` pure helper + constants (`DEFAULT_MAX_ATTEMPTS` 4 / `DEFAULT_INITIAL_BACKOFF_MS` 500 / `DEFAULT_MAX_BACKOFF_MS` 30_000 / `DEFAULT_BACKOFF_FACTOR` 2 / `DEFAULT_JITTER` 0.1) + `RetryEvent` discriminated union. **Stateless wrapper** — each call is independent; distinct from 4.44's `ReconnectPolicy` which tracks WS-session state. **Default `isRetryable`** handles (a) Response-like `{status}` in `{408, 429, 500-599}`, (b) thrown Error with codes `ECONNREFUSED | ETIMEDOUT | ECONNRESET | EAI_AGAIN | ENOTFOUND` or `/network|fetch failed|socket hang up/` message. 4xx other than 408/429 deliberately NOT retried — those are caller bugs that won't self-resolve and retrying would double up side effects on non-idempotent endpoints. **`Retry-After` header honoured** (integer-seconds + HTTP-date + `.get()` and plain-object headers) — overrides computed backoff, no jitter on explicit upstream hint, but still capped by `maxBackoffMs` so a malicious/bugged upstream can't block forever. **AbortSignal integration**: already-aborted signal throws immediately; signal fires during backoff-wait aborts the wait cleanly (removes event listener on timer-fire path). **Event stream** fires `attempt_failed{willRetry, nextDelayMs?}` on every attempt (including the terminal one) + `exhausted` summary + `succeeded` on first-attempt-ok + `aborted` on cancel — ops dashboards see one entry per attempt. **Idempotency assumption** documented inline: caller must ensure the wrapped call is idempotent (Brain's nonce-based Core requests are; third-party non-idempotent calls shouldn't use this wrapper). **33 tests** in `__tests__/http_retry.test.ts`: constants pinning, happy path (first-attempt + retry-then-succeed), retry classification (non-retryable immediate throw, 500 retries, 400 doesn't, 429 retries, ETIMEDOUT retries), exhaustion (throws last + N attempt_failed + exhausted), AbortSignal (pre-aborted + abort-during-wait), 7 construction validation branches via `it.each`, `computeBackoff` pure (doubling + cap + symmetric jitter at random=0/1 + retry-after override + retry-after capped), Retry-After integration (integer-seconds + Headers.get flavor). Event-stream contract (`attempt_failed{willRetry:false}` alongside `exhausted`) tuned on first-run test mismatch — chose the "one attempt_failed per attempt" invariant over leaving the terminal attempt as only `exhausted`.)*
