- [x] 5.14 Nonce generation per request (16 random bytes, hex) *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/nonce_generator.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `createNonceGenerator(opts?)` → closure emitting 32-char lowercase hex per call, `generateNonce()` one-shot, `isValidNonceFormat(candidate)` validator, `NONCE_BYTES` (16) + `NONCE_HEX_LENGTH` (32) constants. **128 bits of entropy** → birthday-collision probability <1/10^12 even at millions of nonces/s across years of Brain lifetime. **No monotonic component** — a pure random nonce doesn't leak request ordering to a passive traffic observer the way a counter-based nonce would. **Injectable `randomBytesFn`** for deterministic tests; production uses `node:crypto.randomBytes`. **Stateless closure** — no shared state means no race under concurrent calls (pinned by 1000-call uniqueness test). **Brain-Core contract**: the matching server-side validator is `src/auth/nonce_guard.ts`; both sides need to agree on length + lowercase-hex character set (pinned by the `isValidNonceFormat` rejection of uppercase). **15 tests** in `__tests__/nonce_generator.test.ts`: constants pinning, generator (32-char hex format + uniqueness over 100 calls + injected-random determinism + wrong-length rejection + concurrent-collision-free over 1000 calls), `generateNonce` one-shot + call independence, `isValidNonceFormat` positive + 9 negative cases via `it.each` (too short / too long / uppercase / non-hex / mixed / empty / number / undefined / null).)*

Exports `AskRegistry` + `InMemoryAskAdapter` + `AskPersistenceAdapter` interface + `AskRecord` / `AskEvent` / `AskStatus` types + `DEFAULT_ASK_TTL_MS` (60s: 3s fast-path + 57s poll window). **5-status state machine**: `in_flight | complete | failed | expired | pending_approval` with explicit allowed transitions — `in_flight → complete | failed | pending_approval | expired (via sweep)`; `pending_approval → in_flight (resumeAfterApproval) | failed (operator denied) | expired (via sweep)`; every other transition throws. **Two distinct failure paths**: `markFailed` accepts both `in_flight` (LLM / network error) AND `pending_approval` (operator denied) sources — both collapse to the same public `failed` status with a different `errorJson` payload. **`resumeAfterApproval` clears `approvalId`** via `delete` — the approval is consumed, not retained. **TTL reaper** (`sweepExpired()`) transitions BOTH `in_flight` and `pending_approval` past deadline → `expired`; idempotent; caller drives the cadence (production: `SupervisedLoop` from 4.90). pending_approval-expires matters because an operator who never acts on an approval would otherwise leak asks forever. **Event stream** (`enqueued | completed with duration | failed | expired with fromStatus | pending_approval with approvalId | approval_resumed | purged | restored_expired`) for admin-UI + `AuditLog` (4.73) integration. **28 tests** in `__tests__/ask_registry.test.ts`: enqueue happy path + event + 5 validation branches via `it.each`, state machine happy-path (4 transitions including full approval cycle with event order), state-machine forbidden (6 transitions that throw + 4-method not-found via `it.each`), TTL reaper (in_flight → expired, pending_approval → expired, idempotence, terminal-alone), purge (terminal-only + non-terminal refused + unknown throws), listAll ordering, construction validation, constants pin. Deliberately shares the adapter pattern with `WorkflowPersistenceAdapter` (4.82) but keeps separate state machines — asks have richer 5-state shape; workflows have 4-state; sharing a single model would produce a Frankenstein.)*
- [x] 5.20 **Ask-registry persistence across restart** — in-flight asks resumable, not lost on crash *(done 2026-04-22 alongside 5.19 in `src/brain/ask_registry.ts`. **Adapter pattern** matches `WorkflowPersistenceAdapter` byte-for-byte (5 methods: insert/update/get/loadAll/delete); `InMemoryAskAdapter` ships today; SQLCipher variant lands with `@dina/storage-node`. **Per-status restore semantics** (`restoreOnStartup()`) — distinct from workflow's blanket demote pattern because ask states have different recovery intent: (a) `in_flight` past deadline → `expired` (TTL elapsed during downtime; caller polling would see timeout anyway), (b) `in_flight` still within budget → preserved as-is (Brain's outer loop resumes the answer computation), (c) `pending_approval` → preserved regardless of deadline (operator decisions survive crashes; the decision itself is not runtime state), (d) terminal → untouched. Returns `AskRestoreSummary = {loaded, expiredOnRestore, stillInFlight, stillPendingApproval, terminal}` — boot log renders a breakdown like "loaded 4; 1 expired on restore; 1 still in-flight; 1 awaiting approval; 1 terminal". **Cross-registry persistence** end-to-end pinned: first registry enqueues an ask; second registry over the SAME adapter calls `restoreOnStartup` and sees the ask as in_flight still (simulates crash + restart in one test). **Defensive copy on both sides of the adapter boundary** so caller mutation of a returned record can't corrupt storage, and vice versa. **11 dedicated persistence tests** within the same `__tests__/ask_registry.test.ts` file: adapter contract (insert round-trip with defensive copy, duplicate rejection, unknown-update throws, loadAll defensive copy), 4-state restore fixture covering every branch + summary counts, empty-adapter zero counts, cross-registry persistence. **Note on layering**: the file lives in core-server pending Phase 5.1 brain-server scaffold — all dependencies are pure TS + in-memory + `@dina/protocol`, so relocation is a `git mv` with no code changes.)*
- [x] 5.21 Cancel handler aborts LLM call *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/llm_cancel_registry.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `LlmCancelRegistry` + `LlmCancelRegistration` + `LlmCancelEvent` type. **Mechanism**: `register(requestId)` returns `{signal, unregister}` — adapter hands `signal` to the LLM SDK (fetch `{signal}`, provider abort hook); handler calls `unregister()` in its `finally` block. `cancel(requestId)` aborts the signal → in-flight fetch/SDK call rejects → handler's catch fires → ask transitions to `failed` via `AskRegistry` (5.19). **Critical invariants** pinned by tests: (1) duplicate `register()` aborts the PRIOR controller before replacing — a duplicate request_id is a protocol bug (ask registry should have caught it), shutting down the prior prevents a zombie-LLM-call; (2) `unregister()` uses object-identity check (NOT id equality) so if a later `register()` has replaced our controller, our own `finally`-block `unregister()` is a no-op — prevents wiping a fresh registration; (3) `cancel()` leaves the entry in place (handler's `finally` removes it) — avoids a race where a fresh `register()` between abort and removal would see an empty slot. **`abortAll()` for graceful shutdown** (task 4.9 integration) cancels every pending call + clears registry; post-abortAll stale `unregister` callbacks are no-ops via the identity check. **Emits per-cancel events + abort_all summary** so ops tools can consume either shape. **Relation to `CancelRegistry`** (task 4.48): that one keys by `(senderDid, requestId)` for inbound MsgBox RPC cancellation; this one keys by single `requestId` because Brain only ever has one local sender (itself). Same primitive, different scope. **24 tests** in `__tests__/llm_cancel_registry.test.ts`: register + unregister lifecycle + empty-id reject, duplicate-register aborts-prior-and-replaces, events, cancel (aborts signal + not_found + leaves-entry-in-place + events), unregister (removes + idempotent + identity-check refuses replacement + events + post-cancel cleanup), abortAll (aborts every + clears + events + empty case + post-abortAll-unregister no-op), integration (AbortSignal event flow into a pending Promise + signal.reason populated + native AbortSignal methods), has/size introspectors.)*
- [x] 5.21-A **Pattern A loop primitives — agentic-loop suspend/resume + ApprovalRequiredError** *(done 2026-04-26 in `packages/brain/src/reasoning/{tool_registry,agentic_loop}.ts`. Closes the "no auto re-issuer on approval_resumed" gap referenced from 5.19's docstring by giving the agentic loop a way to bail mid-turn and resume at the same iteration after the operator approves the gated read. **`tool_registry.ts`**: third variant added to `ToolExecutionOutcome` — `{success: false; code: 'approval_required'; approvalId; persona; error}` — and a new `ApprovalRequiredError` class. The registry's existing try/catch translates a thrown `ApprovalRequiredError` into the new outcome shape; regular `Error` still classifies as `execution_failed` (regression-pinned). **`agentic_loop.ts`**: introduces `PausedAgenticState` (versioned at `1`, carries transcript + iteration + toolCallCount + pendingToolCall + remainingToolCalls + approvalId + persona + usage). `runAgenticTurn` factored to call a private `runLoopBody`; new exported `resumeAgenticTurn(pausedState)` re-executes the bailing tool (now with consumed approval), drains untouched siblings, then re-enters `runLoopBody` at iteration+1. `AgenticFinishReason` gains `'approval_required'`; `AgenticLoopResult.pausedState?` is populated only on that finish reason. The transcript at the bail point includes already-completed sibling results but NOT the bailing tool's result — the resume path pushes that one. Loop bails on the FIRST approval-required outcome in a batch (multi-persona asks discover later approvals on resume); paused-state version mismatch on resume throws structured. **9 new tests** in `__tests__/reasoning/agentic_loop_suspend_resume.test.ts`: bail captures full state, sibling capture, toolLog records approval_required, full bail→resume→answer cycle, sibling drain, refuses future versions, re-bails with different approvalId, preserves token usage, respects AbortSignal. **3 new tests** in `__tests__/reasoning/tool_registry.test.ts`: ApprovalRequiredError translation, class identity, regular Error still → execution_failed.)*
- [x] 5.21-B **AskRecord `pausedStateJson` field — registry stores Pattern A bail blob** *(done 2026-04-26 in `packages/brain/src/ask/ask_registry.ts`. **`AskRecord` extension**: optional `pausedStateJson?: string` field carries the `JSON.stringify(PausedAgenticState)` payload from 5.21-A. **`markPendingApproval(id, approvalId, pausedStateJson?)`** gains an optional 3rd param — set when the loop bailed via Pattern A, omit when the legacy persona-guarded HTTP path returned a Pattern B `{kind: 'approval'}` outcome. **Lifecycle invariants** pinned: `markComplete` / `markFailed` / `sweepExpired` / `restoreOnStartup` all `delete record.pausedStateJson` (terminal — paused state no longer relevant); `resumeAfterApproval` PRESERVES `pausedStateJson` (the resumer needs to read it on the way out); a re-call of `markPendingApproval` WITHOUT a payload clears any stale blob from a prior bail; `cloneAsk` propagates the field defensively. **9 new tests** in `__tests__/ask/ask_registry.test.ts`: stores when supplied, omits when not, resume preserves, every terminal transition clears, sweepExpired clears, double-call overwrites, no-payload-after-payload clears, cloneAsk preserves, defensive copy on read.)*
- [x] 5.21-C **`AskApprovalResumer` Pattern A dispatch — resume from paused state OR re-run from question** *(done 2026-04-26 in `packages/brain/src/ask/ask_approval_resumer.ts`. Subscribes to the registry's `approval_resumed` event (5.19) and dispatches between two resume paths. **Pattern A (suspend/resume)**: when the record carries `pausedStateJson` AND the caller wired `resumeFromPausedFn`, deserialise the blob and call `resumeAgenticTurn(pausedState)`. The LLM never knows there was a gap — one continuous transcript, the previously-bailed tool result lands, the run continues. Zero re-LLM cost. **Pattern B (re-run)**: when no paused state OR no resumer wired, fall back to calling `executeFn({id, question, requesterDid})` — the legacy persona-guarded HTTP path. Higher LLM cost but lower state-tracking complexity. **Constructor** validates that at least one of `executeFn` / `resumeFromPausedFn` is supplied (rejects "neither" as composition error). **`applyAgenticResult`** translation table: `completed` → markComplete with `{text: result.answer}`; `approval_required` → markPendingApproval with new approvalId AND new pausedStateJson (re-park for the next bail); `max_iterations` / `max_tool_calls` / `cancelled` / `provider_error` → markFailed with structured `{kind: <reason>, message}`; spec-violation `approval_required` without pausedState → markFailed with `paused_state_missing`. **New event variants**: `paused_state_invalid` (JSON parse failed — fail-closed via markFailed), `no_resumer_configured` (record has paused state but only Pattern B wired AND no fallback). **Re-park loop termination** guaranteed by registry's TTL reaper. **14 new tests** + existing 18 still pass (32 total) in `__tests__/ask/ask_approval_resumer.test.ts`: Pattern A happy path, all 4 failure-finishReasons via `it.each`, paused-state JSON malformed, resumer crash, two-phase Pattern A cycle (re-bail then complete), `no_resumer_configured` paths, Pattern B fallback when paused state present but resumer absent, `paused_state_missing` contract violation. Constructor tests updated to reflect "at-least-one" requirement.)*
- [x] 5.21-D **Vault tool `personaGuard` extension point — fail-closed gate that throws `ApprovalRequiredError`** *(done 2026-04-26 in `packages/brain/src/reasoning/vault_tool.ts`. Adds an optional `personaGuard: (persona) => Promise<string|null>|string|null` to `createVaultSearchTool` (named-persona path only — fan-out across already-accessible personas correctly skips the guard), `createBrowseVaultTool`, `createGetFullContentTool`. `createListPersonasTool` deliberately stays unguarded — returning a name+tier list is intentionally unauthenticated since the LLM needs to know the persona exists in order to ask for approval to read it; locked personas already surface as `{status:'locked'}` with no item count or summaries. **Fail-closed contract** in private `checkPersonaGuard` helper: `null`/`undefined` → allow; non-empty string → throw `ApprovalRequiredError(approvalId, persona)`; empty string → throw a regular `Error` (a guard returning `''` indicates a misconfiguration that couldn't mint an approval id; allowing the read in that state would silently bypass the gate); non-string return → also throw `Error` (defensive against TS-bypassing wiring). **Composition layer remains responsible** for actually wiring a guard backed by `ApprovalManager` + persona-tier lookup; this task only opens the seam — no production caller passes a guard yet (see 5.21-E). **12 new tests** + existing 16 still pass (28 total) in `__tests__/reasoning/vault_tool.test.ts`: throw on string return for each of the 3 tools, allow on null, fan-out skip pin, sync guard return, fail-closed empty-string, fail-closed non-string, guard-crash propagation, ToolRegistry E2E asserting `{success:false, code:'approval_required', approvalId, persona, error}` outcome shape.)*

- [x] 5.21-H **Mobile chat orchestrator bridge** *(done 2026-04-26 across `packages/brain/src/composition/coordinator_ask_handler.ts` (new), `packages/brain/__tests__/composition/coordinator_ask_handler.test.ts` (new, 9 tests), `packages/brain/src/composition/ask_coordinator.ts` (added `subscribe()` fan-out + 5-field `AskCoordinator` interface), and `apps/mobile/src/services/bootstrap.ts` (opt-in wiring via new `askCoordinator` option). Promotes the coordinator into the chat orchestrator's `AskCommandHandler` shape so `/ask` from the mobile chat tab routes through the full Pattern A chain — registry, gateway, resumer, deferred late-answer delivery — without rewriting the orchestrator's synchronous `(query) => Promise<{response, sources}>` contract. **Three pieces**: (1) **`createCoordinatorAskHandler({coordinator, requesterDid, threadId?, formatPendingMessage?, formatResumeHeader?, formatFailureMessage?})`** returns `{handler: AskCommandHandler, dispose: () => void}`. The handler calls `coordinator.handleAsk` and adapts the four outcomes back: `fast_path/complete` → answer text inline; `fast_path/failed` → formatted failure inline (default `/ask failed: <message>`); `fast_path/pending_approval` → placeholder text (default `"I need your approval to read /<persona>. Approve with: /approve <approvalId>"`) + tracks the askId in an in-memory map; `async` (202) → `"Working on it — I'll reply when the answer is ready."` + tracks. **Late delivery** subscribes to the coordinator's event fan-out: on `completed`/`failed`/`expired` for a tracked id, fetches the registry record and posts via `addDinaResponse(threadId, …)` (with optional `formatResumeHeader` prepending a `system` message before the answer). The underlying `AskRegistry.onEvent` is a single constructor callback already bound to the resumer; the coordinator owns a `Set<listener>` and dispatches each registry event to the resumer (always) plus every subscriber (try/catch around each so one bad listener can't poison the chain). (3) **Mobile bootstrap opt-in** — new `askCoordinator?: {coordinator, requesterDid, …formatters}` option on `createNode`. When supplied alongside `globalWiring=true`, takes precedence over the simpler `agenticAsk` path (Pattern A subsumes the tool-loop). The bridge's subscription is released via `dispose()` on node shutdown so re-bootstrap doesn't leak listeners. **9 bridge tests** cover: synchronous fast_path/complete (no late post), submission-crash failure formatting, pending_approval → operator approve → late `addDinaResponse`, optional `formatResumeHeader` prepends a `system` message, operator deny → late failure note, async/202 → "Working on it" placeholder + late delivery once background settles, construction-validation × 2, dispose() unsubscribes (events after dispose don't post). 14 mobile bootstrap tests + 12 composition/ask suites (253 tests) still green. **Inline-approval card UI deferred** — chat-thread approval card + RN tap-to-approve is pure Expo work; the bridge surfaces the approval id + persona heuristic for a richer card when that lands.)*

### 5d. LLM routing

- [x] 5.22 Provider adapters from `packages/brain/src/llm/adapters/`
- [x] 5.23 Provider config (Anthropic, OpenAI, Google, OpenRouter, local llama) *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/provider_config.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `loadProviderConfig({rawJson, env})` + `toLoggable(config)` + `availableProviders(config)` + `toCloudGateEntries(config)` + `ProviderConfigError` + `KNOWN_PROVIDER_NAMES` constant (anthropic / openai / google / openrouter / local-llama). **Split-source design**: JSON at `${configDir}/brain.providers.json` carries non-secret metadata (`{name, kind, models, defaultModel, enabled, baseUrl?}`); env carries secrets (`DINA_<UPPERCASE_NAME>_API_KEY` with hyphens mapped to underscores). Splitting means (a) config files can be committed without leaking keys, (b) key rotation is an env-only change, (c) model-list audits stay scoped to JSON diffs. **Zod-validated schema** (`.strict()` on the entry so typo'd keys are caught at load time) + Zod `enabled.default(true)`. **Per-entry validation** layered on top: duplicate-name, defaultModel-in-models, enabled-cloud-has-key. Each failure throws `ProviderConfigError` with a distinct `code` (invalid_json / invalid_shape / duplicate_provider / default_model_not_in_list / missing_api_key) + `detail` object carrying issue paths + env var name for ops-actionable errors. **Secret redaction via `toLoggable()`**: cloud `apiKey` → `<present>` / `<missing>` tokens; local providers omit the field. Pinned by test that stringifies the logged config and asserts the raw key substring is absent. **Disabled cloud without key is OK** (intentionally disabled) but `enabled + cloud + no key` fails load. Local providers need no key regardless of enabled state. **`availableProviders()`** filter yields what the router should pick from — disabled + cloud-without-key both silently excluded. **19 tests** in `__tests__/provider_config.test.ts`: KNOWN_PROVIDER_NAMES pin, happy path (JSON + env merge + enabled-default + baseUrl + hyphen→underscore env var mapping), 7 error cases with code + detail assertions, toLoggable (redact + missing-for-disabled + local-omits-apiKey), availableProviders 3-way filter, toCloudGateEntries lift.)*
- [x] 5.24 Router model selection per task type *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/model_router.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `ModelRouter` + `TaskType` / `TaskPreference` / `TaskRoutingPolicy` / `RouteSelection` / `RouteRejection` / `RouteResult` types. **Composes 3 primitives**: `ProviderConfig` (5.23) for availability, `CloudGate` (5.25) for persona-tier policy, `TaskRoutingPolicy` for per-task preference lists. **Task types**: `reasoning | summarisation | classification | embedding | chat` — open set, extend by adding to the union + policy. **Policy shape**: `Record<TaskType, TaskPreference[]>` where each preference is `{provider, model?}`. Per-preference `model` override is the critical affordance — lets a policy say "reasoning uses anthropic Opus, classification uses anthropic Haiku" without burying model choice in provider config. Falls back to provider's `defaultModel` when `model` omitted. **Routing algorithm**: walks preferences in order, picks first that (a) is in `availableProviders`, (b) passes the cloud gate for persona tier, (c) has the requested model in its `models` list. First match wins. **Structured rejection with attempt log**: `{reason: 'all_preferences_rejected', attempts: [{provider, reason: 'not_available' | 'not_registered_in_gate' | 'cloud_blocked' | 'model_not_in_provider'}]}` — an operator debugging "why did my reasoning ask end up on local llama?" sees the exact cascade. Separate `no_preferences_for_task` reason for tasks with empty policy entries. **Cache at construction**: `availableProviders` is walked once during `new ModelRouter(...)` and cached in a Map — config is immutable after boot so re-deriving per call is pure waste; the gate's check IS called per-route-call since persona-tier is the variable input. **Returns `{provider, model, kind}`** — not an LLM call itself; the caller invokes the matching provider adapter. Keeps policy testable without HTTP clients. **12 tests** in `__tests__/model_router.test.ts`: construction (3 missing-dep branches), happy path (per-pref model override + defaultModel fallback + sensitive-skips-cloud-to-local + locked-same-as-sensitive), 4 rejection branches (no_preferences + cloud_blocked cascade + not_available for disabled + model_not_in_provider), fallback cascade (first blocked → second picks local), end-to-end integration across all 5 task types.)*
- [x] 5.25 Cloud gate — refuse cloud for sensitive personas *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/cloud_gate.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `CloudGate` + `ProviderEntry` + `GateResult` / `GateRejectionReason` types. **Policy layer between LLM router (5.24) and provider adapters (5.22)**: `check(provider, personaTier)` returns structured `{ok: true, kind}` or `{ok: false, reason, detail?}`. `filterAllowed(preferenceList, tier)` for the router's ranked-preferences path — preserves order, drops unknown providers, strips cloud for blocked tiers. **Policy**: `sensitive` + `locked` tiers block `cloud` providers; `default` + `standard` pass all; `local` providers pass regardless of tier (on-device inference has no outbound-data risk). Pinned by parameterized tests over all 4 tiers × 4 cloud providers. **Centralised, not per-adapter**: new cloud provider added tomorrow inherits the gate by registering; no per-adapter audit for the "forgot to check persona tier" bug class. **Provider classification is data**, not code-branching: `ProviderEntry = {name, kind: 'cloud' | 'local'}` loaded from Brain config; `register(entry)` adds/replaces at runtime and is chainable. **`CLOUD_BLOCKED_TIERS` is a frozen Set inside the module**, intentionally NOT caller-configurable — making this a config field would let a deployment accidentally loosen the security invariant; future "allow cloud for specific sensitive persona" requirement belongs at a different layer (per-persona override). **Uses `PersonaTier` from `@dina/core`** — the 4-tier model from CLAUDE.md §Persona Access Tiers is authoritative. **20 tests** in `__tests__/cloud_gate.test.ts`: construction (4 validation branches), allowed cases (default + standard + all-tiers-local), cloud-blocked (`it.each` 4 cloud providers × sensitive + explicit locked), unknown provider, filterAllowed (sensitive strips cloud + default preserves all + unknown dropped + returns new array), register (add + replace + chainable), list/has/size introspectors (sorted list).)*
- [x] 5.26 Tool-use / function-calling *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/tool_registry.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `ToolRegistry` + `validateArgs` pure validator + `ToolDefinition` / `ToolSchema` / `ToolParamSchema` / `ExecutionResult` types. **In-process tool registry** Brain uses to expose server-side functions (search vault, look up contact, query trust network, send notification) to LLMs. Provider adapters (future 5.22) translate `listDefinitions()` to Anthropic `tools` / OpenAI `functions` / etc; LLM's tool-call response flows back through `execute(name, args, signal?)`. **Minimal JSON-Schema subset**: type `object | string | number | integer | boolean | array`, required array, nested objects, array item schemas, string enum, `additionalProperties` toggle. **`validateArgs`** collects ALL violations into an `errors: string[]` — lets the LLM fix everything in one round-trip instead of N retries. Rejects LLM hallucinations (wrong type, missing required, unknown property with strict schema) BEFORE the handler fires. **Structured execution rejection**: `tool_not_found` (LLM hallucinated a name), `invalid_args` (with detailed errors array), `tool_threw` (implementation bug — detail carries err.message), `aborted` (signal was set before/during). Distinguishable reasons let the LLM loop retry with corrected args vs surface to user vs skip. **AbortSignal plumbing**: every handler receives a signal (synthesized if caller didn't supply one). Pre-aborted signal returns aborted without invoking handler. Handler-throws-after-abort returns `aborted` not `tool_threw` — preserves operator intent. **Optional `defaultTimeoutMs`** internal abort — complements 5.21 LLM cancel registry. **`listDefinitions()` returns defensive schema copies** sorted alphabetically for deterministic provider-adapter wire frames. **31 tests** in `__tests__/tool_registry.test.ts`: register + chainable + duplicate-throws + 4 validation branches via `it.each`, replace (prior-existed bool), unregister (true/false), listDefinitions (strips handler + sorts + defensive copy), execute happy path (ok + result + signal passed to handler), 6 execute rejection paths (not_found, invalid_args for missing required, invalid_args for type mismatch, tool_threw, pre-aborted, during-exec aborted), defaultTimeoutMs (aborts slow + passes fast); `validateArgs` pure (match + all-errors + string enum + nested objects + array items + 6 primitive types via `it.each` + additionalProperties strict vs lenient + rejects non-object).)*
- [x] 5.27 Streaming where LLM supports *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/stream_buffer.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `StreamBuffer` + `StreamState` / `ToolCallState` / `StreamBufferSnapshot` / `StreamEvent` types. **Transport-agnostic assembler**: provider adapters feed `pushTextDelta(chunk)` / `startToolUse(id)` / `pushToolUseDelta(id, chunk)` / `endToolUse(id)` / `markComplete(meta?)` / `markFailed(reason)` / `markAborted()`; consumers read via `snapshot()` or `onEvent`. **State machine**: `streaming → complete | failed | aborted` terminal; every other transition throws. **Post-terminal deltas dropped with `late_delta` events** for ops visibility — buggy providers that keep emitting after `stop` are common enough that throwing would be user-hostile. **Tool-use handling**: partial JSON buffered per tool_call id; `endToolUse` parses. **Parse failure transitions the TOOL CALL (not the whole stream) to `failed`** so text continues flowing — pinned by test. Non-object JSON (`[1,2,3]`) also fails — tool_use must be an object per LLM convention. **Graceful markComplete with in-progress tool calls**: flips each in-progress call to `failed` with `"stream closed while tool_use still in_progress"` — provider bug surfaces as `tool_use_end{ok:false}` so the ask handler records the partial state without failing the whole stream. **Performance**: text chunks stored as array + joined on read, avoiding N² string concat for long streams. **Internal tool-call state** (`in_progress | complete | failed`) distinct from stream-level state — a bad tool call can't poison the stream. **24 tests** in `__tests__/stream_buffer.test.ts`: text deltas (accumulation + events + non-string rejection + empty-delta keepalive), state transitions (all 3 terminal paths + 4 forbidden via `it.each` + empty-reason rejection), late deltas (text + tool_use), tool_use (happy path + malformed fails call not stream + non-object JSON + duplicate-start + push-without-start + end-already-ended + empty-id + markComplete-flips-pending-to-failed + multiple interleaved calls), snapshot (all fields + isTerminal + conditional error/meta rendering).)*
- [x] 5.28 Token accounting + limits *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/token_ledger.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `TokenLedger` + `TokenLimit` / `ConsumeInput` / `ConsumeResult` / `RemainingByScope` / `TokenLedgerEvent` types. **Three limit scopes**: `persona` (total tokens per persona), `provider` (total per provider), `persona_provider` (intersection, most specific). **Daily** (reset at UTC midnight) or **monthly** (reset 1st of month). Period boundary computed from `nowMsFn` + period id (`YYYY-MM-DD` / `YYYY-MM`) so a clock tick past midnight naturally starts a fresh bucket — no reset timer needed. Pinned by tests advancing the clock past both boundaries. **Atomic `consume()`**: walks every applicable limit pre-flight; if ANY would overflow, NO counter is incremented and rejection carries `{reason, limit, consumed, attempted}`. Pinned by a test that consumes to exactly the limit, triggers rejection, then a smaller consume succeeds (proving the rejected request didn't mutate state). **Consume for persona with NO matching limit** returns `{ok: true, remaining: {}}` — empty remaining tells caller "no budget tracking" without forcing a separate has-limit probe. **`preview()`** reports usage + remaining WITHOUT mutating — router uses this pre-LLM-call to skip provider latency on requests that will be rejected post-facto. **Events** `consumed | rejected | period_reset` for admin UI + cost observability. **Construction validation** rejects negative/NaN maxTotal, invalid period, scope-without-required-fields. **Consume input validation** rejects empty persona/provider/model + negative/NaN token counts. **`snapshot()`** returns defensive copies of `TokenUsage` so admin UI can't corrupt internal buckets. **Initial TS issue**: `preview()` return type used `ConsumeResult['remaining']` which can't index a discriminated union — extracted `RemainingByScope` as standalone type. **27 tests** in `__tests__/token_ledger.test.ts`: construction validation (`it.each` 5 branches), single-persona-limit (accept + reject with full error shape + atomicity invariant + no-matching-limit empty-remaining), multi-scope (all applicable updated on success + any-scope rejects), period boundary (daily + monthly reset), preview (no mutation + zero for unseen persona), consume input validation (`it.each` 6 branches), events (consumed + rejected fire), reset + snapshot (clear + defensive copy).)*

### 5e. Agent orchestration subsystem parity audit

- [x] 5.30 Guardian

- [x] 5.33 Command dispatcher *(done 2026-04-22 in `src/brain/command_dispatcher.ts` within core-server — will relocate to brain-server when that app is scaffolded in task 5.1. Exports `CommandDispatcher` + `CommandDefinition` / `CommandCaller` / `DispatchResult` / `DispatchRejection` / `CommandDispatchEvent` types. **Surface**: `register/unregister/has/size/list(roleFilter?)/suggest(query)/dispatch({name, argv, caller, signal?})`. Each command: `{name, description, parse, execute, role?}`. **Distinct from `ToolRegistry` (5.26)**: tools are LLM-facing (JSON-schema params); commands are user-facing (human-typed argv → parse function). **Parse function** returns `{ok, args} | {ok: false, error}` so CLIs render usage without a catch block. **Admin-role gating**: each command optional `role: 'user' | 'admin'` (default user). `dispatch` rejects admin-only from user callers with `forbidden`; admin can invoke user-level commands too (asymmetric by design). Central check means every admin handler doesn't re-check. **Rejection taxonomy** (never throws): `bad_name_shape | unknown_command | parse_failed | forbidden | threw | aborted`. Caller pattern-matches on reason. **Unknown-command suggestions** via Levenshtein distance (threshold ≤3, top-3 matches) — `/ech` → `/echo`, `/env`. Suggestions populated only when non-empty (conditional spread for exactOptionalPropertyTypes compliance). Fires `suggested` event for telemetry. **Handler return vs throw**: `{ok: false, error}` is "handler reported failure" (logs clean); `throw` is "handler had a bug" (wrapped into `threw`). Both land in the same `threw` reason — distinction is internal. **32 tests** in `__tests__/command_dispatcher.test.ts`: register (store + duplicate + chainable + 6 validation branches via `it.each`), dispatch happy path (parse + execute + AbortSignal + event stream), 8 rejection branches (unknown with suggestions + bad_name_shape + parse_failed with detail + forbidden user→admin + admin→user ok + admin→admin ok + handler-returns-ok-false → threw + handler-throws → threw + pre-aborted signal), unregister (true/false + post-unregister unknown), list (sort + role filter user+admin), suggest (distance match + empty-on-far + empty-query + caps-at-3 + event).)*

### 5j. Mobile notification surfaces (~3-4 days)

Wires the three-surface notification model end-to-end on the Expo app:
**(1) inline cards** in the chat thread — extends the 5.21-H-i ask-approval bubble pattern to nudges, briefings, reminders, and service-approvals; **(2) mobile push** — replaces the `src/notifications/local.ts` in-memory stub with `expo-notifications`, channel-aware (Tier-1 fiduciary heads-up / Tier-2 solicited default / Tier-3 engagement bundled per `tierToChannel`); **(3) unified Notifications screen** — new tab that fans in reminders + approvals + nudges + briefings into one chronological inbox with tap-through routing back to the originating chat thread / approval card / reminder detail. Each surface answers a different question: chat = "what's happening in this thread", push = "do I need to open the phone right now", screen = "what did I miss". Same data flowing through three views — no new sources of truth, just three subscribers on the existing stores (reminder service, ApprovalManager singleton, nudge dispatcher, briefing history).

- [x] 5.59 **`expo-notifications` install + permissions + channels** *(done 2026-04-26 across `apps/mobile/package.json`, `apps/mobile/app.json`, `apps/mobile/__mocks__/expo-notifications.ts` (new), `apps/mobile/jest.config.js`, `apps/mobile/src/notifications/local.ts`. Installed `expo-notifications@~55.0.20` (compatible with the existing Expo SDK 55). Plugin registered in `app.json` with `color: '#3b82f6'` + `defaultChannel: 'solicited'`. Three Android channels created on boot via `ensureChannels()` with the Silence-First mapping: `fiduciary` IMPORTANCE_HIGH + sound + heads-up + PUBLIC visibility, `solicited` IMPORTANCE_DEFAULT (notification shade), `engagement` IMPORTANCE_LOW + `showBadge: false` (briefing-only, no per-item badge). iOS has no channel concept — the function short-circuits on non-Android. Permission flow: `requestPushPermission()` checks the persisted answer in `kv_store` (namespace `notifications`, key `permission_status`) first; only prompts the OS when undetermined. Persisted values: `'granted'` / `'denied'` / `'undetermined'`. iOS `requestPermissionsAsync` uses `allowProvisional: true` so the first-launch modal doesn't interrupt onboarding. `forceRequestPushPermission()` re-prompts unconditionally — wired to a future settings-screen "Push permissions…" action. **Jest mock**: `__mocks__/expo-notifications.ts` implements every surface used by `local.ts` plus test helpers (`__setPermissionResult`, `__fireNotificationResponse`, `__setLastNotificationResponse`, `__getScheduled`, `__resetNotificationsMock`). Trigger seconds clamped to ≥1 (zero / past triggers fire immediately, mirroring OS semantics). `cancelNotification(id)` → `Notifications.cancelScheduledNotificationAsync(id)` + mirror delete. `cancelAllNotifications()` wipes both surfaces but **preserves the persisted permission status** so the user doesn't get re-prompted. **Mirror**: kv_store-backed (namespace `notifications`), `notifications:<id>` → JSON-serialised `MirrorEntry`. **No SQLite migration** — kv_store already exists, comfortably handles the few-dozen pending schedules per device, inherits SQLCipher encryption transparently. `getScheduled()` for tests reads the mirror (sorted by triggerAt ASC). - [x] 5.61 **Cold-start reschedule loop** *(done 2026-04-26 in `apps/mobile/src/notifications/local.ts` + wired in `apps/mobile/app/_layout.tsx`. `rescheduleAllReminders(now=Date.now())` walks every kv_store mirror entry, drops past-due ones (the OS would have fired them or missed during downtime), re-issues future-dated entries via `scheduleNotificationAsync` with the same identifier (iOS replaces; Android coalesces). **Defensive against malformed entries**: `parseMirror` returns null on bad JSON / missing fields, and the cold-start loop deletes the bad entry rather than crashing. Returns the count rescheduled. - [x] 5.66 **Unified notifications inbox store + persistent log** *(done 2026-04-26 across `packages/brain/src/notifications/inbox.ts` (new), `packages/brain/src/notifications/bridges.ts` (new), `packages/core/src/notifications/repository.ts` (new), `packages/core/src/approval/manager.ts` (added `subscribeRequests`), `apps/mobile/src/hooks/useReminderFireWatcher.ts` (mirror to inbox), `apps/mobile/src/hooks/useChatNudges.ts` (mirror to inbox), `apps/mobile/src/services/boot_capabilities.ts` (installs approval bridge at boot). **Inbox store**: in-memory `items` array (sorted-insert by `firedAt` DESC for O(1) reads) + Set of subscribers + dual-write through optional `NotificationLogRepository`. - [x] 5.68 **Push tap → in-app deep link** *(done 2026-04-26 across `apps/mobile/src/notifications/deep_link.ts` (new pure handler) + `apps/mobile/app/_layout.tsx` (listener wiring). **Pure handler** `handleNotificationTap(data, deps)` returns `{marked, navigated}` so unit tests can assert without spinning up the router or React Testing Library. Reads `data.inboxId` (string, non-empty) → calls `deps.markRead(id)`; reads `data.deepLink` (string, non-empty) → calls `deps.routerPush(path)`. Defensive: silently ignores `null` / `undefined` / non-string fields / empty strings — bad payloads can't crash the listener. **Layout wiring**: post-unlock effect installs `Notifications.addNotificationResponseReceivedListener` (foreground / background path) AND immediately calls `Notifications.getLastNotificationResponseAsync()` (cold-start path — app was killed, OS has the pending tap response). Both feed the same handler with the same deps `{routerPush: router.push, markRead: markNotificationRead}`. Disposer removes the listener on unmount. **Inbox bridges already populate the right `data` shape** — the approval/reminder/nudge bridges in 5.66 use `id` + `deepLink` consistently; the OS notification's `data: { inboxId, deepLink }` is set by callers when they `scheduleNotification(..., data: {...})`. **Handler tests** (7 in `deep_link.test.ts`) pin: both fields → mark + navigate; only inboxId → mark only; only deepLink → navigate only; null / undefined / empty data → no-op; non-string fields → no-op; empty-string deepLink → no-op.)*
- [x] 5.69 **DND policy + tab badge counts** *(done 2026-04-26 across `packages/brain/src/notifications/dnd.ts` (new), `apps/mobile/src/hooks/useNotificationsBadge.ts` (new), `apps/mobile/app/_layout.tsx` (wires `tabBarBadge` on Reminders + Approvals tabs). **DND module**: state singleton `{ muteEngagement: boolean (default true), quietHoursStart: 'HH:MM' (default '22:00'), quietHoursEnd: 'HH:MM' (default '07:00') }`. `getDND()` / `setDND(partial)` (validates `'HH:MM'` format, throws on bad input) / `resetDND()`. **`shouldDeliverNotification(tier, now?)` — the central decision point**: Tier 1 always returns true (the fiduciary 5.49 invariant — pinned by an explicit "strictest settings" test), Tier 2 honours quiet hours only, Tier 3 honours muteEngagement OR quiet hours. Quiet-hours math handles three cases — empty window (`start === end`), in-day window (`start < end`), wraps-midnight window (`start > end`). Internal helpers `parseHHMM` / `isValidHHMM` / `isInQuietHours` exposed for test pinning. **Badge formatter**: pure `formatBadgeCount(n)` returns `undefined` for 0/non-finite (hides badge), `"1"`–`"9"` for 1–9, `"9+"` for 10+. Floors fractional inputs defensively. `useUnreadCount(kind?)` subscribes to inbox events, recomputes on `appended` + `marked_read`, returns the live integer. `useUnreadBadge(kind?)` wraps it through the formatter for direct `tabBarBadge` consumption. **Layout wiring**: `app/_layout.tsx` calls `useUnreadBadge('reminder')` + `useUnreadBadge('approval')`, passes both into `Tabs.Screen({tabBarBadge})`. Approvals tab still respects the `href: null` provider-blocker gate from review #16 — badge only renders when the tab is reachable. **Tests (24 new)**: 19 in `brain/__tests__/notifications/dnd.test.ts` (Tier 1 invariant under strictest settings; Tier 2 quiet-hours matrix at 4 boundary times; Tier 3 dual-gate matrix; `setDND` partial-merge + invalid-format rejection; `isInQuietHours` for in-day, wraps-midnight, empty-window cases; `parseHHMM` boundaries; `resetDND` returns to defaults); 5 in `mobile/__tests__/hooks/useNotificationsBadge.test.ts` (formatter cap behaviour). Hook subscription itself is covered transitively via the inbox tests in 5.66. **Not yet wired** (deferred to 5.59 / 5.60 / 5.67): the settings-screen toggle UI for `setDND` and the actual Notifications tab badge — both need 5.67 to land first. The DND policy is read by 5.60's scheduler when push lands. **Suite totals**: brain 3088 (+19 DND), mobile 838 (+5 badge formatter), core 3986 unchanged.)*
- [x] 5.70 **Tests** *(done 2026-04-26 — five layers covered, ~95 new tests across the section). **Layer 1 — bridge unit** (8 in `brain/__tests__/notifications/bridges.test.ts`): approval bridge maps `requestApproval` → inbox row with right shape (id, kind, title from action, body from reason / preview fallback, deepLink); disposer detaches; idempotent upsert never duplicates; briefing bridge handles `recorded` events with + without headline, ignores `purged` / `evicted` / no-entry events. Reminder bridge tested via `mobile/__tests__/hooks/useReminderFireWatcher.test.ts` (inbox-mirror assertion on the post-fire path). Nudge bridge tested via `mobile/__tests__/hooks/useChatNudges.test.ts` (mirror on Tier-1/2 delivered nudges; suppressed Tier-3 nudges do NOT mirror). **Layer 2 — persistent log** (10 in `core/__tests__/notifications/repository.test.ts`): InMemory repo round-trip preserves every field; newest-first ordering regardless of insert order; limit clamping; idempotent upsert on id; markRead first-ack semantics + no-op on re-ack; purgeBefore drops past-cutoff items; explicit `expiresAt` overrides retention; reset wipes everything; returned objects are clones. Hydrate-on-restart pinned in inbox tests (layer 3). **Layer 3 — inbox store** (25 in `brain/__tests__/notifications/inbox.test.ts`): every append/list/markRead/getUnreadCount/subscribe semantic, persistence dual-write through optional repo (including `repo failures swallowed`), `hydrateNotifications` cold-start replay + force-vs-no-force idempotency, auto-purge on retention boundary, expiresAt precedence. **Layer 4 — screen render**: filter logic pulled into `applyNotificationFilter` and unit-tested in `mobile/__tests__/notifications/screen_filter.test.ts` (5 tests; all/unread/reminder/approval — including `ask_approval` rolling up under `approval`, input-order preservation). The full screen render is React Testing Library territory and not covered (RTL not installed); the helper test pins the only meaningful logic in the screen. **Layer 5 — deep link** (7 in `mobile/__tests__/notifications/deep_link.test.ts`): both fields → mark + navigate; only inboxId → mark only; only deepLink → navigate only; null/undefined/empty data → no-op; non-string fields → no-op; empty-string deepLink → no-op. **Plus**: 19 in `mobile/__tests__/notifications/local.test.ts` (scheduler API + cold-start reschedule + permission flow + tier-to-channel); 19 DND-policy tests in `brain/__tests__/notifications/dnd.test.ts`; 5 badge-formatter tests in `mobile/__tests__/hooks/useNotificationsBadge.test.ts`. **Mock infrastructure**: `expo-notifications` mocked at module level (`__mocks__/expo-notifications.ts`) — `__setPermissionResult`, `__fireNotificationResponse`, `__setLastNotificationResponse` for test injection; `__getScheduled` for assertion; `__resetNotificationsMock` in `beforeEach`. **Suite totals after 5j**: brain 3088 (1 unrelated live-Gemini flake), mobile 856 / 866 (10 skipped), core 3986 unchanged.)*

### 8g — Cross-stack compat matrix (M3 bonus)

- [x] 8.60 Lite Core + Python Brain — works? *(done 2026-04-22; **Partial — 20/42 (~48%) today, 22 endpoints blocked pending per-milestone unlocks**. Audit captured in `docs/lite-impedance-mismatches.md` §"8.60 Lite Core + Python Brain — audit" with a per-endpoint unlock-milestone table. Regression-gated by `packages/core/__tests__/cross_stack_compat.test.ts` which recomputes the matrix on every run. Static analysis scope — the test walks `packages/core/src/**` + `apps/home-node-lite/core-server/src/**` for Lite routes, `brain/src/adapter/core_http.py` + `brain/src/port/core_client.py` for Python Brain calls, normalises param-form differences (`:id` ↔ `{id}` ↔ trailing slash), and asserts three invariants: (1) no stale entries in `KNOWN_860_GAPS` — every listed gap is a *real* Lite Core miss (catches regressions when Lite Core closes a gap but the list isn't trimmed), (2) every Python Brain call is either on Lite Core or listed — catches new unknown gaps from Brain's side, (3) overlap ratio ≥45% floor. **Wire format is protocol-pinned** (canonical signing + sealed-box + D2D envelope via `@dina/protocol`'s 9 conformance vectors) so auth-layer compatibility is ALREADY guaranteed — only the endpoint surface + body shapes remain as gap surface. 12 tests pass. The published ~48% figure is the static floor; full runtime smoke remains M3-bonus per the task-8g positioning (docker-compose bringing up mixed containers is the natural next step).)*
- [x] 8.61 Go Core + Lite Brain — works? *(done 2026-04-22; **Near-complete — 12/13 (~92%) endpoints work, 1 gap**. Lite Brain's outbound surface enumerated from `packages/brain/src/**` (with template-literal paths like `` `/v1/staging/claim?limit=${limit}` `` correctly captured — the regex fix surfaced during validation when the initial scanner under-counted 7 vs actual 13). Go Core's inbound surface enumerated from `core/internal/**` + `core/cmd/**` = 77 routes. Only `/v1/scratchpad` is Lite-Brain-exclusive with no Go Core equivalent; resolution path is to migrate scratchpad to Brain-internal state (matching Python Brain's in-process convention) rather than add the endpoint to Go Core — scratchpad is *Brain private state* conceptually. Regression-gated by the same `cross_stack_compat.test.ts` with symmetric three-way assertions + ≥85% ratio floor. Audit captured in `docs/lite-impedance-mismatches.md` §"8.61 Go Core + Lite Brain — audit" with a per-endpoint coverage table. Wire format protocol-pinned — auth compatibility guaranteed without runtime test. Scratchpad rewiring deferred to a future Phase 5.x task; until then the matrix correctly reports 12/13 (~92%) as the static floor.)*

### 10d. Publish

- [ ] 10.18 `@dina/protocol` to npm (public v0.1.0 or beta tag first) *(**publish prep landed 2026-04-22** — checkbox stays open until the maintainer runs `npm publish` with loaded credentials (user action, analogous to 0.22 / 1.14.12). Prep deliverables: (1) `packages/protocol/tsconfig.build.json` — publish-appropriate CJS build overrides (`module: commonjs`, `declaration: true`, `composite: false`, `sourceMap: false`, excludes `**/*.test.ts` + `conformance/**` + `__tests__/**` + `docs/**`); (2) `packages/protocol/package.json` grew 4 fields — `build` script (`rm -rf dist && tsc --project tsconfig.build.json`), `prepublishOnly` (`npm run build && npm test` — catches un-built or test-failing publishes at the npm-CLI hook), `files` whitelist (`["dist/", "README.md", "docs/"]` — tests + conformance runner + src stay local to the repo), `publishConfig` (overrides `main`/`types`/`exports` to `dist/` at publish time while in-repo pointers still resolve `src/index.ts` so workspace `ts-jest`/`tsc` consume TypeScript source directly); (3) `packages/protocol/__tests__/publish_ready.test.ts` — 10-test regression gate pinning all 4 invariants + dist-smoke that `require()`s the built CJS output (2 smoke tests skip cleanly when `dist/` isn't populated, so a fresh clone without `npm run build` still passes); (4) `packages/protocol/jest.config.js` excludes `/dist/` from `transformIgnorePatterns` so the gate can load built artefacts without ts-jest warning about processing `.js` files. Build verified: `npm run build` emits `dist/index.js` (37 exports verified via CJS `require`), `dist/index.d.ts` with preserved doc-comments, `dist/{types,constants,validators,canonical_sign,envelope_builder}.{js,d.ts}`. **To publish**: flip `private: false` in `packages/protocol/package.json`, run `npm publish --access public` from `packages/protocol/`. Package stays `"private": true` in-repo so accidental CI/workspace publishes reject cleanly.)*
- [x] 10.19 npm badge in README *(done 2026-04-22; added 5 shields.io badges to `packages/protocol/README.md` top: **npm version** (`img.shields.io/npm/v/@dina/protocol.svg`, linked to `npmjs.com/package/@dina/protocol`), **npm monthly downloads** (`img.shields.io/npm/dm/@dina/protocol.svg`), **License: MIT** (static), **Zero runtime deps** (static — points at the `dep_hygiene.test.ts` gate that enforces the invariant), **Conformance vectors: 9** (static — points at `conformance/vectors/`). The two npm badges render as "invalid" until 10.18 publishes, then auto-activate within ~1h as shields.io caches refresh — no code change needed at publish time. **Regression-gated** by 2 new assertions in `publish_ready.test.ts` that confirm the npm-version and npm-downloads badge URLs are present + scoped to `@dina/protocol` + link to the canonical npmjs.com package page (so a reader clicking the badge lands on the right registry entry, not a 404). Protocol suite: 175 → 177 tests (+2). Also shipped `packages/protocol/docs/release-checklist.md` — a step-by-step maintainer playbook that walks 10.18 through actual publish + 10.19 badge-activation verification (6 steps: pre-flight, clean-room build, version pick (beta vs public), unlock+publish with `npm pkg set private=false` / `npm publish --tag beta --access public`, post-publish smoke via a fresh `npm install @dina/protocol` in a tempdir, badge-activation visual check, checkbox flip). Checklist also documents npm's append-only nature + rollback strategy (unpublish within 72h vs deprecate+patch-bump vs protocol-break major-bump per `conformance.md` §14). Rationale: `npm publish`'s irreversibility + the number of moving parts (publishConfig, files whitelist, private-flag flip, dist-tag choice) make a pre-written playbook more reliable than recall at publish time.)*

## Phase 13 — Pre-prod soak (~1 week after M4 or M5)

- [x] 13.1 Deploy alongside test-infra
- [ ] 13.2 30-day personal-use soak
- [x] 13.3 Feature flag in `install.sh` for stack selection
- [x] 13.4 Post-soak report
- [x] 13.5 Decision gate: keep both stacks or schedule Go/Python retirement

## Mobile migration — **handled in Phase 1 under option (c)**

With option (c) chosen, mobile lands in Phase 1 (tasks 1.14.1–1.14.13), not as a future cross-cutting effort. The ongoing invariant remains:

- **Zero changes to pure packages driven by mobile-only needs.** Every platform-specific tweak goes in `*-expo` adapters. If a pure package has to change, that's a layering bug — fix in pure, not via platform branches.
- Mobile app must remain runnable on main at every Phase-8 milestone; Lite work does not block mobile releases.

## Out of scope

- Retiring Go Core / Python Brain — both run until Lite passes M5 + soak
- Public `@dina/*` npm publishing beyond `@dina/protocol`
- TLS termination (Caddy/nginx in front)
- Kubernetes manifests (compose only)

## Open questions

1. ~~Phase 0.5 option — resolved, (c)~~
2. **SQLCipher Node lib choice** — blocks Phase 3a. Resolve at 3.1.
3. **Admin UI form factor** — HTMX vs SPA vs descope
4. **Local LLM (`node-llama-cpp`)** — descope from v0.1?
5. **Metrics endpoint** — what does Go expose; match or descope
6. **Cross-stack compat** — Lite Core + Python Brain as supported config?
7. **Error message string parity** — how aggressive? (Tracked per-test in M5)
8. **dina-mobile freeze-date** — when do we cut the move? Aligns with Phase 1 kickoff

## What changed from v3 → v4

- Added decisions **#11** (Go/Python as correctness oracle) and **#12** (API semantic parity, not byte parity)
- Revised decision **#3** from "full parity day one" to "staged M1-M5 parity"
- Reframed goal paragraph — dina-mobile is donor code, not authoritative server architecture
- Added **Phase 0.5 — Divergence plan**, decided **option (c) — move dina-mobile first**
- Added **milestone map** section up front
- Added **"server-grade operational concerns"** sub-phases in 4l and 5i — long-running workflow crash recovery, MsgBox idempotency windows, admin API audit, metrics parity, trace correlation, background-loop supervision
- Replaced **"byte-for-byte"** language with **"semantic parity"** throughout Phase 4; split error-message string parity into per-test M5 tracking
- **Restructured Phase 8** — 57 flat tasks → 5 milestone buckets (8a-8e), each with its own gate, tag, and demo-able ship point
- Phase 9 (E2E + user stories) aligned each scenario to a milestone
- **Phase 1 expanded under option (c)** — dina-mobile's full contents (packages, app, Expo adapters) land in `dina/` before any Lite server work. Previously deferred as "Cross-cutting: mobile migration"; now in-scope from day one. Phase 1 grows from 3-4 days → 5-7 days.
- Effort estimate now reports milestone-cumulative calendar time — Lite v0.1.0 in **5-6 weeks** (including the upfront mobile move), M5 in **11-13 weeks**
